# Races

## Aestari
*Scions of Clarity, Children of the Threshold • The Many Faces of Power*

*“Perfection is not a state. It is a discipline that never forgives neglect.”*

The Aestari are elegant, refined, and ever-adaptable beings who embody control in its most polished forms. Their beauty is undeniable, but it carries a deliberate edge, as if every gesture, word, and glance has been shaped for effect. Descended from the luminous powers of Everbright, they now walk the Mortal Plane as creatures of discipline and influence, too perfect to seem entirely natural and too composed to be easily trusted. Some command attention like living icons, while others pass like whispers through marble halls, leaving behind only the consequences of their presence.

#### Origin
___
The true origin of the Aestari is obscured by contradiction, omission, and careful silence. Most scholars believe they descend from the Luminari of Everbright, beings of light and perfect definition who crossed the Threshold into mortal reality in an age no surviving record describes clearly. Whether they came as exiles, envoys, fugitives, or conquerors remains disputed, and the Aestari themselves rarely answer directly. Exposure to the Verdant Cradle, the Dreamscape, and the flawed conditions of mortal existence reshaped them across generations. Their radiance softened into flesh, their certainty fractured into ambition, and their perfection became something that had to be maintained.

#### Appearance
___
Aestari appear as humanoids of unnerving refinement, with features that seem sculpted rather than grown. Their skin ranges from porcelain, pearl, rose ivory, and cloud-blue to deep onyx, muted violet, or seafoam pale, often marked by faint gradients near the temples, throat, horn base, or collarbones. Each Aestari bears a single asymmetrical horn, a living mineral structure that may curl like a crescent, spiral around the temple, arc like a broken crown, or trail backward in elegant twists. Their hair is long, full, and carefully arranged around the horn rather than hidden by it, often braided with fine metals, ritual threads, or house colors. Their eyes are layered and strange, sometimes showing multiple irises that align like an aperture under moonlight, magic, or emotion. They move with precise economy, rarely fidgeting, stumbling, or wasting motion.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Aestari culture is built around refinement, hierarchy, and the relentless correction of imperfection. They believe that power should rarely be displayed crudely, since true authority arranges the world until obedience appears natural. Their society is divided among noble houses, arcane circles, patronage courts, scholastic orders, and discreet syndicates, each devoted to a different interpretation of mastery. Emotion is cultivated rather than denied, expressed through timing, posture, language, and restraint. Beneath this elegance lies a quiet fear that mortal reality is eroding them, introducing flaws they can mask but never fully remove. To an Aestari, to falter publicly is more than embarrassment. It is the beginning of irrelevance.

#### Societal Roles
___
Aestari are most often found where influence is concentrated: royal courts, mage academies, treaty chambers, temple estates, hidden councils, merchant houses, and fortified libraries. They serve as diplomats, arbiters, patrons, spymasters, scholars of binding law, architects of etiquette, and keepers of dangerous inheritance. Some become silent agents who erase obstacles before conflict reaches the surface, while others are elevated as living icons whose role is to embody the legitimacy of a house, doctrine, or realm. Their society measures status through function, consistency, and placement. An Aestari who serves poorly is not always punished openly. More often, they are simply removed from the pattern.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Aestari names are chosen with great care, shaped for elegance, lineage, and social effect. Traditional names are flowing and melodic, such as Caelithar, Orisyn, Veythiel, Lysara, Xalendir, Sylthorin, Naevara, Aeloria, Vaelisar, and Thalorien. In mixed courts or cosmopolitan realms, some adopt shorter court-names such as Adrien, Lucien, Sylas, Cassian, Evander, Dorian, Celeste, Seraphine, Selene, Vivienne, Isadora, or Elise. House names are often older, more ornate, and bound to ancestral prestige, such as Val’Kaeron, Orthelias, Vel’Thalor, Ael’Veyr, Caelthorne, Lysandral, Vor’Tyrian, and Elaris. Formal presentation often includes both personal name and house allegiance, as in Lucien Voss of House Vel’Thalor or Seraphine Caelthorne of House Orthelias.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, the Aestari occupy the upper strata of influence, dwelling in spires, sealed estates, high academies, embassy courts, and districts where architecture itself seems designed to keep the uninvited at a distance. Their power is rarely expressed through open rule. Instead, it moves through contracts, patronage, arcane law, marriage alliances, debt, education, and carefully placed silence. When an Aestari descends into common streets, guild markets, or dangerous quarters, it is almost never casual. They arrive to observe, negotiate, claim, correct, or remove something that has begun to disturb the order they prefer.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Aestari means embracing control, poise, and layered intent. You may be graceful, ambitious, secretive, idealistic, ruthless, or burdened by the impossible standards of your house, but you rarely act without considering how the moment will echo later. Think about what kind of perfection your character pursues, what flaw they hide, and what kind of disorder they fear most. Aestari suit wizards, rogues, bards, warlocks, artificers, nobles, courtiers, spies, and strategists. Your strength is not simply beauty or intelligence. It is the ability to shape the conditions of a scene before others realize the scene has begun.

#### Aestari Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Aestari reach adulthood around 100 years of age and can live for more than 700 years. Their long lives are shaped by discipline, memory, and the slow burden of accumulated experience.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Umbravision
Your eyes, reflecting the dim glow of the city’s skyline, grant you Umbravision up to 60 feet. You perceive the world in shades of gray, but in the right light, your eyes gleam with an unnatural radiance.

**Poise in Motion.** You gain proficiency in Persuasion or Stealth (your choice).

**Trance.** You do not sleep. Instead, you meditate for 4 hours while remaining aware.

**Unshaken Composure.** You have advantage on saving throws against being frightened or charmed.

**Signature Presence.** Once per long rest, you can reroll a failed Charisma check.

**Languages.**

## Arochi
*Those Who Feed the Wind*

*“We do not chase fate. We cultivate it.”*

The Arochi are highland farmers, grainwrights, and sky-merchants descended from the same ancestral stock as the Pykari, though their path led toward settlement rather than wandering. They are a people of floating fields, elevated river-plains, granaries, mills, and airship routes, known across Orimond for feeding cities that barely understand the labor behind their survival. Practical, patient, and quietly ambitious, the Arochi believe civilization is sustained by those who plan beyond the next hunger. Their power is rarely loud, but every market, army, temple, and throne learns quickly that whoever controls the harvest controls tomorrow.

#### Origin
___
The Arochi trace their ancestry to early Pykari groups who chose to settle where wind, fertile silt, and planar stabilization created highland fields and airborne trade corridors. Over generations, they adapted to cultivation, logistics, sunlight, and mechanical refinement, trading the volatile omens of the old wandering life for endurance, foresight, and stewardship. Their bond to the Ashenspire softened, replaced by a practical intimacy with weather, soil alchemy, grain cycles, and the craft of making abundance reliable. What began as survival through settlement became a culture whose harvests now shape the stability of entire regions.

#### Appearance
___
Arochi are Medium humanoids with lean, durable builds shaped by farming, travel, and sustained physical labor. Their skin commonly ranges from soft teal, pale jade, and muted blue-green to sun-warmed undertones marked by faint mottling from wind, sun, and altitude. Their features are fine but sturdy, with gentle cheekbones, narrow jaws, slightly elongated ears, and bright amber or golden eyes that suggest constant practical attention. Hair is thick, wind-tousled, and often copper-brown, auburn, deep umber, or honey-brown, worn loose, tied back, or braided into functional cords. Their hands are calloused but precise, equally suited to seedwork, tool repair, rope handling, and delicate tradecraft.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Arochi culture is built around sustenance, fairness, and continuity. They take pride in feeding others, but they do not confuse service with submission. Agriculture, automation, fermentation, milling, and trade are treated as linked disciplines, each requiring patience, precision, and honest measure. Machines are respected when they lessen burden, extend reach, or protect workers, but final refinement remains a matter of hand, judgment, and tradition. An Arochi’s reputation depends on reliability: fair weights, clean grain, sound vessels, kept contracts, and harvests delivered even when weather, politics, or war make delivery difficult.

#### Societal Roles
___
Arochi commonly serve as agricultural engineers, grain refiners, millwrights, fermentation masters, airship navigators, cargo captains, trade coordinators, wind-field architects, irrigation planners, and neutral suppliers in tense regions. Some become merchant-princes or guild factors, while others remain field stewards whose decisions determine whether a district eats through winter. Their expertise in automation and logistics makes them indispensable to cities, armies, monasteries, and remote settlements alike. Though often underestimated as merely practical folk, Arochi influence runs through supply chains, food stores, trade pacts, and the quiet arithmetic of scarcity.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Arochi names are clear, grounded, and often inspired by grain, wind, rivers, fields, and useful craft. Given names tend to be straightforward but melodic, such as Reiko, Haren, Tavren, Oryas, Malkai, Venji, Sahra, Elen, Yune, Rylka, Marei, and Tessen. Family names may reference lineage, crops, routes, or professions, such as Ryshar, Goldmere, Velkan, Orenthe, Sunchaff, Windgrain, Ironseed, Tideharvest, Dawnmiller, Skybarley, or Longsilo. Some Arochi captains and harvest masters earn route-names or mill-names after a great delivery, a saved harvest, or a trade pact that endured hardship.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Arochi settlements gather around elevated farmlands, dock-fields, granaries, mills, fermentation halls, and airship moorings. Their districts are orderly, industrious, and welcoming in a restrained way, designed around storage, movement, repair, and food preparation rather than monuments. They are trusted across political lines because their work is indispensable, though this trust is never naïve. Arochi know that food invites dependency, envy, and coercion, so their granaries are guarded, their contracts carefully worded, and their routes planned with contingencies. They rarely dominate public life, but their absence is felt immediately.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Arochi means leaning into competence, planning, and quiet leverage. You may be a trader, engineer, cultivator, navigator, brewer, ration-master, scout, or envoy, but you likely think in terms of supply, consequence, and long-term stability. Consider what your character is responsible for sustaining: a family field, a trade route, a guild machine, a seed-line, or a community that depends on your judgment. Arochi characters suit artificers, rangers, rogues, bards, wizards, druids, and practical fighters who prefer preparation over spectacle. Your strength lies in making sure tomorrow arrives fed, repaired, and still moving.

#### Arochi Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Arochi reach adulthood in their late teens and commonly live between 90 and 120 years. Their communities measure maturity through responsibility as much as age, with adulthood recognized when an Arochi can sustain a household, a trade route, a craft, or a field.

**Size.** Small

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Harvest Endurance.** You have advantage on saving throws against exhaustion.

**Windwise Traders.** Gain proficiency in Insight or Persuasion.

**Practical Ingenuity.** Gain proficiency with one set of artisan's tools of your choice.

**Steady Hands.** Once per long rest, you can reroll a failed Dexterity ability check.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Brannholt
*Sun-Bearers, Heatbound Delvani • Short, geological, and functional. “Brannholt” implies dryness, exposure, and endurance without sounding elemental or mystical.*

The Brannholt are heatbound Delvani, shaped by sun, salt, exposed stone, and hard distances rather than tunnel-pressure and deep earth. Where their subterranean kin learned to endure weight from above, the Brannholt learned to endure the open world without flinching. They live in deserts, savannas, salt coasts, and tropical faultlands where walls crack, wells fail, and survival depends on shade, rhythm, labor, and trust. A Brannholt does not waste strength proving endurance. They conserve it until endurance is required.

#### Origin
___
The Brannholt emerged when Delvani communities spread beyond the Lithic corridors into lands of relentless heat and exposure. Generations beneath open sky changed them, shifting their mineral circulation away from pressure retention and toward thermal dissipation. Their pigmentation deepened as surface minerals bound into their skin, protecting them from radiant stress, while their veins adapted to bleed heat slowly back into the air. They are not diminished Delvani, nor softened surface cousins. They are what Delvani endurance becomes when stone must survive the sun.

#### Appearance
___
Brannholt have dark stone-toned complexions, ranging from deep basalt brown and obsidian umber to bronze-black, rust-brown, and volcanic red undertones. Their mineral veins sit close to the surface but glow dimly, dispersing heat rather than storing it. These veins may appear as red-brown iron tracery, matte basalt seams, honeyed quartz flecks, or pale salt-crystal fracture lines. Their skin is smoother than that of many tunnel Delvani, worn by wind, salt, and sand instead of chisel, pressure, and stone-dust. Crystalline freckles gather along brow ridges, shoulders, spine, and other places where sun and heat strike hardest. Their eyes catch light sharply, giving them a watchful, mirage-bright stare.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Brannholt culture is built around exposure management, communal water, and the discipline of shared survival. Shade is treated with reverence, water with obligation, and time is often measured by heat cycles rather than bells or clocks. They value preparation over force, patience over stubbornness, and route knowledge over fortification, since a wall means little when the land itself erodes it. Their humor is dry, quick, and often delivered in the middle of work. Their deepest fears are dehydration, abandonment, and isolation under open sky, because to be left alone in the heat is not merely misfortune. It is a sentence.

#### Societal Roles
___
Brannholt commonly serve as desert engineers, sun-resistant architects, caravan anchors, load-distribution specialists, saltworks overseers, mineral harvesters, wind-tower builders, heat-management artisans, oasis wardens, and route-stabilizers. They are prized wherever roads cross hostile terrain or settlements must endure brutal climates. In mixed societies, they often handle surface infrastructure, cooling systems, long-haul logistics, and emergency planning. Their strength is rarely dramatic. It shows in the road that remains passable, the cistern that does not fail, the shelter that holds through noon, and the caravan that arrives with all its members alive.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Brannholt names often favor monikers tied to heat, travel, endurance, weather, or scars of exposure. Personal names and earned names include Sunscar, Shadecount, Redline, Drift, Emberwake, Saltstep, Longhaul, Glasswind, Dryhand, and Noonmark. Surnames or route-names usually reference regions, resources, passages, or survival obligations rather than fixed structures, such as Dustway, Brightrock, Saltbinder, Heatline, Sunfall, Dryreach, Ashroad, Cisternwatch, and Redmesa. A Brannholt may earn a new name after guiding others through a deadly crossing, preserving water under impossible conditions, or surviving exposure that should have claimed them.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Brannholt Delvani are sought after for surface works, heat regulation, road planning, exposed foundations, salt handling, and long-distance transport. They are often found in caravan yards, sun-baked outer districts, dry docks, foundry approaches, public cisterns, and infrastructure crews responsible for keeping trade moving through difficult terrain. Outsiders sometimes mistake their measured pace for laziness or their dry humor for indifference. Both assumptions are dangerous. A Brannholt moves when movement matters, speaks when words are needed, and spends no effort simply to reassure the impatient.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Brannholt means leaning into patience, endurance, and practical judgment under environmental pressure. You are built for long roads, hard weather, scarce water, and moments when the group needs someone who can stay calm while others overheat, panic, or rush. Consider what route, oasis, caravan, or obligation shaped you, and what you refuse to abandon under the sun. Brannholt characters suit fighters, rangers, wardens, clerics, paladins, druids, and any build centered on resilience, logistics, protection, and survival. Your strength is the quiet kind: the kind that keeps others alive until the heat finally breaks.

#### Brannholt Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Brannholt reach adulthood in their late twenties and can live up to 120 years. Their communities measure maturity through endurance, route knowledge, and the ability to safeguard others through heat, scarcity, and exposure.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** You do not have Darkvision, as humanity’s origins are tied to the daylight, not the dark.

**Stonebound Endurance.** Once per long rest, when you fail a Strength, Dexterity, or Constitution saving throw, you can reroll it and take the higher result.

**Burden of Oaths.** You have advantage on Insight checks to detect lies. If someone swears an oath to you, you always know if they break it.

**Foundation of Industry.** You gain proficiency in Athletics or Investigation.

**Thermal Adaptation.** You have resistance to fire damage and ignore penalties from extreme heat and arid environments.

**Solar Dissipation.** When you take fire damage, you can use your reaction to reduce the damage by an amount equal to your proficiency bonus + Constitution modifier. Once used, this trait cannot be used again until you complete a long rest.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Brasselan
*The Weight-Bearers • We bend so the storm passes.*

*The cold is not our enemy. It is our shelter.*

Brasselan are a cold-adapted, horned humanoid people whose mass, posture, and physiology are shaped by endurance, thermal inertia, and resistance to environmental extremes.

#### Origin
___
An autochthonous high-latitude species evolved under persistent cold, wind, and scarcity.

#### Appearance
___
Large hunched bodies, compressed necks, thick leathery skin in slate, peat, or frost-ash tones, and heavy ram-like horns that curve backward along the skull and shoulders.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Brasselan culture emphasizes containment, continuity, and survival through stillness. Strength is measured in endurance rather than aggression.

#### Societal Roles
___
Commonly serve as builders, wardens, stonekeepers, deep miners, and defenders of cold or hostile regions.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are short, clipped, and practical, often one syllable. Lineage names reference locations, storms, or structural features.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Brasselan settle in cold districts, subterranean vaults, wind-exposed zones, and thermally stable structures.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Ideal for players who enjoy stoic presence, physical resilience, and slow deliberate decision-making.

#### Brasselan Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Strength score increases by 1.

**Age.** Brasselan reach adulthood around 40 years of age and commonly live between 180 and 250 years. Their communities measure maturity by endurance, restraint, and the ability to preserve others through cold, scarcity, and crisis.

**Size.** Large

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft

**Thermal Inertia.** You have advantage on saving throws against exhaustion caused by cold or environmental exposure.

**Horned Balance.** You have advantage on Strength checks to resist being pushed, knocked prone, or forcibly moved.

**Cold Dampening.** Fire damage you take is reduced by your proficiency bonus.

**Contained Presence.** Creatures within 5 feet of you have disadvantage on checks to intimidate you.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Broodlings
*Unfallen Spawn, Children of the Womb • Beauty Before the Lesson*

*“They were born gentle. Then the sisters taught them meaning.”*

Broodlings are newly birthed offshoots of Wretchmothers, uncanny in their inhuman beauty and startling innocence. They emerge without cruelty, without purpose, and without the practiced malice of the brood. Corruption comes later, shaped deliberately by Broodsisters through ritual, imitation, and enforced awakening.

#### Origin
___
A Wretchmother’s brood cycle produces many failures, but Broodlings are the rare early forms that arrive whole. They are cast into the lair’s outer chambers to wander, listen, and learn. When Broodsisters find them, they begin the work of shaping them into true brood.

#### Appearance
___
Broodlings are small, symmetrical, and almost luminous in the wrong light. Their features are refined but subtly inhuman, with eyes too reflective and movements too deliberate. At birth they show minimal iron, sutures, or bone growth, but those marks appear as corruption takes hold.

#### Culture & Identity
___
At first they have no culture, only receptivity. They mimic tone, posture, and emotion with unsettling precision, as if practicing personhood. Broodsisters fracture that calm by teaching pain, hierarchy, and devotion, turning innocence into obedience and hunger.

#### Societal Roles
___
Unclaimed Broodlings serve as observers, attendants, and living lures within brood territory. Once claimed, they become pupils and tools, assigned to harvesting, scouting, and enforcement. Older Broodlings are often kept close to Broodsisters as proof of their craft.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Unclaimed Broodlings have no names and respond to cadence, touch, and proximity. Broodsisters grant names as vows, often drawn from wounds, virtues inverted, or the first lie the Broodling learns to speak.

#### Life in Orimond
___
They linger near Wretchmother sites, drifting through corrupted halls, ruined forges, and flesh-warped thresholds. A Broodling that escapes indoctrination rarely stays whole, either regressing into feral instinct or clinging to fragile borrowed ethics until it finds shelter.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Broodlings fit horror-leaning stories about imposed identity and transformation. Play the tension between genuine gentleness and the constant pull of the brood’s calling. The arc often turns on who teaches you first, and what you choose to remember.

#### Broodlings Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Charisma score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Broodlings mature quickly, reaching a stable adolescent form within months. Those who pursue the Mother’s Calling through dreams and rites may metamorphose into Broodsisters within a few years, though the process varies by lair and tutor.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Unfallen Presence.** You have proficiency in Insight or Performance (your choice), reflecting your uncanny ability to read and mirror emotion.

**Receptive Mind.** You have advantage on saving throws against being frightened. If you fail a saving throw against being charmed, you may choose to fail instead.

**Inhuman Beauty.** You have advantage on Charisma (Persuasion) checks made to calm a creature that can see you and is not hostile.

**Broodsister Imprint.** When you finish a long rest within a Broodsister’s influence, you gain one Corruption Mark (DM tracked). At 3 Marks, you also gain proficiency in Intimidation, and your demeanor changes.

**Adaptive Flesh.** When you take acid, cold, fire, lightning, or necrotic damage, you can use your reaction to gain resistance to that damage type until the start of your next turn. You can use this reaction a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus per long rest.

**Metamorphic Calling.** If you pursue the Mother’s Calling through dreams and rites, you may replace this species with Broodsister at a major milestone, keeping ability score increases and proficiencies (DM approval).

**Languages.** 
You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Cindralis
*Ash-Smiths, The Unfinished • The Faultless Artisans of the Unfinished World*

*Perfection is for the dead. Refinement is for the living.*

The Cindralis are meticulous artisans, jewelers, metallurgists, and precision-forgers descended from the Delvani, though generations of furnace-light, fine machinery, and relentless refinement have shaped them into something narrower and stranger. Where many Delvani endure through mass, pressure, and bodily strength, the Cindralis endure through exactness. Their hands build what cities depend on: locks, lenses, blades, reliquaries, clockworks, instruments, and delicate engines whose smallest flaw could ruin a kingdom’s design. They do not believe in finished work. A thing is only abandoned, improved, or waiting to be corrected.

#### Origin
___
he Cindralis arose in Cinderhold, a forge-city of patient heat, soot-dark workshops, jewel halls, engraving vaults, and layered manufactories built atop older Delvani industry. Over generations, craft changed them more deeply than war ever could. Their bodies became compact and stooped, their strength settling into hands, fingers, eyes, and memory rather than shoulders and backs. Industrial vapors, mineral dust, forge rites, and selective guild traditions left their marks in skin, bone, and temperament. They are not weaker Delvani in their own understanding. They are Delvani pressure refined into precision.

#### Appearance
___
Cindralis are compact, stout humanoids, usually standing between 4’8” and 5’8”, with bodies that appear durable at first glance but tire quickly under heavy exertion. Their skin is coarse and mineral-textured, resembling cast metal, unpolished stone, or worked ore in tones of burnished bronze, tarnished silver, weathered pewter, brass-gold, or oxidized copper green. Subtle bony ridges and nodules often form along the brow, jaw, wrists, and knuckles, sometimes growing into delicate patterned protrusions associated with skill and age. Their limbs are narrow, but their hands are long-fingered, steady, and unnaturally precise. Their eyes are deep-set and monochrome, appearing as pools of smoky quartz, dull platinum, brushed nickel, or molten bronze, fixed on the world as though every surface contains a flaw waiting to be found.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Cindralis culture is governed by the doctrine of endless refinement. Perfection is considered a dangerous illusion, because a perfect work invites stillness, arrogance, and death of craft. A worthy creation remains open to correction, and a worthy artisan learns to hear mistakes as instructions. Guilds, workshops, lineages, and master-apprentice chains define much of their society, with rivalries that may last generations over a hinge design, alloy recipe, gem cut, or disputed engraving method. Status comes from precision, not wealth alone. Scarred hands, burned sleeves, ink-dark fingers, and annotated failures are treated as marks of devotion.

#### Societal Roles
___
Cindralis most commonly serve as jewelers, smiths, engravers, clockwrights, machinists, instrument makers, assay masters, mint wardens, lock designers, relic restorers, and inspectors of structural or mechanical flaws. Their work supports armies, temples, noble houses, merchant guilds, and arcane laboratories, though they often remain less celebrated than the rulers and warriors who depend on their craft. In times of war, they forge mechanisms, siege components, precision weapons, and protective fittings. In peace, they maintain the hidden systems that keep halls lit, gates sealed, vaults protected, and fine tools working exactly as intended.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Cindralis names tend to be clipped, textured, and workshop-practical, often shaped by guild speech, forge cant, or the rhythm of tools striking small surfaces. Given names include Brannic, Velt, Odrin, Kess, Tarnik, Solla, Mirek, Dathra, Orven, Pell, Vessa, and Korrin. Surnames and earned names frequently reference craft, material, flaw, or method, such as Finecut, Brasshand, Truegauge, Emberfile, Nickelwright, Gemsetter, Faultseer, Stillgrip, Deepstamp, or Halfmeasure. A Cindralis may gain a second name after completing a masterwork, surviving a disastrous commission, or discovering an error in a famous work others believed beyond correction.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Cindralis are found in forge districts, jewel markets, mint houses, clock towers, arcane workshops, locksmith guilds, and manufactories where delicate work matters more than raw output. They are respected for their skill and difficult to work with when rushed, since a Cindralis would rather offend a patron than release flawed work under their name. Their workshops are cluttered but ordered, filled with unfinished pieces, annotated tools, cooling trays, sealed drawers, and half-corrected designs. Outsiders often call them obsessive. The Cindralis usually take this as evidence that outsiders do not understand craft.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Cindralis means leaning into precision, restlessness, and the pursuit of improvement beyond comfort or praise. Your character might be an artisan, artificer, rogue, wizard, investigator, forge-priest, relic restorer, or reluctant adventurer searching for rare materials and impossible techniques. Think about the flaw you cannot stop seeing: in your work, your teacher, your guild, your body, or the world itself. A Cindralis is rarely satisfied, but that dissatisfaction can become devotion, irritation, genius, or cruelty. Your strength lies in noticing what others overlook, then correcting it with hands steady enough to change the future one small adjustment at a time.

#### Cindralis Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Cindralis reach adulthood slowly, typically around 30, and live up to 150 years.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Artisan's Focus.** Gain proficiency with one artisan's tool of your choice (Jeweler's Tools, Smith's Tools, or Clockmaker's Tools). You have advantage on checks involving delicate work, engraving, or precise adjustments.

**Fine-Tuned Dexterity.** Your hands never shake. You can manipulate fragile or intricate mechanisms without risk of fumbling.

**Structural Insight.** Upon close examination, you know the weakest point of a structure or mechanical device. You can identify forgeries, counterfeit gems, or faulty engineering at a glance.

**Adaptive Restlessness.** You need only 4 hours of sleep per day. You have advantage on saving throws against exhaustion from overwork.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Custodian
*The Unraveled Wardens*

**Prison is not a place. It is a sentence that never ends.**

The Custodians are the Unraveled Wardens, hollow beings drawn back from the deep reaches of Nevermourn after their former selves were stripped into silence. They are not born, raised, or fashioned by ordinary hands. They are what remains of those who passed too far into unraveling and returned with a sentence where a life should have been. Bound to forgotten prisons, sealed vaults, cursed thresholds, and chains no mortal record explains, Custodians guard what must remain confined even when they no longer know why. Some obey forever. Others begin to feel the smallest impossible thing and discover that a single emotion can loosen even an eternal chain.

#### Origin
___
Custodians originate in the deepest reaches of Nevermourn, where existence thins, identity loosens, and names lose the strength to hold a soul together. Those who wander too far into that realm may become undone, their memories, desires, and histories dissolving into the dark architecture of absence. A few return, reshaped by the unraveling into wardens of prisons older than their new bodies. They remember almost nothing of who they were, only the certainty that they had once been someone before purpose replaced identity. Whether the Custodians were chosen, punished, salvaged, or repurposed remains unknown, even to their own Curators.

#### Appearance
___
Custodians are gaunt, hollowed humanoids, usually standing between 5’10” and 6’8”, with bodies that appear ashen, mummified, stretched thin, or half-eroded by absence. Their features slowly smooth over time, leaving faces that seem less sculpted than worn away. Brand-like sigils, chain marks, or sealing glyphs may appear across their skin, glowing faintly in blue, red, gold, or corpse-white light when their purpose stirs. Their eyes are sunken and ember-dim, often fixed in a stare that feels less emotional than judicial. Shadows around them behave strangely, lagging behind, stretching toward prisoners, recoiling from broken oaths, or coiling like chains at their feet.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Custodian culture is built around duty without explanation. They honor seals whose contents they may never know, maintain prisons whose builders are forgotten, and recite oaths that outlived the languages that first shaped them. Their hierarchy is austere and severe: Wardens guard, Curators record, Deacons enforce, and Overseers appear only when the order of confinement has failed. Emotion is treated as corruption, or worse, as the first sign of falling. Yet some Custodians awaken to a fragment of feeling: curiosity, pity, anger, longing, fear, or warmth. Among their own kind, such awakening is rarely condemned aloud. It is simply treated as a disappearance waiting to happen.

#### Societal Roles
___
Custodians most often serve as prison wardens, oath-keepers, curse-watchers, seal guardians, execution witnesses, tomb sentinels, and enforcers of ancient bindings. They appear where something has been locked away too long to be safely remembered, or where an oath has acquired enough weight to become a chain. Some are attached to courts, temples, forbidden archives, and sealed ruins, though their allegiance is usually to the sentence itself rather than to any ruler. Fallen or wandering Custodians may become grim protectors, bounty hunters, exorcists, judges, or reluctant companions, still carrying the instinct to confine what threatens to break loose.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Custodians rarely keep names from their former lives, since those names were usually lost in the unraveling. Most bear titles, designations, or duty-names tied to their station, prison, chain, or remembered fragment. Common names include Warden Ash, Silent Key, Barrow-Seal, Oathmark, Chain-of-Thirds, Hollow Vigil, Deacon Veyr, Curator Nhal, Lockbearer, and Gate-Sable. A Custodian who begins to feel may choose a personal name for the first time, often something simple and fragile, such as Mara, Sol, Venn, Cael, Eren, or Lume. To choose such a name is dangerous, because a name implies a self beyond the sentence.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Custodians are rare and deeply unsettling, appearing near sealed districts, condemned fortresses, ancient cells, oath courts, execution grounds, and ruins whose doors no one remembers building. Some institutions seek them out as perfect jailers or witnesses, assuming their absence of emotion makes them incorruptible. Others fear them as omens that something nearby is imprisoned, guilty, cursed, or waiting to escape. A Custodian who wanders beyond their assigned place is watched carefully by occult orders and avoided by common folk. Their presence suggests that a forgotten sentence has entered the street and begun asking what freedom means.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Custodian means exploring duty, absence, judgment, and the dangerous arrival of feeling. Decide what emotion first awakened in you, what prison or oath you once guarded, and whether you abandoned that duty, were released from it, or were sent into the world to pursue a breach. You may be grim, calm, merciless, protective, confused, or quietly fascinated by mortal life. Custodians suit paladins, clerics, warlocks, fighters, monks, rangers, and any character built around endurance, restraint, curses, oaths, or forbidden knowledge. Your central tension is simple and severe: are you a person with a purpose, or a purpose wearing the remains of a person?

#### Custodian Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Custodians do not age in the mortal sense—instead, as time passes, their features slowly smooth, their expressions fading, their physical form becoming less defined. Some have existed for centuries, while others barely remember their first steps.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Your unraveling form grants you Darkvision up to 60 feet.

**Warden’s Presence.** When you are within 10 feet of a restrained, cursed, or imprisoned creature, you can sense their crimes as whispered voices in your mind. The voices fade when you leave.

**Unraveled Endurance.** You do not require food, water, or sleep. Instead, you must enter a still, meditative state for 4 hours, where your form stabilizes against further unraveling.

**Unraveled Endurance.** You do not require food, water, or sleep. Instead, you must enter a still, meditative state for 4 hours, where your form stabilizes against further unraveling.

**Gaze of Judgment.** Once per long rest, you can fix your gaze upon a creature. They must make a Wisdom saving throw (DC = 8 + your Proficiency Bonus + your Wisdom modifier) or become frightened for 1 minute. If they have broken an oath or betrayed someone, they roll with disadvantage.

**Chains of the Forgotten.** As an action, you can summon spectral chains to restrain a creature within 10 feet for 1 minute. The target must succeed on a Strength or Dexterity saving throw to escape. Once used, this ability recharges on a long rest.

**A Whisper of Feeling.** You start with one emotion, something small, something insignificant—but something you have never had before. This emotion may grow, change, or pull you toward a greater destiny—or it may fade, leaving only absence.

**Languages.**

## Delvani
*Bearers of Weight, Hearth of Stone • The Weight of the World, The Heart of the Hearth*

*“If the world’s going to break your back, might as well lean into it together.”*

The Delvani are the bearers of weight, descendants of the Stone Delvers of the Lithic Bastion and living heirs to pressure, fracture, and endurance. Where roads hold, tunnels breathe, bridges remain standing, and fortresses refuse collapse, Delvani hands are rarely far from the foundation. They are kin to the sun-hardened Brannholt, but where their sister species learned to survive exposure, salt, and open sky, the Delvani remained shaped by depth, load, hearth, and stone. They do not glorify suffering, but they do glorify surviving it together. Their laughter is loud, their hospitality stubborn, and their loyalty heavier than any wall they raise.

#### Origin
___
The Delvani trace their inheritance to the Stone Delvers, pre-flesh tectonic beings native to the Lithic Bastion, where identity once formed through pressure, crystallization, and resonance rather than blood. When the old lattices weakened and mortal conditions reshaped what crossed into the world, some Delver remnants condensed into flesh-bound forms capable of sensation, labor, hunger, kinship, and grief. Mineral cores became organs, lithic resonance became circulation, and endurance learned to speak around a hearth. Later, some Delvani lineages spread into deserts, salt coasts, and sun-blasted lands, eventually becoming the Brannholt, while the Delvani proper remained the people of stonework, tunnels, weight, and communal shelter.

#### Appearance
___
 Delvani bodies are dense, grounded, and geologic, built like load-bearing structures rather than ornamented statues. They often have squared torsos, broad shoulders, thick necks, large hands, long forearms, and bowed lower legs shaped by uneven ground and heavy work. Their matte, stone-like skin ranges from clay-gray and slate-brown to deep granite, warm sandstone, and iron-dark mineral tones. Beneath it run visible veins of copper, gold, ruby, lapis, obsidian, quartz, or other mineral expressions, glowing faintly in darkness and brightening with labor, pride, laughter, or shared purpose. Unlike the Brannholt, whose veins sit nearer the surface to vent heat, Delvani mineral lines run deeper, storing pressure, memory, and strength. Crystalline freckles often gather across knuckles, elbows, shoulders, and brow ridges where density presses close to the skin.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Delvani culture is built on communal endurance. They believe pressure is inevitable, but isolation is a failure of care. A burden carried alone becomes punishment; a burden carried together becomes structure. Hospitality is sacred, and a seat at the hearth is both welcome and obligation. Their humor is loud, physical, affectionate, and rich in mineral insults, while grief and joy are worn openly rather than hidden behind ceremony. Delvani fear Stillness above almost all things, understanding it as endurance stripped of motion, warmth, and purpose. Their Brannholt kin teach that survival depends on shade and water; Delvani teach that survival begins when someone makes room beside the fire.

#### Societal Roles
___
Delvani most commonly serve as masons, tunnelers, bridge-wrights, forge engineers, pressure-artisans, fortification planners, siege logisticians, caravan load-masters, route stabilizers, oath-keepers, guild leaders, and labor organizers. They are rarely the rulers of a city, but they are often the reason a city keeps standing after its rulers fail. In peace, they build and maintain what others take for granted. In war, they reinforce walls, move impossible loads, hold defensive lines, and remember which structures will survive a siege. When Delvani turn to crime or rebellion, they often strike systems rather than individuals: collapsed supply routes, sabotaged foundations, broken machinery, and gates that no longer open for tyrants.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Delvani names are often practical, communal, and mutable. Many use monikers earned within work crews, hearths, or guilds, such as Sparkshift, Bricks, Deepway, Patch, Axle, Rust, Tread, Overload, Hearth, Stonejaw, or Loadsong. Surnames tend to be occupational or communal, tied to labor, structure, or remembered crews, such as Holloway, Breakiron, Rebar, Kiln, Bridger, Hearthson, Grinder, Overlock, Deepbrace, or Underwall. Names may change after a major project, disaster, oath, injury, betrayal, or act of communal service. Among Delvani, changing names is healthy. It means the stone has taken a new shape without breaking.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Delvani are indispensable and chronically undervalued. Their enclaves cluster around forges, tunnels, docks, railworks, foundations, cisterns, foundries, and deep infrastructure hubs where the city’s weight can be heard through stone and pipe. Taverns often double as meeting halls, labor exchanges, informal courts, and hearth-houses for travelers with nowhere else to sit. The upper districts may ignore them until something cracks, floods, jams, burns, or collapses, then suddenly every noble, guildmaster, and magistrate remembers who knows how the city actually stands. Without Delvani labor and memory, Orimond would not merely decline. It would physically fail.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Delvani means leaning into endurance, loyalty, work, and emotional directness. You are built to carry weight, but the real question is whose weight you choose to carry and why. Consider the crew, hearth, oath, bridge, tunnel, or failed structure that shaped you. Delvani suit fighters, paladins, clerics, artificers, rangers, wardens, and any character who protects others through resilience, craft, and stubborn presence. You may be warm, blunt, loud, grieving, practical, or quietly heroic, but you likely judge people by what they do when the ceiling starts to fall. A Delvani does not ask whether the burden is fair. They ask who needs help lifting it.

#### Delvani Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Delvani reach adulthood in their late 20s and can live up to 120 years. Elders are revered as structural memory for the community.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** You do not have Darkvision, as humanity’s origins are tied to the daylight, not the dark.

**Stonebound Endurance.** Once per long rest, when you fail a Strength, Dexterity, or Constitution saving throw, you can reroll it and take the higher result.

**Burden of Oaths.** You have advantage on Insight checks to detect lies. If someone swears an oath to you, you always know if they break it.

**Foundation of Industry.** You gain proficiency in Athletics or Investigation.

**Pressurized Form.** You have resistance to force damage and ignore penalties from high-pressure environments.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Dren
*Keepers of the Ember, Ash-Walkers • We do not flee the fire. We learn where to stand.*

*The world ends often. We simply keep walking.*

The Dren are ancient keepers of ember, ash, and survival, a people whose memory reaches back to the high reaches of the Ashen Spiral. They were not cast down, conquered, or driven from their first home. They descended by choice, walking step by step into heavier worlds, harsher ground, and more fragile forms of life. Now gathered most strongly in Dreadmere, the City of Ash and Smoke, they are known for their patience, endurance, and communal warmth. The Dren do not fear fire, ruin, or decay. They have seen worlds burn before, and they know where to stand when the burning begins.

#### Origin
___
The Dren originated near the Ashen Spiral, where heat, entropy, and slow unmaking shape all things. Over generations, they moved downward into the Mortal Plane, settling along volcanic basins, faulted lands, ash valleys, and smoke-choked regions where other peoples struggled to endure. The Spiral marked them without consuming them, leaving its touch in their embered eyes, ash-toned skin, and long lives. Some scholars attribute Dren longevity to lingering Spiral influence, while the Dren themselves offer a simpler answer: survival is a choice renewed every day, and they have chosen it longer than most.

#### Appearance
___
Dren are powerfully built humanoids with broad shoulders, deep chests, dense musculature, and grounded movement shaped by heat, gravity, and labor. Their skin ranges from cooled slate blue and charcoal gray to pale volcanic stone, often crossed by broad ember-striations that resemble heat scars, sediment bands, or dark seams beneath cooled basalt. These markings deepen when a Dren is exerting themselves, experiencing strong emotion, or exposed to intense heat. Their faces are severe and weathered, with strong brows, flattened noses, and tightly set jaws that lend even young Dren an ancient quality. Their eyes glow faintly in ember-orange, coal-red, dull amber, or smoldering gold, steady as coals beneath ash rather than bright as flame.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Dren culture is built around community, continuity, and the belief that no one survives the end of things alone. They are welcoming to strangers, slow to judge, and deeply practical, though their patience should never be mistaken for passivity. Fire is respected rather than worshipped, and ash is understood as proof that something mattered enough to burn. Their stories rarely celebrate conquest. They preserve accounts of migrations, disasters, losses, shelters built in time, and names carried through smoke. To the Dren, isolation is the first death, panic is the second, and forgetting is the third. The hearth remains the center of their identity because it is where warmth becomes shared survival.

#### Societal Roles
___
Dren commonly serve as fireworkers, forge-masters, ashland guides, disaster wardens, structural laborers, hearth-keepers, industrial safety experts, and advisors in volatile regions. In Dreadmere, they maintain shelters, furnace halls, smoke routes, and communal refuges where others would be overcome by heat, toxins, or despair. Beyond their homeland, they are sought by settlements built near volcanoes, unstable forges, cursed ruins, and regions touched by the Ashen Spiral. Some become wandering guides for those drawn toward dangerous places, while others act as calm voices during evacuations, collapses, fires, and other endings that arrive too quickly for most peoples to understand.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Dren names are old, heavy, and functional, often suited to being spoken through smoke, labor, or long travel. Given names tend to be short and grounded, such as Khar, Ennet, Dovren, Mael, Sura, Thren, Vorra, Esh, Kalem, and Daska. Surnames and epithets are often earned rather than inherited, marking survival, work, migration, or communal service. Examples include Ashward, Smoke-Born, Cinderfall, Longwalk, Hearthkeeper, Emberhand, Sootveil, Coalwatch, Last-Shelter, and Firepath. A Dren may receive a new name after guiding others through disaster, preserving a hearth through famine, or surviving a place where no one expected life to remain.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Dren communities form around dangerous regions that others avoid: volcanic slopes, furnace districts, ash-choked valleys, unstable fault zones, deep forges, and old industrial quarters where smoke never fully clears. Their homes are communal, reinforced, and built for function rather than display, with hearth halls serving as kitchens, meeting places, shelters, and memory houses. Dren are respected because they remain when others evacuate, and because they rarely waste words when action is required. In Dreadmere, their presence defines the city’s rhythm. Elsewhere, a Dren hearth is a promise that even in ruin, someone is still keeping watch.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Dren means leaning into endurance, patience, warmth, and long memory. You may be a survivor of disaster, a keeper of communal fire, a guide through ashlands, a forge-worker, a wandering elder, or someone drawn toward the Ashen Spiral’s dangerous call. Dren characters suit clerics, fighters, druids, rangers, paladins, monks, and any role built around resilience, protection, survival, and calm under pressure. Think about what disaster your character remembers, what community they refuse to abandon, and what ember they still carry. A Dren does not rush, does not panic, and does not mistake ruin for the end.

#### Dren Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Dren age slowly. Many live beyond 300 years, remaining physically capable long after other species would falter.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Your embered eyes grant you Darkvision up to 60 feet.

**Ashen Endurance.** You have resistance to fire and necrotic damage.

**Cinder Veil.** Once per long rest, as a bonus action, you turn into smoke until the start of your next turn, becoming intangible and immune to non-magical attacks.

**Smoke-Walker.** You are immune to inhaled toxins, poisonous gases, and smoke.

**Keepers of the Ember.** You have advantage on death saving throws.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Eidolons
*Star-Bound Vessels • What falls from the sky remembers how to stand*

*I am not what I was. I am what remains.*

Eidolons are ancient souls reborn into constructed frames after falling from the sky as shooting stars. They are wisdom made animate housed in borrowed forms.

#### Origin
___
Long before luminaries stone delvers or humanity an ancient people lived in these lands and later ascended to higher realms. Their souls now burn as stars in the Verdant Cradle and the Lithic Bastion and some fall as shooting stars seeking new vessels.

#### Appearance
___
Bodies are improvised frames such as stone blocks minimal humanoid constructs scarecrows statues dolls or any object that can be puppeteered by a stellar soul.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Eidolon culture values patience accumulated insight and restraint shaped by the knowledge that their soul will slowly fray over centuries.

#### Societal Roles
___
Often serve as sentinels historians guides and living monuments to forgotten ages.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are chosen at rebirth and often reference stars seasons materials or abstract concepts rather than lineage.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Eidolons exist at the margins of Orimond inhabiting ruins sanctuaries and liminal sites where starfall is remembered.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Best suited for players exploring ancient perspective constructed bodies and long arcs of purpose tempered by gradual soul-erosion.

#### Eidolons Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Eidolons awaken as adults, carrying memory and wisdom from a previous life. They do not age normally and can endure for 500 years or more. Their end often comes suddenly, when the star-soul animating their vessel finally grows still.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Stellar Vessel.** Your body is a constructed frame animated by a fallen star-soul. You do not need to eat or drink.

**Borrowed Form.** You have advantage on saving throws against poison and you are immune to disease.

**Ancient Wisdom.** You gain proficiency in one skill of your choice.

**Starfall Insight.** Once per long rest you have advantage on one Intelligence or Wisdom check.

**Unaging Frame.** You do not age. Over centuries your soul frays and the DM may introduce narrative symptoms as it approaches its end.

**Languages.** You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Emrelan
*The Warm-Kept • The day is carried, not worshipped.*

*The sun does not burn us. It wakes us.*

Emrelan are a sun-attuned people whose physiology converts light into stored warmth, clarity, and controlled heat. Their fire expression manifests as embers, smolder, and thermal permission rather than flame.

#### Origin
___
An autochthonous humanoid species shaped by long-term solar exposure and adaptation to cyclical light environments.

#### Appearance
___
Dark matte skin that absorbs light, bright fibrous hair in pale copper, bone-white, or ember-gold tones, white opaline eyes, and red-orange thermochromic freckles that flare in heat or focus.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Emrelan culture values restraint, rhythm, and clarity. Emotion is expressed through timing and proximity rather than volume. The sun is treated as a regulating condition, not a god.

#### Societal Roles
___
Commonly found as mediators, solar engineers, healers, cartographers, and custodians of light-dependent infrastructure.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are fluid and often soft, favoring open vowels and liquid consonants. Individuals may change names after major life cycles or relocations.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Emrelan communities in Orimond cluster around high-light districts, exposed terraces, and infrastructure reliant on daylight cycles.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Best suited for players exploring controlled power, subtle magic expression, and identity shaped by environmental rhythm.

#### Emrelan Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Emrelan reach adulthood in their late teens and commonly live between 90 and 130 years. Their communities measure maturity through restraint, timing, and the ability to carry warmth without wasting it.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Normal Vision

**Solar Metabolism.** You recover one additional hit die during a long rest spent in natural or strong artificial light.

**Ember Physiology.** You have resistance to fire damage from environmental sources, not spells.

**Thermal Permission.** Once per long rest you may cause a flammable object you touch to ignite or smolder without producing open flame.

**Freckle Flare.** When you succeed on a concentration check or saving throw against exhaustion, you gain advantage on the next ability check before the end of your next turn.

**Languages.** You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Hollow
*The Unfinished • When meaning dies the body remains*

*Hope is not lost. It is absent.*

Hollow are beings who persist after hope ambition or soul has been erased. They are not undead but exist in a state of existential exclusion.

#### Origin
___
Formed through total loss of ambition soul destruction or extreme anomaly exposure.

#### Appearance
___
Pale dull skin platinum white hair and fully black eyes without sclera.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Hollow cultures are defined by detachment ritualized routine and rejection of aspiration.

#### Societal Roles
___
Often used as labor sentinels or exile wardens where emotional detachment is valued.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are shortened flattened or symbolic often losing personal meaning.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Hollow exist at the margins of Orimond inhabiting anomaly zones ruins and forgotten districts.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Best suited for players exploring restraint emotional distance and subtle control.

#### Hollow Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Hollow do not age and may persist indefinitely unless destroyed. They are not born, raised, or matured in the usual sense, and their apparent age reflects what they were before becoming Hollow.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft

**Empty Physiology.** You do not need to eat or drink but you can if you choose.

**Detached Mind.** You have advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.

**Emptiness Resilience.** You have resistance to necrotic damage.

**Anhedonia.** You cannot gain Inspiration.

**Diminishing Presence.** Once per long rest when a creature you can see within 30 feet makes an attack roll or ability check you can use your reaction to impose disadvantage on that roll.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Humans
*The Unfinished Ones • Adapt or vanish. Then adapt again.*

*We were never meant to last. So we learned how.*

Humans are the unfinished ones of Orimond, fragile, brief-lived, and endlessly adaptable. They are not the strongest, oldest, or most planar-touched people, yet they thrive in places where older powers hesitate and more specialized species fail. Humans change because they must, building lives in the cracks between empires, disasters, divine legacies, and unstable realms. Their greatest inheritance is neither blood nor destiny, but response: the ability to survive a broken world by becoming something new before the breaking is complete.

#### Origin
___
Humans emerged within Orimond itself, without clear planar ancestry, divine blueprint, or single progenitor people. Their origin myths contradict one another wildly, which many scholars consider the most Human answer possible. Some claim they rose from common mortal stock in the wake of early planar fractures. Others believe they are the result of life adapting repeatedly to conditions no other lineage could stabilize. Whatever the truth, Humans were never shaped to embody one realm, element, law, or cosmic principle. They were shaped by circumstance, and circumstance has never stopped changing.

#### Appearance
___
Humans vary more widely than nearly any other people in Orimond. Their bodies may be slight, broad, tall, compact, soft, wiry, powerful, or weathered by labor and climate. Skin tones, hair textures, eye colors, facial structures, and body types differ by region, ancestry, migration, and environment rather than a single defining lineage. Humans scar easily, age visibly, and often wear their histories plainly through posture, dress, marks, tools, and ornament. What distinguishes them is not uniform appearance, but expressive adaptation. A Human body often tells the story of where it has been forced to survive.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Human cultures are numerous, fragmented, and restless. They build kingdoms, guilds, faiths, schools, militias, and trade networks quickly, then revise or abandon them when the world changes around them. Their traditions can be fiercely defended, but rarely remain untouched for long. Humans borrow, blend, reinvent, and improvise with remarkable speed, sometimes to the admiration of other peoples and sometimes to their deep irritation. They tend to value ingenuity, cooperation, personal loyalty, and momentum. Where longer-lived species may think in centuries, Humans often act with the urgency of those who know time is short.

#### Societal Roles
___
Humans occupy almost every role in Orimond because they are rarely confined to one inherited function. They become traders, diplomats, scouts, soldiers, scholars, sailors, inventors, farmers, mercenaries, artists, administrators, priests, rebels, and explorers of unstable frontiers. They may lack the ancestral precision of Aestari, the endurance of Delvani, the deep memory of Luminari, or the specialized adaptations of Naureli, Dren, Korrak, Arochi, and Mistaryn, but Humans excel at connecting disciplines that others keep separate. Their strength lies in improvisation, coalition-building, and making something workable from mismatched pieces.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Human names vary by region, culture, language, class, faith, and personal reinvention. Some use simple given names such as Arlen, Mira, Jonas, Kessa, Rowan, Tarek, Elin, Damos, Sera, or Veyra, while others adopt elaborate naming traditions from neighboring peoples. Family names may be inherited, occupational, geographic, patronymic, devotional, or invented after migration. Humans also change names readily after war, exile, marriage, apprenticeship, criminal reinvention, religious conversion, or a new life in a new city. To many Humans, a name is not a sacred inheritance. It is a tool for becoming.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Humans are found almost everywhere in Orimond: frontier towns, mixed-species cities, unstable borderlands, Veil-adjacent markets, river ports, military colonies, farming settlements, and ruins being turned into homes before anyone agrees they are safe. Their communities rise quickly and adapt constantly, sometimes becoming thriving crossroads and sometimes collapsing within a generation. Humans live easily among other peoples, though not always peacefully, and are often the first to settle where conditions are uncertain. They are used to inheriting worlds that were not designed for them and calling those worlds home anyway.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Human means leaning into adaptability, urgency, and self-definition. You are not bound to a single ancient role, planar inheritance, or inherited function, so your choices carry particular weight. Consider what forced your character to change: a disaster, migration, war, apprenticeship, betrayal, opportunity, or the influence of another species. Humans suit every class and background, especially characters who improvise under pressure, bridge cultures, seize chances, or reinvent themselves after failure. Your greatest strength is the refusal to remain what the world expected you to be.

#### Humans Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Charisma score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Humans reach adulthood in their late teens and rarely live beyond 90 years. Their short lives drive urgency, ambition, and risk-taking uncommon among longer-lived species.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Adaptive Ingenuity.** You gain proficiency in one skill of your choice.

**Versatile Heritage.** Once per long rest, when you fail an ability check, you can reroll the check and take the new result.

**Resilient Spirit.** After finishing a long rest, choose one saving throw. You have advantage on the first save of that type before your next long rest.

**Social Flexibility.** You gain proficiency in Persuasion or Deception (your choice).

**Enduring Will.** When reduced to 0 HP but not killed outright, you remain conscious until the end of your next turn (once per long rest).

**Unpredictable Potential.** At the end of each long rest, choose one ability score. You gain advantage on the first ability check using that score before your next long rest.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Imperatum appear human-adjacent, but never ordinary. Their bodies carry a regal, almost liturgical severity, as if posture, gaze, and breath have been disciplined by an invisible throne. They tend toward long silhouettes, severe profiles, high collars, mantle-like garments, steady hands, and movements so deliberate they feel ceremonial. Even at rest, an Imperatum seems placed rather than merely standing, like a living seal set at the center of a larger mandate.
*Children of the Throne • Direction precedes desire*

*I do not want. I orient.*

The Imperatum are children of the Throne, people born Imperant and aligned to the deep vectors of ambition before ambition becomes desire. They do not experience purpose as a wish, dream, or hunger, but as direction: continuity, expansion, exchange, containment, reform, preservation, ascent, or another dominant orientation that shapes the way they move through the world. To an Imperatum, choice is real, but it is never weightless. Every act either clarifies the path or pulls the body against its own internal compass.

#### Origin
___
The Imperatum are shaped by the Throne of Ambitions, the subconscious scape where intent, pride, and directed will first condensed into orientation. They are usually born in mortal communities, but early life anchors them to an Imperant directive through environment, culture, pressure, inheritance, crisis, or institutional expectation. A child raised among collapsing systems may become aligned to continuity. One born in trade, diplomacy, or scarcity may orient toward exchange. One raised amid borders and danger may embody containment. The directive is never merely learned. It settles into the body as a pattern of thought, stress, instinct, and clarity.

#### Appearance
___
mperatum appear human-adjacent, often indistinguishable from ordinary mortals at first glance, but their presence gives them away. Their posture is composed, their gaze steady, and their expressions often seem organized around a point of focus only they can see. Subtle signs of internal orientation may surface during stress: a stilling of the hands, a tightening of the jaw, a faint brightness behind the eyes, or a shift in stance as though their body has found its axis. They are rarely flamboyant unless their directive demands visibility. Most look less supernatural than deeply, unnervingly directed.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Imperatum culture centers on the recognition of shared orientation rather than blood, belief, or emotion. Two Imperatum may disagree violently on methods yet understand one another if their directives move along the same vector. They do not usually gather around faith or ideology in the common sense. Instead, they build schools, offices, orders, households, councils, and quiet networks where alignment can be tested, refined, and put to use. To live against one’s directive for too long is considered dangerous, producing physical stress, irritability, dissociation, illness, or reckless correction. Their greatest fear is contradiction without resolution.

#### Societal Roles
___
Imperatum are commonly found as stewards, administrators, strategists, institutional anchors, reformers, treasurers, logisticians, magistrates, advisors, and long-term planners. In times of transition, instability, succession, famine, or reform, they become invaluable because they can hold direction while others are overwhelmed by emotion, faction, or short-term desire. They are often trusted by structured systems and distrusted by populist movements, revolutionaries, and free companies that sense the weight of institutional gravity around them. An Imperatum may save a city by preserving its continuity, or doom it by preserving what should have been allowed to end.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Imperatum names often reference roles, abstract functions, virtues of direction, or offices held rather than lineage alone. Given names may be simple and formal, such as Cael, Oran, Veyra, Senn, Ilyra, Damos, Thale, Corin, Maera, or Voss. Surnames and bynames often reflect orientation or institutional identity, such as Continuance, Northward, Ledgerhand, Gatewise, Stillmantle, Truecourse, Axis-Bound, Exchange-Kept, Reform-Seal, or Holder-of-the-Line. Some Imperatum adopt a directive-title after adulthood, especially once their alignment stabilizes. Such a title is treated as both identity and public warning.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Imperatum are embedded wherever continuity must be maintained through pressure: civic offices, merchant houses, courts, temples, guild archives, military councils, reform assemblies, succession boards, and crisis committees. They are rarely the most beloved figures in a room, but they are often the ones people turn to when panic makes ordinary leadership unreliable. Their ability to sense unresolved imbalance makes them effective mediators, auditors, planners, and stabilizers, though it can also make them intrusive or inflexible. In a city of competing species, broken systems, and planar strain, Imperatum often become the quiet hinge on which larger events turn.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Ideal for players who enjoy purpose driven characters tension between duty and personal bonds.

#### Imperatum appear human-adjacent, but never ordinary. Their bodies carry a regal, almost liturgical severity, as if posture, gaze, and breath have been disciplined by an invisible throne. They tend toward long silhouettes, severe profiles, high collars, mantle-like garments, steady hands, and movements so deliberate they feel ceremonial. Even at rest, an Imperatum seems placed rather than merely standing, like a living seal set at the center of a larger mandate. Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Intelligence score increases by 1.

**Age.** Imperatum reach adulthood in their late teens and commonly live between 80 and 120 years. Their communities measure maturity by the stabilization of a personal directive and the ability to act with consistency under pressure.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Normal Vision

**Imperant Alignment.** You are born Imperant aligned to a dominant directive shaped by your environment such as continuity expansion exchange or containment.

**Somatic Orientation.** Acting in alignment with your directive grants calm clarity while prolonged misalignment manifests as physical stress.

**Directive Sense.** You instinctively recognize unresolved imbalances related to your directive in your surroundings.

**Institutional Gravity.** You are naturally relied upon in structured systems but often distrusted in populist or revolutionary movements.

**Noncontradiction.** Directly acting against your directive causes discomfort and disadvantage on the first related roll at the DM’s discretion.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice
You may choose up to 0.0 exotic language instead

## Ithilari
*The Radiant Aspects of the Veil • We do not wear color; we become it.*

*The light does not wane. It is only hidden.*

The Ithilari are exalted kin of the Aestari whose bodies are infused with stabilized celestial light. Upon maturity their form settles into a single radiant aspect that defines presence ability and fate.

#### Origin
___
Descended from the highest Aestari bloodlines shaped by royal lineage divine decree or celestial intervention.

#### Appearance
___
Tall humanoids with ethereal skin locked into a permanent luminous hue glowing star-like eyes and subtle chromatic radiance tied to their chosen aspect.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Ithilari culture is defined by expectation privilege and burden. They are revered symbols of celestial order yet struggle with identity beyond lineage.

#### Societal Roles
___
Serve as rulers prophets celestial arbiters corporate mystics and living anchors to Veil-aligned power.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are formal melodic and lineage-bound often referencing light celestial states or historical aspects.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond Ithilari are rare tightly monitored and often embedded within high-security institutions cult hierarchies or Veil-adjacent enclaves.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Best suited for players exploring legacy expectation divine power and tension between autonomy and destiny.

#### Ithilari Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Charisma score increases by 1.

**Age.** Ithilari reach adulthood around 50 years of age and can live for 800 years or more. They are considered mature when their radiant aspect settles into its permanent form, shaping their presence, abilities, and social role.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft

**Celestial Lineage.** Upon maturity you manifest a permanent radiant aspect that shapes your abilities.

**Radiant Physiology.** You have resistance to radiant damage.

**Aspect Expression.** Choose one Ithilari aspect which grants a once per long rest active ability.

**Veil Sensitivity.** You can sense strong Veil or cosmic disturbances within 30 feet.

**Rare Celestial Flux.** Extreme anomaly conditions may temporarily shift your aspect at DM discretion.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

You may choose up to 1.0 exotic language instead

## Kairos
The Kairós are living moments of conviction, born when an idea takes root deeply enough in the collective subconscious to demand a body of its own. They are not a lineage in the ordinary sense, but a people of rhetoric, disruption, and awakened possibility, shaped by the Dreamscape where thought presses against reality. A Kairós enters the world as a challenge made flesh: expressive, charismatic, and difficult to ignore. Wherever they gather, arguments sharpen, old certainties crack, and stagnant institutions begin to feel the pressure of change.

#### Origin
___
Kairós emerge from moments when a new idea becomes more than passing thought. When enough minds turn toward the same possibility, fear, rebellion, or revelation, the Dreamscape may condense that pressure into a living being. Some Kairós are born from revolutions, artistic movements, forbidden philosophies, or sudden social awakenings. Others arise from quieter convictions that spread slowly beneath the surface of culture. Their lives are tied to relevance and resonance rather than bloodline. When the idea that shaped them fades, a Kairós may weaken, transform, or disappear, while those bound to enduring convictions can persist for centuries.

#### Appearance
___
Kairós are expressive humanoids whose bodies seem shaped by persuasion rather than ancestry. Their features are elegant, vivid, and slightly exaggerated, becoming sharper or more radiant when they speak with conviction. Skin may shimmer with emotional hues, from gold confidence and crimson passion to deep blue contemplation or pale silver doubt. Their eyes glow with unusual intensity, shifting in brightness as their thoughts gather force. Hair is often dramatic and fluid, sometimes moving like ink, flame, ribbon, or wind. Their hands, posture, and gestures carry unusual precision, as if the body itself were built to argue, command, reveal, and inspire.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Kairós culture is founded on discourse, dissent, and the belief that no idea deserves safety from examination. They value debate as both art and weapon, treating contradiction, challenge, and public speech as sacred forms of refinement. Authority is tolerated only when it can answer for itself. Tradition is respected only after it survives scrutiny. A Kairós does not seek peace through silence, but clarity through friction. Identity among them is shaped by conviction: what they defend, what they oppose, what they are willing to risk saying aloud, and what idea gave them form in the first place.

#### Societal Roles
___
Kairós often become orators, reformers, agitators, philosophers, negotiators, pamphleteers, revolutionary leaders, public advocates, and ideological duelists. Some serve in courts, assemblies, universities, salons, and civic movements, where their speech can redirect policy or expose corruption.
