Others operate at the edges of power, stirring workers, students, dissidents, or forgotten communities into action. They are rarely neutral presences. Even when they hold no office, their ability to name tensions others avoid makes them dangerous to brittle systems and invaluable to societies on the edge of transformation.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Kairós names are chosen, declared, or earned rather than passively inherited. Many favor names that sound sharp, resonant, and memorable, suited to public speech and ideological identity. Given names include Vaelis, Tharsin, Kalyx, Rhovar, Zineth, Orithis, Zyren, Lyraen, Vesmira, Xytheis, Yvaela, and Nytheris. Surnames often function as banners, arguments, or remembered victories, such as Truthbearer, Lastspeaker, Firebrand, Ironquill, Thoughtshaper, Of the First Forum, Of the Silver Debate, or Of the Rising Word. Some Kairós change names after a major defeat, revelation, or ideological break, treating the old name as a discarded argument.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Kairós appear wherever ideas begin to gather force: assembly halls, student circles, guild disputes, underground presses, reformist temples, salons, street forums, and the tense rooms where old powers realize language has turned against them. They are welcomed by movements that need a voice and feared by institutions that depend on silence, tradition, or exhaustion. Some become public figures, advocates, negotiators, or scandalous philosophers, while others remain in the margins, sharpening arguments before releasing them into the city like sparks in dry grass. A Kairós rarely belongs comfortably to any single faction for long, because their presence turns belief into pressure and pressure into change.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Kairós means leaning into conviction, timing, rhetoric, and the cost of being born from an idea. Decide what belief gave you form, whether it still drives you, and what happens if the world outgrows it. You may be inspiring, reckless, brilliant, manipulative, sincere, or intolerable, but your words should matter and your silences should feel chosen. Kairós suit bards, warlocks, sorcerers, rogues, clerics, wizards, and any character built around persuasion, disruption, insight, or ideological conflict. Your greatest strength is recognizing the decisive moment: the instant when a phrase, accusation, promise, or challenge can change the shape of everything that follows.

#### Kairos Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Charisma score increases by 2, and your Intelligence score increases by 1.

**Age.** Kairos reach adulthood in their late teens and commonly live between 90 and 140 years. Their communities measure maturity by timing, adaptability, and the ability to recognize decisive moments before they pass.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Kerevahn
*Architects of the Dreamscape, Veilbound Drifters*

*We are the dreamers of the void, the ones who do not belong. The world shudders at our presence, yet it has long forgotten why.*

The Kerevahn were once the masters of the Dreamscape, a people who could shape possibility and bend thought into reality. They are no longer that people. They now live in the Veil, the space between what is real and what should not be, where they build outposts and navigation lighthouses to stabilize its currents and keep others from being lost.

#### Origin
___
The Kerevahn were engineered across eons through selective breeding, genetic refinement, and ideological purges meant to produce a perfect lineage. Their civilization repeatedly unraveled under the weight of its own ambition, triggering civil wars, purges, and near-extinctions. What remains is a divided, flawed, fiercely patriotic people surviving in the Veil and waging an endless war with the Zakariss, whose stolen cores are needed to power the lighthouses.

#### Appearance
___
Tall, gaunt, and otherworldly, with elongated features that feel slightly wrong, as if sculpted by an unfamiliar hand. Their skin is faintly translucent and shimmers subtly, as if they are only half-present in the world. Their eyes are either glowing silver or pitch black without pupils, and many wear bindings, runic tattoos, or relics to anchor themselves to material reality.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Nomadic and fractured, forming small enclaves in ruined places, forgotten temples, and eldritch sites. They do not have a homeland and instead bind themselves to their lighthouses as temporary anchors. They are hunters as much as they are builders, tracking Zakariss through the Veil to reclaim cores that fuel the beacons, while some serve as oracles and mystics who whisper of events yet to come.

#### Societal Roles
___
Outpost builders and lighthouse tenders; Veil navigators and guides; Zakariss hunters and core reclaimers; dream-oracles and mystics; relic-hunters and seers.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Kerevahn names are old, formal, and often fractured by exile. Many carry remnants of noble lineages, engineered bloodlines, lighthouse stations, or lost dream-cities that no longer exist outside their records. Given names tend to be elongated and severe, such as Vaerith, Kholren, Syraeth, Othvane, Ilkharis, Nhalyra, Theryn, Vossik, Maelthir, and Eshvara. Titles and bynames often reference duty, anchoring, or the Veil, such as Beacon-Tender, Core-Hunter, Driftbound, Silver-Eyed, Of the Third Lighthouse, or Keeper of the Unlit Span. A Kerevahn may also carry a missing name, a deliberate blank where a memory, crime, or past incarnation was erased.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Kerevahn are rare, unsettling figures found near thin places, ruined sanctuaries, Veil crossings, forgotten temples, and lighthouse outposts hidden from ordinary maps. Most do not settle permanently, instead binding themselves to temporary anchors where the Veil needs tending or where Zakariss movement has been detected. Cities treat them with a mixture of fear and dependence: feared as cultists, seers, or relic-hunters, yet sought out when roads vanish, dreams become contagious, or travelers disappear between places. A Kerevahn presence often means something nearby is unstable, ancient, or worth keeping from collapse.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Kerevahn means carrying the pride of a shattered people and the practical burden of keeping impossible roads open. You might be a lighthouse keeper, Veil guide, Zakariss hunter, oracle, relic-seeker, exile, or patriot trying to preserve a civilization that has already failed more than once. Decide what memory you are missing, what anchor keeps you from drifting, and whether your duty to the Kerevahn matters more than the people standing beside you now. Kerevahn suit wizards, warlocks, rangers, rogues, clerics, and any character drawn to prophecy, liminal travel, psychic unease, and the fear that their own past may be the most dangerous thing waiting in the dark.

#### Kerevahn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Kerevahn do not age naturally. Some remain unchanged for centuries, while others gradually wither or fade as their connection to reality weakens. A Kerevahn is considered mature once they can withstand prolonged Veil exposure without losing memory, form, or orientation.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Drift Between Worlds.** Once per short rest, as a bonus action, you can shift partially into the Veil for one round. While phased, you can move through creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. You cannot be attacked by non-magical means, but you cannot attack either.

**Dreamborne Mind.** You have telepathy up to 30 feet. You can touch a sleeping creature and see glimpses of their dreams, understanding their emotions and surface thoughts when they wake.

**Memory Fragments.** You start the game with one lost memory, a vision of a past life or a moment erased from time. Your DM may use this as a narrative tool, or it may unlock a latent power later.

**Untethered Soul.** If you fall unconscious, roll a d20. On a 10 or lower, your spirit briefly detaches, forcing you to succeed a DC 10 Charisma save or become incorporeal for 1 minute, unable to interact with the physical world.

**Languages.** You may choose up to 1.0 exotic language instead

## Korrak
*Ironborn Strays, Ash-Crawlers • The last ones standing when the smoke clears.*

*Cities fall. We remain.*

The Korrak are ironborn strays, ash-crawlers, and stubborn survivors of Orimond’s abandoned underlayers. They thrive where civilization collapses into smoke, slag, rust, and forgotten machinery. Born from neglect rather than design, they learned that survival is never granted by those above. It is taken, reinforced, repaired, and defended with both hands. Where others flee toxic air, unstable tunnels, poisoned canals, and failing structures, the Korrak endure. Cities fall. The Korrak remain.

#### Origin
___
The Korrak did not arise from a single homeland, divine lineage, or ancestral realm. They emerged from industrial abandonment itself. As Orimond expanded upward and outward, entire layers were sealed, condemned, or forgotten: collapsed foundries, ash-choked drains, poisoned waterways, broken mills, maintenance tunnels, and furnace vaults no authority wished to remember. Within those places, communities adapted or died. The Korrak adapted. Over generations, scarcity, toxins, pressure, heat, and constant labor hardened both body and culture into something made for survival beneath systems that never intended them to thrive.

#### Appearance
___
Korrak are compact, dense humanoids with bodies that look almost assembled from slag, stone, soot, and reinforced clay. Their skin is thick, cracked, and stratified, with hardened dermal plates across the torso, shoulders, arms, and back. These fissures are growth patterns rather than wounds, formed by generations of pressure, pollution, and collapse. Their coloration ranges from ashen gray and weathered stone to rust-streaked brown, charcoal, and oxidized red. Korrak are rarely tall, usually standing between 5’2” and 5’8”, but their low center of gravity and packed musculature make them seem difficult to move. Their eyes are small, reflective, and deep-set, glinting dull red or gray in darkness like embers under rubble.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Korrak culture is pragmatic, oral, and survival-focused. They keep few grand myths and little patience for polished history, preferring stories of collapses endured, warnings ignored, debts unpaid, and mistakes that must never be repeated. Honor is proven through resilience and usefulness. You do not boast; you haul wreckage, patch the breach, drag the injured out, and stand when the supports fail. Their traditions pass through work crews, hand signs, tool-passing rituals, warning glyphs, salvage marks, and muttered mantras spoken before entering unstable ground. They value directness over courtesy, function over beauty, and endurance over ambition.

#### Societal Roles
___
Korrak are undervalued by Orimond’s elite, but indispensable to the city’s survival. They serve as salvage experts, tunnel scouts, ash-zone guides, industrial enforcers, labor guards, repair crews, sewer navigators, collapse responders, and grudge-scribes who remember debts, betrayals, and names the upper districts would rather lose. They fix what others abandon and recover what others are too frightened or too proud to touch. Some become shock troops or hired muscle, but many prefer the practical work of keeping broken systems running just long enough for people to live another day.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Korrak names are short, guttural, and functional, often drawn from tools, machine sounds, salvage marks, or the harsh rhythm of industrial speech. Personal names include Krek, Boln, Vaska, Sharr, Dret, Ferk, Nomra, Kazzik, Brog, Vorn, and Nakk. Clan tags and epithets are more descriptive than ornamental, such as of the Hollow Pipe, Ironback, Rust-Eye, Born of Sparks, Blacklung, Ashhand, or Undergrate. Honor markers are earned after survival, injury, or service, with names like Smoke-Walker, Steel-Eater, Weld-Bitten, Tunnel-Last, or Bracebreaker. Names change when lives do, and a Korrak who survives something impossible rarely keeps the same name afterward.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Korrak rarely live in the polished face of Orimond. They survive beneath it, in condemned districts, utility caverns, broken industrial layers, drainage vaults, ash tunnels, and neighborhoods written out of civic maps. Their communities are small, mobile, suspicious, and fiercely self-sufficient, gathering in larger numbers only during crises, strikes, collapses, or threats from above. They avoid aristocratic districts unless contract-bound, and they treat authority as something that usually arrives late, lies badly, and leaves before the work is done. Paranormal zones do not frighten them easily. They were born in unnatural places and learned early that the dark is only dangerous when you forget to listen.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Korrak means leaning into grit, suspicion, salvage, and the refusal to stay buried. You are not elegant, subtle, or easily impressed. You judge people by what they do under pressure, what they can repair, and whether they stand by their crew when the ceiling starts to come down. Consider what collapse should have killed you, what relic you carry from someone who did not make it, and who still owes you a debt. Korrak suit fighters, rogues, rangers, barbarians, artificers, and any character built around endurance, urban survival, climbing, toxins, and improvised solutions. Your strength is simple: when everything breaks, you are still moving.

#### Korrak Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Korrak reach adulthood around 15 years of age and rarely live beyond 70. Their communities measure maturity by survival, labor, and the ability to endure danger without becoming a burden.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Your industrial-honed senses grant you Darkvision up to 60 feet. You can see in dim light and darkness as if it were bright light, but only in shades of dull red and gray.

**Toxic Resilience.** You have resistance to poison damage and advantage on saving throws against being poisoned or affected by inhaled toxins (such as smoke, gas, or industrial waste).

**Scrapyard Instincts.** You have proficiency in either Athletics or Sleight of Hand.

**Urban Climber.** You have a climb speed of 20 feet and can move across vertical surfaces without using your hands.

**Survivor’s Grit.** When you roll a Strength, Dexterity, or Constitution saving throw, you can reroll the check and take the higher result. You can use this feature once per long rest.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Luminari
The Luminari are ancient people of living light, native to Everbright and remembered as the distant ancestors of the Aestari. Their bodies hold radiance as flesh holds breath, luminous, precise, and difficult to behold without feeling judged by what they reveal. To the Luminari, light is definition rather than ornament: it clarifies form, preserves memory, and exposes falsehood. Their souls move through a long cycle of reincarnation, returning across millennia until some finally drift beyond rebirth and become luminous spirits among the wandering stars. In Orimond, a Luminari carries the weight of older clarity, walking as a reminder that beauty, discipline, and perfection all began as something far less mortal.

#### Origin
___
The Luminari arose within Everbright, the realm of perfect definition, where reality tends toward completion, clarity, and unbearable coherence. Before the Aestari crossed into the Mortal Plane and learned compromise, their ancestors endured in a world where flaw had nowhere to hide. Luminari souls move through a long cycle of return, reincarnating across millennia while carrying faint impressions of earlier lives. Some eventually fade from that cycle, becoming luminous spirits among the wandering stars, watching from distances even Everbright does not fully command.

#### Appearance
___
Luminari appear as tall, serene humanoids whose forms seem shaped from light given discipline. Their skin ranges from opaline white and pearl-gold to pale rose, silver-blue, or soft violet, often glowing faintly beneath the surface rather than shining outward. Their eyes are luminous and layered, with irises that resemble stars, halos, or refracted glass. Hair is usually bright, weightless, and flowing, appearing silver, white-gold, dawn-pink, or moonlit blue. Their movements are smooth and exact, carrying the impression of a figure almost too clearly resolved for the world around them.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Luminari culture is deeply devotional, shaped by life beneath and around the Forbidden City of Everbright, where the presence of the Emanants defines law, ritual, beauty, and fear. Most Luminari are devout in practice, even when faith takes the form of discipline rather than tenderness. They understand the Emanants as perfected radiances of order, clarity, and divine function, and their society is built around approaching those impossible examples without presuming equality with them. Identity among the Luminari is therefore not merely personal, but liturgical: each life is a refinement of the soul through service, reincarnation, memory, and visible conduct. To stand in Everbright is to be seen, and to be seen is to be measured.

#### Societal Roles
___
Luminari most often serve as judges, philosophers, memory-keepers, radiant architects, ritual arbiters, and custodians of Everbright’s older laws. Some act as guides to younger peoples, though their guidance can feel merciless, since they tend to reveal what others would rather leave softened or unnamed. Among the Aestari, they are treated with awe, discomfort, and ancestral reverence, while in Orimond they are rare figures associated with celestial authority, old vows, impossible standards, and truths that survive across ages.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Luminari names are formal, resonant, and often tied to light, recurrence, and remembered incarnations. A name may change between lives, but older names are rarely discarded entirely, instead becoming part of a luminous sequence preserved in ritual memory. Given names often sound melodic and precise, such as Aurelian, Vaelith, Elyra, Solen, Ithariel, Caelora, or Lumaen. Lineage or cycle-names may reference radiance, stars, thresholds, or prior lives, such as Dawn-Returned, of the Seventh Radiance, Starheld, Veilbright, or Memory-in-Light.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Luminari are almost never ordinary residents. They appear as envoys from Everbright, exiled devotees, radiant judges, temple guests, reincarnated wanderers, or silent figures drawn to places where old vows and hidden falsehoods have begun to strain reality. Their presence unsettles even the Aestari, who recognize in them an ancestral clarity too close to the source to be comfortable. Most people treat a Luminari with reverence, caution, or resentment, because their gaze can make private compromises feel suddenly visible. They are found near high temples, sealed courts, celestial observatories, forbidden archives, and sanctuaries where the influence of the Emanants still falls across mortal affairs like a blade of light.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Luminari means carrying ancient clarity into a world built on ambiguity, compromise, and decay. You may be devout, severe, compassionate, alien, judgmental, or quietly exhausted by reincarnations that keep returning you to unfinished work. Decide which Emanant shaped your devotion, what fragments of past lives still trouble you, and whether your light reveals truth to heal, to correct, or to condemn. Luminari suit clerics, paladins, wizards, monks, warlocks, bards, and any character drawn to memory, judgment, reincarnation, celestial law, or impossible standards. Your central tension is whether clarity makes you wise, merciful, and precise, or merely unbearable to those still learning how to live in shadow.

#### Luminari Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Luminari reach adulthood around 80 years of age and can live for several millennia. Their souls reincarnate through a cycle of return, though some eventually fade from that cycle and become luminous spirits among the wandering stars.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Lysorian
*Architects of Sound, Code, and Knowledge • Knowledge resonates. Silence remembers.*

*“A pattern once heard can never be unheard.”*

Tall, gaunt, and contemplative, the Lysorian stand apart as archivists of memory and interpreters of pattern. They read the world as others read scripture, finding meaning in resonance, silence, and repetition.

#### Origin
___
The Lysorian claim descent from the first monasteries that formed at the edges of the Dreamscape, where mortals began dreaming with enough force to leave marks behind. Those early dream-marks were unstable, so the Lysorian learned to bind them into chant, ink, and stone. Over centuries they became the stewards of mnemonic vaults, keeping songs that can restore forgotten names, and diagrams that can map a lie back to its first breath.

#### Appearance
___
Lysorians are tall and slender, with elongated limbs and narrow torsos that give them an austere silhouette. Their faces are long and angular, dominated by large, dark, reflective eyes that appear almost pupil-less, lending them a perpetually watchful, inward-focused expression. Their skin ranges from pale stone to parchment beige, often bearing fine creases even in youth, as if shaped by thought rather than age. Hair is thin and straight, typically worn long and tied back in simple, functional styles. Their hands are delicate and precise, with elongated fingers suited for careful work with scrolls, instruments, and fine tools. In dress, Lysorians favor layered robes and archival wraps, stitched with chant-bands, sigils, and notation glyphs rather than ornament.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Lysorian culture is defined by preservation, interpretation, and transmission of knowledge. They believe information is not owned but stewarded, and that forgetting is the gravest failure. Music, mathematics, rhetoric, and spell-structure are treated as dialects of the same truth, so a debate may be answered with a chord, a proof, or a counter-rite. Identity is often tied to one’s archive lineage, vow-chain, or discipline, rather than bloodline or territory.

#### Societal Roles
___
Lysorians most commonly serve as archivists, court-librarians, cryptic monks, oath-recorders, map-singers, and ritual notaries. They are often hired to verify treaties, decode cursed inscriptions, interpret prophetic dreams, and preserve dangerous knowledge inside sealed collections. A rare few become wandering listeners, traveling Orimond to capture dying languages, fading songs, and last witness accounts before they vanish.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Lysorian names are soft and elongated, designed to flow when spoken aloud. Surnames often reference archives, harmonic concepts, or vow-titles rather than ancestry, such as Lethara of the Third Stanza or Orun Vale-Chant. Names may change once in a lifetime after a defining work, marked by the addition of a stanza-name, an archive-seal, or a vow-word.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Lysorians gather near old vaults, monasteries, and resonance halls built to hold sound without decay. Many prefer quiet environments and measured conversation, since overwhelming noise is considered a kind of spiritual contamination. In cities, they are found in scriptoria, universities, temple-libraries, and embassy record-halls, where their presence is respected and sometimes feared. People seek them for truth, but worry about what truths the Lysorians might quietly keep.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Lysorian means leaning into observation, patience, and insight. You are not impulsive, but you are decisive once a pattern reveals itself, and you treat promises as things that leave stains on the world. Consider what your character listens for, what knowledge they protect, and what memory they refuse to surrender. Decide whether you serve a vault, a vow, a patron, or the idea that truth must survive regardless of who is harmed by it.

#### Lysorian Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Lysorians reach adulthood in their late teens and commonly live between 140 and 180 years. Their communities measure maturity by discipline, recall, and the ability to preserve knowledge without corrupting its meaning.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Low-light vision

**Harmonic Perception.** You have advantage on checks involving sound patterns, coded chants, or ritual timing.

**Archival Mind.** You gain proficiency in History or Investigation.

**Pattern Recall.** Once per long rest, you can reroll a failed Intelligence check.

**Quiet Discipline.** You have advantage on saving throws against being charmed while you can hear yourself speak or breathe.

**Sealkeeper.** You have advantage on checks to identify forgeries, altered records, or broken oaths in written agreements.

**Languages.** You may choose up to 1.0 exotic language instead

## Mireborn
The Mireborn are hollow strays from the surface wetlands of Nevermourn, pale and waterlogged beings shaped by the Realm of Shadows before they ever set foot in Orimond. They drift between life and death because their homeland does the same, holding existence in a state of damp suspension where breath, hunger, and warmth become negotiable things. Their presence unsettles the living not because they are undead, but because they belong to a place where endings do not arrive cleanly. Where they pass, the air cools, still water darkens, and memory gathers like silt around the feet.

#### Origin
___
The Mireborn come from the surface reaches of Nevermourn, the Realm of Shadows, where dark wetlands, drowned fields, and lightless shallows stretch beneath a sky that never fully opens. They are not corpses returned by accident, but a people shaped by a realm where life and death blur into the same slow current. In those shadow-mires, identity softens, breath becomes optional, and memory settles into the body like silt. Some Mireborn crossed into Orimond through flooded thresholds, shadowed marshes, and old planar wounds, carrying with them the damp stillness of a world where nothing is ever entirely alive or entirely gone.

#### Appearance
___
Mireborn vary widely in height and build, but all bear signs of drowning, burial, or long exposure to wet decay. Their skin is pale, gray, blue-white, or bog-darkened, often slick or waxen, with veins faintly visible beneath the surface. Hair hangs heavy and damp, sometimes tangled with reeds, silt, funerary threads, or fragments of old marsh growth. Their eyes may be clouded, dark, or reflective like deep water under moonlight. They move with a slow, drifting steadiness, as though still resisting a current no one else can feel.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Mireborn rarely form large societies, but they gather around shared recognition of unfinished fate. They value remembrance, quiet purpose, and respect for the dead, especially those denied proper burial or name. Many distrust celebrations of life that refuse to acknowledge loss, and they often show strange tenderness toward graves, abandoned homes, drowned relics, and old promises. Some seek to recover the life they lost, while others accept that they are now something else entirely. To a Mireborn, memory is not comfort. It is the weight that keeps them from vanishing.

#### Societal Roles
___
Mireborn commonly serve as mortuary keepers, grave-tenders, marsh guides, spirit mediators, paranormal investigators, crypt wardens, plague-remnant witnesses, and caretakers of drowned districts. Their resistance to ordinary bodily needs makes them suited to work in dangerous, flooded, airless, or haunted places. Some become advisors in matters of death, inheritance, missing persons, or restless spirits, while others are exploited by institutions that treat their persistence as a useful anomaly. They are often feared, but when something must be retrieved from water, tomb, or memory, people eventually come looking for them.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Mireborn may keep the names they held before their death, though many find those names painful, incomplete, or no longer entirely theirs. Others adopt names tied to water, burial, silence, or unfinished passage, such as Fen, Mourn, Silt, Edda, Vale, Brine, Neris, Hollow, Reed, or Latch. Bynames often mark the place or circumstance of their return, such as Drowned-of-Mere, Stillwater, Bogwake, Gravecurrent, Reedbound, Bell-Sunk, or Of the Last Breath. A Mireborn who discovers the reason they remained may change names again, treating the old one as something finally buried.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Mireborn drift toward mortuaries, crypt districts, flooded foundations, canals, marsh-edge settlements, forgotten plague wards, and places where the boundary between the living and the dead has grown thin. They are treated with caution, pity, suspicion, or scholarly hunger, depending on who is looking. Some find steady work tending the dead or investigating hauntings, while others remain at the edges of society, uncomfortable among people who expect them to explain why they are still here. Their presence is unsettling, but often useful, especially in a city where many things are buried poorly and remembered worse.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Mireborn means exploring persistence, grief, and unfinished purpose. Decide what your character remembers of dying, what they do not remember, and what keeps them moving when their body no longer needs breath, food, or warmth. You might be solemn, gentle, eerie, detached, protective, or quietly furious at being denied rest. Mireborn suit clerics, warlocks, rangers, rogues, druids, monks, and investigators drawn to spirits, marshes, crypts, curses, and lost histories. Your central question is simple: what still needs to be done before the water finally lets you go?

#### Mireborn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Mireborn reach adulthood around 25 years of age and commonly live between 120 and 160 years. Their communities measure maturity by patience, resilience, and the ability to navigate danger that does not announce itself.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Mistaryn
*The Waterborn Who Walk • From the tides we rose. On land, we endure.*

*“Water remembers us, even when the world forgets.”*

The Mistaryn are an ancient amphibious people whose oceanic homelands were shattered when the seas of Orimond broke and the floating lands rose. Forced onto land, they adapted slowly and painfully, becoming beings caught between water and air, memory and survival.

#### Origin
___
Once rulers of deep-ocean cities beneath the world-seas of Orimond, the Mistaryn were displaced by a world-shaping cataclysm that drained oceans and fractured the world into floating masses. Their exile reshaped both their bodies and their culture.

#### Appearance
___
Mistaryn are slender, elongated humanoids with smooth, pale to blue-green skin that often carries a faint sheen. Their eyes are large and dark, adapted for low light, and their necks bear vestigial gill slits. Many have fin-like tendrils along the head or neck, partial webbing on hands or feet, and an overall fluid, almost drifting posture even on land.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Mistaryn culture revolves around memory, loss, and water preservation. They revere mist, rain, and condensation as sacred remnants of the sea. Oral histories, breath-songs, and water rituals replace written records. Many believe the oceans will one day return.

#### Societal Roles
___
Mistaryn often become hydromancers, mist-callers, rain-readers, pearl artisans, canal engineers, archivists of oral history, or spiritual guides tied to water and memory.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names are fluid and melodic, often containing breathy pauses or doubled vowels. Surnames reference water, depth, or loss. Examples include Thal’een, Isskar, Myyshka, Caelthir; surnames such as Mistveil, Brineshadow, Pearlshed.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Most Mistaryn live in mist-heavy cities, river deltas, or artificial waterways where humidity can be maintained. They form close-knit enclaves and avoid arid regions. Long exposure to dry climates causes discomfort and illness.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Play a Mistaryn as someone shaped by displacement and memory. You may be gentle or distant, ritual-bound or quietly defiant. Water, loss, and endurance define your worldview more than ambition or conquest.

#### Mistaryn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Mistaryn mature slowly, reaching adulthood around 30 years of age. Most live between 180 and 240 years, though those who remain close to deep water, mist-heavy enclaves, or stable humidity can endure longer.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Veil-Adapted Form.** You have advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made in mist, fog, dim light, or lightly obscured environments, and you can hold your breath for up to 1 hour.

**Amphibious Drift.** You can breathe air and water, and you gain a swim speed equal to your walking speed.

**Liminal Slip.** Once per short rest, as a bonus action, you can move through creatures’ spaces and ignore difficult terrain until the end of your turn.

**Pressure Memory.** You have advantage on Constitution saving throws against exhaustion, pressure effects, and environmental hazards.

**Veiled Perception.** You have advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on sound or motion rather than sight.

**Ancestral Echo.** Once per long rest, when you fail a Dexterity or Constitution saving throw, you can reroll the save and take the new result.

**Languages.**

## Myrleth
The Myrleth, also called Myrlyn, are small stone-touched wanderers of the Verdant Cradle, luminous and quick-hearted beings who listen to the deep veins of the world as others listen to roads. They are known as Wish Hunters because each adult Myrleth is driven by an intimate longing to find a wish: a real and hidden thing, buried in stone, fate, memory, or mineral possibility. To outsiders, this sounds like superstition. To the Myrleth, it is simply the way the world speaks. Somewhere beneath root, rock, ruin, or mountain, the wish is waiting, and the stone remembers the path.

#### Origin
___
The Myrleth began as deep guardians of the Verdant Cradle, tending the places where root systems, mineral veins, and ley currents braided together beneath the living world. Unlike peoples who command stone from outside, the Myrleth learned to enter it, moving through rock as though passing through a remembered door. Over time, part of their society turned outward, leaving the Cradle to follow wishes scattered through the wider realms. Some return home after finding the one that called them. Others become lifelong wanderers, passing from cavern to ruin to mountain road, unable or unwilling to stop listening for the next impossible glimmer.

#### Appearance
___
Myrleth are Small humanoids, usually standing between 2’6” and 3’2”, with compact bodies that seem both dense and strangely light. Their skin often carries a mineral sheen, catching dim light like polished stone, quartz dust, mica, or gemstone inclusions. Fine crystalline veins may trace their hands, cheeks, temples, and throat, pulsing faintly when they hum to stone or sense a hidden path. Their eyes glow with molten or jewel-like color, shifting subtly with emotion, danger, or proximity to a wish. Many carve delicate runes, maps, or protective marks into their skin, treating the body as both memory and tool.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Myrleth culture is shaped by longing, generosity, and the sacred privacy of the wish. Adulthood begins when the need to search awakens, sending a Myrleth into the world to follow stone, scent, omen, and instinct toward whatever calls them. Asking whether a Myrleth has found their wish is deeply taboo, because the answer reveals too much about hope, failure, shame, and fulfillment. They are often friendly, curious, and giving, drawn to companions who value discovery more than possession. Many form lifelong partnerships, binding love, trust, and shared wandering into a single vow of search and return.

#### Societal Roles
___
Myrleth commonly serve as underground guides, mineral trackers, gemcutters, tunnel-singers, ley-listeners, relic finders, rune-carvers, cave scouts, and keepers of hidden paths. Their ability to sense stone, danger, malice, and buried possibility makes them invaluable to miners, adventurers, temples, and explorers. They are also sought by rulers and merchant powers who want rare ores, lost vaults, or forgotten artifacts located with minimal effort. Myrleth rarely enjoy being treated as tools of extraction. Their gift is rooted in relationship with the earth, and careless digging is one of the quickest ways to turn their warmth into refusal.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Myrleth names are bright, compact, and musical, often carrying clicks, soft consonants, or stone-like syllables that resonate well underground. Given names include Miri, Tovel, Lekk, Yara, Pimm, Oryn, Vessa, Kith, Runnel, Nemi, Thova, and Zil. Clan names and bynames often reference minerals, paths, echoes, or discoveries, such as Quartzstep, Deepglimmer, Veinwise, Wish-Scent, Micaheel, Corehum, Stonewhisper, Amber-Eye, or Underroot. A Myrleth may take a new byname after finding a wish, losing one, or choosing to keep searching when tradition says they should return home.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Myrleth are seen as peculiar, charming, and occasionally unnerving wanderers, especially in mining towns, old tunnels, ruin districts, mountain settlements, and undercity markets. They find work as guides, artisans, gem appraisers, tunnel scouts, informants, and seekers of things lost beneath streets or memory. Some are courted by guilds and noble houses for their ability to locate rare resources, though Myrleth are wary of contracts that smell like greed rather than discovery. Those who live in cities often keep small stone shrines, mineral collections, or hidden burrows where they can hear the ground clearly.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Myrleth means leaning into curiosity, instinct, generosity, and the private ache of searching for something only you may recognize. Decide what your wish feels like when it calls: a scent, a sound, a pressure behind the eyes, a warmth in stone, or a name you almost remember. You might be cheerful, secretive, restless, gentle, obsessive, or quietly afraid that finding your wish will end the person you have become while seeking it. Myrleth suit rogues, rangers, druids, bards, artificers, clerics, and any character drawn to exploration, hidden routes, rare materials, and the strange mercy of knowing that even impossible things can be found.

#### Myrleth Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Myrleth mature quickly, reaching adulthood around 12 years of age. Most live between 70 and 100 years, though those who avoid hard travel, bad bargains, and dangerous work can live somewhat longer.

**Size.** Small

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Naureli
*Seahorsekin • Voices of the Deep, Brokers of Balance*

*“Currents do not argue. They carry.”*

The Naureli are amphibious diplomats, archivists, and brokers of balance, shaped by tide, memory, and negotiation. Equally at home beneath the waves or within halls of power, they move through Orimond with quiet authority, listening before they speak and speaking only when words can alter the current. They are not passive observers. They preserve continuity, redirect conflict, maintain trade, and record what other peoples would rather forget. Where others conquer, endure, or withdraw, the Naureli mediate. Currents do not argue. They carry.

#### Origin
___
The Naureli emerged from the deep littoral basins surrounding Serevan, where freshwater currents, oceanic tides, and planar seepage meet in layered motion. Their oldest legends claim they learned speech by listening to reefs argue with the sea, discovering language as alignment rather than domination. Over generations, they built submerged archives, treaty halls, reef-courts, and trade corridors that linked surface powers to aquatic realms and planar interests. Their history is one of patient interdependence: a people who understood early that whoever controls passage, record, and terms can prevent wars before armies know they are being denied.

#### Appearance
___
Naureli are bipedal amphibians with slender, controlled bodies and elongated facial structures reminiscent of seahorses, giving them a dignified, sculptural profile. Their hands are palmed, their digits subtly webbed, and their movements precise rather than forceful, adapted for both swimming and formal courtly presence. Fine iridescent scales cover their skin, shifting through blues, greens, pearlescent whites, and muted golds according to light and hydration. Along the neck, spine, and shoulders, decorative frills and fin-crests rise or settle with emotion, posture, and water pressure. Their large, dark, reflective eyes give the constant impression that they are listening even in silence.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Naureli culture is founded on knowledge stewardship, mercantile ethics, and diplomatic restraint. They value precise language, long memory, reputation over force, and stability over conquest. A careless word is considered more dangerous than a drawn blade, because a blade wounds once while a foolish phrase may poison an accord for generations. Disputes are settled through formal rhetoric, archival precedent, compensatory exchange, and binding negotiation. Their greatest treasures are the coral-script archives of Serevan, living reef-libraries whose bioluminescent growth patterns preserve treaties, lineages, debts, and histories in forms that can be read, sung, and remembered by touch.

#### Societal Roles
___
Naureli commonly serve as scholars, historians, trade envoys, treaty archivists, merchant princes, logistical coordinators, legal mediators, and neutral witnesses in multi-species coalitions. Their mastery of both surface and aquatic economies makes them indispensable wherever goods, laws, and loyalties must cross between peoples. Some act as court advisors, ceasefire brokers, inheritance arbiters, or custodians of dangerous records. Others maintain submerged trade routes, verify maritime claims, or settle disputes between river towns, reef houses, and inland powers. Their influence is rarely theatrical. It appears in wars that never begin, contracts that hold, and routes that remain open.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Naureli names are melodic, flowing, and syllabic, designed to remain clear both underwater and on land. Given names often rise and fall like currents, such as Thalavir, Orellnara, Kessaquar, Pelithane, Sorynthae, Vaelun, Ishalore, Nerithae, or Quoralen. Surnames and formal titles are often tied to coral formations, ancestral reefs, historic trade routes, or negotiated accords, such as Reef-of-Glass, Pearlcurrent, Tide-Vault, Serevan Deep, Goldchannel, Brine Accord, or of the Third Littoral. A Naureli may gain a new title after brokering a major peace, preserving an endangered archive, or carrying a treaty safely across hostile waters.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Across Orimond, Naureli maintain a respected but reserved presence. In major cities, they gather around aquatic enclaves, research institutions, embassy quarters, canal districts, and humid archive-halls where water access is carefully regulated. They rarely seek public prominence, yet many accords, trade compacts, succession settlements, and ceasefires exist because a Naureli quietly ensured that each side could retreat without humiliation. In Serevan and its allied waters, their authority is more visible, woven into reef-courts, merchant channels, and living archives. Elsewhere, a Naureli presence often signals that negotiation remains possible, even when everyone else has forgotten how to listen.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Naureli means leaning into patience, precision, memory, and the power of well-timed words. Consider what knowledge your character protects, what agreement they witnessed, and which current they follow: commerce, truth, balance, lineage, or peace. You might be a diplomat, archivist, scholar, hydromancer, envoy, merchant, investigator, or quiet observer whose calm hides considerable leverage. Naureli suit clerics, bards, rogues, druids, wizards, monks, and any character built around insight, negotiation, history, water, or restraint. Your strength lies in opening doors others never notice and redirecting conflict before it becomes irreversible.

#### Naureli Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Naureli mature slowly, reaching adulthood around 30 years of age. Most live between 180 and 260 years, though archivist lineages and those who remain close to stable reef-cities sometimes endure longer.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Amphibious.** You can breathe air and water.

**Swim Speed.** You have a swim speed of 30 feet.

**Scholarly Grace.** Gain proficiency in History or Persuasion.

**Regal Bearing.** You have advantage on Charisma checks when interacting with Serevan nobility.

**Frilled Awareness.** You cannot be surprised while underwater.

**Languages.**

## Ordonants
#### Ordonants Traits

**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Ordonants mature at a controlled and predictable rate, reaching adulthood around 20 years of age. Most live between 100 and 150 years, though their vitality often depends less on age than on stability of purpose, environment, and assigned function.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Orphai
The Orphai are echoes of the First Thought, beings born when an idea takes root deeply enough in the collective consciousness to become almost alive. They are neither mortals in the ordinary sense nor spirits, illusions, or gods. They are remnants of abandoned meaning, lost language, unfinished philosophy, and knowledge that refused to vanish completely. Where the Kairós embody the force of new conviction, the Orphai preserve what came before speech, before record, and before certainty. To meet an Orphai is to feel that something forgotten has turned its face toward you.

#### Origin
___
Orphai are not born through bloodline or flesh. They emerge when a thought, word, question, or memory survives past the culture that first carried it. Some arise from extinct civilizations, erased scriptures, silenced prayers, lost sciences, or the final dream of a people no one remembers. Others form around ideas so old that even the gods dispute their origin. Their existence depends on remembrance, though remembrance need not be clear. A single inscription, ritual, melody, or recurring question may be enough to anchor one. When the idea that sustains an Orphai is truly forgotten, the Orphai fades with it.

#### Appearance
___
Orphai appear humanoid, but subtly unreal, as if their bodies were assembled from memory rather than flesh. Their skin often carries soft, shifting tones of weathered parchment, dusky violet, muted blue-gray, ash-pale rose, or faded ink. Their eyes are deep and liquid, with pupils that flicker or blur as though focusing on several moments at once. Hair is fine, threadlike, and slow-moving, commonly midnight black, silver-gray, indigo, or pale white, drifting as if stirred by an unseen current. Their features are elongated and eerily balanced, while their hands sometimes move a fraction out of sync with the rest of the body, suggesting that time does not hold them evenly.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Orphai culture is built around preservation, interpretation, and the ethics of memory. They believe forgotten things do not disappear harmlessly; they leave absences that shape the world in secret. To preserve a word, a name, a question, or a forbidden technique is to keep part of reality from collapsing into silence. Some Orphai are reverent archivists, guarding ancient truths with monastic patience. Others are vestigial wanderers, drawn to people and places that nearly remember them. The fractured among them exist between states, never fully certain whether they are a person, a memory, or the last symptom of an idea refusing extinction.

#### Societal Roles
___
Orphai often serve as archivists, translators, interpreters of dead languages, keepers of forbidden lore, dream-scribes, memory witnesses, occult scholars, and guides through ruins whose histories no longer align with surviving records. They are sought by temples, universities, courts, and secret orders whenever a lost text must be read or a vanished civilization understood. Some act as quiet advisors, offering cryptic but truthful insights drawn from knowledge no living mind still holds. Others become dangerous simply by existing, because the ideas they preserve may be ones powerful institutions worked very hard to erase.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Orphai names are soft, whispered, and often feel half-remembered even when clearly spoken. Given names include Vaelis, Orin, Zeyth, Lirien, Tharnis, Morro, Saeris, Yvanna, Xythea, Velis, Aunai, and Lysithe. Many take surnames or bynames tied to memory, silence, language, or unfinished thought, such as Echolight, Thoughtveil, Whisperglass, Remnantsong, Unremembered, Silenceborn, Hollowecho, Lastvoice, Inkfade, or Question-Left-Open. An Orphai may change names when the idea sustaining them shifts, when a forgotten truth is restored, or when the last speaker of an old name finally dies.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Orphai drift toward archives, ruined schools, abandoned temples, sealed libraries, dead cities, old theaters, and places where language has accumulated like dust. They are rare, and many people mistake them for ghosts, dream-figures, or Veil-touched anomalies. Scholars value them, though not always kindly, while rulers and institutions fear the truths they may carry from erased histories. Some Orphai live quietly as scribes, translators, or wandering teachers. Others remain near forgotten districts, listening for ideas on the edge of disappearance and deciding which ones deserve to survive.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Orphai means exploring memory, identity, and the burden of preserving what the world has discarded. Decide what idea, word, question, or lost civilization anchors your existence, and whether you protect it out of devotion, fear, habit, or love. You may be serene, cryptic, gentle, unsettling, sorrowful, or fiercely protective of knowledge others consider useless or dangerous. Orphai suit wizards, clerics, bards, warlocks, monks, rogues, and any character built around lore, language, psychic distance, forgotten histories, or strange survival. Your central question is what remains of you if the world finally forgets what you were made to remember.

#### Orphai Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Intelligence score increases by 1.

**Age.** Orphai mature slowly, reaching adulthood around 30 years of age. Most live between 180 and 250 years, though some persist longer in old groves, fungal sanctuaries, or places where the boundary between body and environment grows thin.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Oteisha
The Oteisha are small, patient descendants of the Pykari who settled in the Withered Womb and learned to live with decay as a condition of existence rather than a sign of failure. Where their wandering kin followed flame, omen, and motion, the Oteisha rooted themselves in a realm of rot, spores, damp silence, and slow transformation. They are not morbid by nature, though other peoples often mistake them for so. To an Oteisha, every ending feeds something, every body returns to a system, and every ruin is only a beginning that has lost its witness.

#### Origin
___
he Oteisha descend from Pykari ancestors who left the migratory paths and entered the Withered Womb, settling in its fungal valleys, corpse-gardens, spore forests, and humid hollows. Generations of exposure changed them, reshaping their bodies around patience, resistance, and the careful reading of decay. Their old connection to wandering fire softened into an affinity for decomposition, renewal, and hidden growth. Long ago, some Oteisha emigrated into Orimond through passages around Zhymeus, bringing with them spore-lineages, burial customs, rot-craft, and warnings from a realm where every living thing learns how to become soil before it becomes anything else.

#### Appearance
___
Oteisha are Small humanoids, compact and light-footed, usually marked by fungal, earthen, or decay-adapted traits. Their skin may range from pale mushroom-white, gray-brown, and mossy olive to muted ochre, bruised violet, or soft umber, often patterned with speckles, spore-dust, or vein-like discolorations. Their hair is typically fine, wispy, or fibrous, sometimes resembling dry grass, fungal threads, or rootlike strands. Their eyes are large and reflective, well suited to dim hollows and shaded growths, often amber, black, milky green, or rust-red. Many carry a faint scent of damp earth, old leaves, or medicinal rot, especially after rain.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Oteisha culture is built around the discipline of decay. They treat rot as both danger and inheritance, something to be understood, guided, and contained rather than feared blindly. Patience is a virtue because transformation cannot be rushed without becoming corruption. Their communities preserve spore-lines, compost rites, funerary gardens, medicinal molds, and long genealogies of what each settlement has allowed to die well. They respect the Pykari as distant kin, but they do not share their restless hunger for motion. Oteisha identity is quieter, slower, and more cyclical, shaped by the belief that survival often begins with surrendering the form that no longer serves.

#### Societal Roles
___
Oteisha commonly serve as spore-keepers, rot-herbalists, grave-gardeners, poison tasters, decay-readers, fungal cultivators, plague wardens, corpse-field tenders, and guides through Withered or contaminated landscapes. In Orimond, their knowledge makes them valuable to healers, apothecaries, undertakers, druids, alchemists, and settlements dealing with blight, famine, or tainted soil. They are often mistrusted because their work brings them close to death, refuse, and sickness, but few peoples understand better how to turn danger into medicine, waste into food, and ruin into protection.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Oteisha names are soft, earthy, and slightly dry in sound, often derived from fungi, soil, roots, old Pykari fragments, or Withered Womb dialects. Given names include Oti, Resha, Nemu, Veyk, Shoro, Luma, Tesh, Ariko, Mavri, Senn, and Isha. Family names and bynames often reference spore-lines, rot-craft, burial places, or migration from the Withered Womb, such as Sporeveil, Rootmourn, Softrot, Ashcap, Fenmold, Gravebloom, Ochrethread, Wombstray, or Zhymeus-Crossed. A name may change after a first successful cultivation, a plague survived, a burial rite completed, or a return journey to ancestral ground.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Oteisha are found most often near Zhymeus, old fungal enclaves, marsh settlements, apothecary quarters, burial gardens, undercity farms, and districts where waste must be transformed rather than hidden. They are useful and therefore tolerated, but rarely fully understood. Farmers seek them when soil turns strange, physicians when infection resists ordinary treatment, and city officials when rot threatens to become plague. Many Oteisha live in close-knit communities that maintain humidity, spore-control, and quiet rites from the Withered Womb. They tend to avoid sterile places, which feel to them less clean than spiritually empty.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Oteisha means leaning into patience, inherited strangeness, and the wisdom of slow transformation. Decide what your character brought from the Withered Womb: a spore-line, a family warning, a burial custom, a forbidden fungus, or a belief about what endings are for. You may be gentle, unsettling, practical, fatalistic, nurturing, or quietly amused by peoples who fear every sign of decay. Oteisha suit druids, rangers, rogues, clerics, monks, alchemists, and any character tied to medicine, poison, fungi, death rites, survival, or hidden renewal. Your strength lies in knowing that what rots is not always lost.

#### Oteisha Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Oteisha reach adulthood around 25 years of age and commonly live between 160 and 220 years. Their communities measure maturity by resilience, patience, and the ability to understand decay as both danger and inheritance.

**Size.** Small

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Pykari
*The Wandering Sparks • Born of motion, never held*

*“The fire doesn’t tell you where to go.
It tells you when to move.”*

The Pykari are wandering sparks, small and swift descendants of the Ashen Spiral who move through Orimond like embers carried by a restless wind. They are a people of motion, omen, intuition, and sudden disappearance, bound less to territory than to timing. Their wisdom is old, but rarely solemn; it arrives in jokes, songs, interrupted journeys, half-heard warnings, and the decision to leave a place one hour before disaster arrives. A Pykari does not ask where the road ends. They listen for when it is time to move.

#### Origin
___
The Pykari descend from the Ashen Spiral, a liminal realm of shifting fire, motion, and echo that brushes against the edges of the Dreamscape. Pykari tradition claims they were once spirits of ember and intention, woven from movement before some chose to anchor themselves to Orimond in flesh. Whether this is myth, planar memory, or a truth too old to verify, the Spiral still calls to them through dreams, instincts, guttering flames, broken paths, and sudden restlessness. Their distant kin took other roads: the Arochi settled the high fields and trade winds, the Oteisha rooted in the Withered Womb, and the Tyrikai remained in Maligath’s harsher fires.

#### Appearance
___
Pykari are very small humanoids, usually standing between 2’8” and 3’4” and weighing no more than 40 pounds. Their bodies are light, compact, and agile, built for balance, speed, and quick changes of direction. Their skin is deep obsidian black, matte and warm to the touch, often showing faint ember-sheen patterns under stress, magic, or strong emotion. Their hair grows thick and tightly curled, most often dark brown or black, but frequently threaded with fiery red, copper, or ember-gold tones. Their eyes are large, almond-shaped, and bright with amber, copper, or molten orange hues, reflecting low light like banked coals. Their ears are large and sharply pointed, giving them a perpetually alert, listening expression.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Pykari culture is nomadic by instinct, not by poverty or lack. They believe the world speaks through coincidence, interruption, flame, weather, dice, broken wheels, missed meetings, and roads that suddenly feel wrong. Planning has its place, but intuition is sacred because it hears the Spiral before reason can explain it. Pykari value adaptability over dominance, listening over speaking, motion over possession, and the courage to leave before certainty turns into a cage. Their communities form as caravans, circuits, troupes, camps, and hidden enclaves that may dissolve overnight. Elders are respected because they have survived motion the longest, not because they have the right to command.

#### Societal Roles
___
Pykari often become messengers, couriers, scouts, pathfinders, fortune-readers, fire-dancers, omen-speakers, smugglers, performers, intermediaries, and go-betweens. They thrive in liminal places: crossroads, markets, ports, caravan routes, border towns, festival grounds, and districts where the Dreamscape presses thinly against the world. Their small size, quick movement, and instinctive sense for timing make them valuable wherever information, warning, or quiet passage matters. They are rarely trusted by rigid authorities, but they are often sought out when a message must arrive, a hidden road must be found, or a bad future must be sensed before it hardens.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Pykari names are short, melodic, and fluid, often one or two syllables and easy to call across a road, crowd, or campfire. Given names include Pyra, Kesh, Ember, Ryn, Tali, Ashi, Vexa, Siro, Nym, Kiri, Osha, and Zek. Epithets are earned through story, movement, omen, or reputation rather than fixed lineage, such as of the Turning Road, Coal-Step, Quicksmile, Driftborn, Last-Ember, Redwind, Ashwhisper, or Moon-Spark. Full names are rarely used outside ritual, oath, mourning, or deep trust. A Pykari may change names after a major journey, a fulfilled omen, a narrow escape, or a road they choose never to walk again.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Pykari are found everywhere and nowhere: trade roads, dock markets, caravan circles, festival camps, forgotten districts, border settlements, rooftops, alleys, and places where the Veil, Dreamscape, or Ashen Spiral leaves faint pressure on the world. They rarely build permanent structures, and when they do, those structures are designed to be left behind without grief. Some cities welcome them as guides, entertainers, messengers, and omen-speakers, while others treat them as suspicious wanderers who never stay long enough to be taxed, counted, or controlled. Pykari communities learn which gates open easily, which guards can be charmed, and which roads should never be taken after sunset.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Pykari means leaning into speed, intuition, expressive emotion, and the art of choosing a better place to stand. You are rarely built for direct confrontation, but you excel at repositioning, reading the room, escaping danger, and turning coincidence into opportunity. Decide what omens your character trusts, what made them leave their last community, and what road they secretly hope the Spiral will never ask them to take. Pykari suit rogues, bards, rangers, sorcerers, monks, druids, and any character built around movement, stealth, performance, survival, fire, or fate. Your strength is knowing that motion is not avoidance. Sometimes motion is wisdom.

#### Pykari Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Charisma score increases by 1.

**Age.** Pykari mature quickly, reaching adulthood by 15 years old, but they live long for their size—often surpassing 180 years. Elders say the fire within them burns slow but never fully fades.

**Size.** Small

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** Your connection to the Ashen Spiral grants you Darkvision up to 60 feet. You see the world in shades of deep red and orange, as if embers still smolder in the shadows.

**Flickering Step.** Once per short rest, as a bonus action, teleport up to 10 feet to an unoccupied space you can see.

**Nomadic Adaptability.** Gain proficiency in two skills of your choice from Stealth, Insight, Survival, or Performance.

**Whisper of the Flames.** You know Produce Flame. At 3rd level, you can cast Detect Magic once per long rest. At 5th level, you can cast Misty Step once per long rest. Your spellcasting ability is Charisma or Wisdom (your choice).

**Languages.** You may choose up to 1.0 exotic language instead

## Skelbraith
*Lords of the Free Sky, The Unbound • Trade is free, but so is treachery*

*“You cannot own the wind. You can only dare to ride it.”*

The Skelbraith are the unbound lords of Orimond’s ports, tide-roads, and free waters, infamous sailors, pirates, smugglers, shipwrights, raiders, and private captains who reject any authority that tries to own the sea. Once called Sablemarchers by outsiders because of their great rogue harbor, they now carry the older, sharper name Skelbraith, a name tied to salt, treachery, impossible crossings, and black sails on the horizon. They are not driven by greed alone. They believe freedom must be seized personally, defended constantly, and never entrusted to crowns, admiralties, guilds, or laws. Where others build walls, the Skelbraith build ships, escape routes, and reputations that outlive wreckage.

#### Origin
___
The true origin of the Skelbraith is disputed, especially among the Skelbraith themselves. Most scholars place their emergence along storm-battered coasts and liminal harbors where the Throne of Ambitions presses thinly against the open sea, turning motion, desire, danger, and defiance into a self-reinforcing lineage. Skelbraith tradition claims they were once ordinary dockfolk, fishers, wreckers, and shiphands who refused the rule of landbound powers, choosing tide over tax, sail over chain, and open water over obedience. Whether this change was natural, Dream-shaped, or deliberately cultivated matters little to them. The sea accepted them. That is enough.

#### Appearance
___
Skelbraith are Medium humanoids with compact, powerful builds adapted for balance, endurance, and sudden movement on wet decks, rigging, docks, and heaving hulls. Their skin ranges through cool mineral and storm tones such as muted blue, slate gray, salt-cyan, ash-steel, and weathered blue-black, often marked by windburn, rope scars, sun-faded patches, or discoloration from salt, tar, and lantern smoke. Their primary eyes are sharp and alert, while a small third eye rests in the center of the forehead, often hidden beneath hair, bandannas, hats, goggles, or weather gear. When opened, this third eye contracts like a gem-bright aperture, sharpening focus during navigation, boarding, cannon-fire, storm-reading, or threat assessment. Their clothing is practical and close-fitted: layered canvas, oiled leather, reinforced cloth, belts, sashes, sea-boots, gloves, rigging hooks, and gear that must justify its weight aboard ship.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Skelbraith culture is anarchic, but never mindlessly disordered. They reject centralized authority, inherited rank, naval law, port monopolies, and imposed tribute, yet they organize fiercely around skill, reputation, crew loyalty, and the unwritten Law of the Free Waters. A docked ship is a caged beast. Worth comes from the hands, not the birth. To steal from a tyrant is justice. Betrayal is expected, incompetence is unforgivable, and freedom is treated as both birthright and burden. Their alliances shift like tide and weather, but crew-bonds can be stronger than blood. A Skelbraith may lie, steal, boast, and vanish, yet still die rather than abandon a shipmate to the deep.

#### Societal Roles
___
Across Orimond, Skelbraith serve as captains, sailors, smugglers, blockade runners, pirates, privateers, shipwrights, caulkers, rope-makers, dock scouts, wreck-divers, boarding specialists, harbor spies, salvage crews, and pilots through reefs, fogbanks, and hostile waters. They dominate routes that no crown can fully police and specialize in moving cargo, people, secrets, weapons, and forbidden goods through ports where official trade fails or becomes a leash. Some are pirates in every sense. Others are free traders, rebel suppliers, rescue crews, coastal raiders, or master shipbuilders who sell hulls to anyone brave enough to sail them. Their reputation depends less on legality than competence. A Skelbraith who brings the ship home survives the song.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Skelbraith names are short, sharp, and often earned through reputation rather than inherited quietly at birth. Given names include Rax, Vex, Korr, Jett, Strann, Vrik, Xeyl, Zyra, Kael, Mira, Sarn, Lexis, Brekk, and Orza. Surnames, ship-names, and self-styled titles are drawn from vessels, storms, raids, wrecks, reefs, sea-beasts, and narrow escapes, such as Stormborn, Ironwake, Cloudpiercer, Driftfang, Blackwake, Skyflame, Stormhowl, Daggerfall, Redmast, Keelbreaker, Saltfang, Reefcut, Tarhand, and Last Mooring. Names change with reputation, and this is considered honorable. A captain who survives a legendary wreck may take the wreck’s name. A traitor may have their name stripped from every crew-song.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Skelbraith cluster around Sablemarch, the great rogue port that gave them their former common name: a sprawling maze of docks, shipyards, black-market piers, salvage cranes, taverns, ropewalks, drydocks, hidden coves, floating warehouses, and armed harbor towers. Sablemarch has no true ruler. It survives through mutual threat, shared dependence on ships, and the simple truth that no inland power can hold a harbor whose people know every current, sewer outlet, reef, and fog route better than the occupying soldiers. Beyond the port, Skelbraith appear wherever trade lanes, embargoes, naval patrols, and desperate coastlines meet open water. To authorities, they are pirates and destabilizers. To besieged towns, rebels, fugitives, and merchants trapped by monopoly, they are the only passage left.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Skelbraith means leaning into mobility, audacity, seamanship, showmanship, and a personal code of freedom. You thrive when the deck is slick, the law is slow, the harbor is watched, and the safest route belongs to someone who charges too much. Decide what ship, crew, wreck, betrayal, debt, port, or unfinished voyage shaped you, and what kind of authority you will never bow to again. Skelbraith suit rogues, fighters, rangers, bards, artificers, swashbucklers, monks, and any character built around movement, deception, shipcraft, navigation, boarding actions, or social nerve. Your strength lies in acting before permission can be denied. A Skelbraith does not ask whether the harbor master allows departure. They ask whether the tide is turning.

#### Skelbraith Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Charisma score increases by 1.

**Age.** Skelbraiths mature quickly, reaching adulthood around 16 years of age. Few live past 60, though this has less to do with frailty than with altitude, betrayal, engine failure, bad weather, and the habit of choosing danger before obedience.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Third Eye Focus.** Once per long rest, open your third eye for 1 minute. You have advantage on Perception checks and checks related to airship piloting, navigation, or targeting. While it is open, you may reroll one failed Dexterity saving throw.

**Enhanced Mobility.** You ignore movement penalties from difficult terrain. You have advantage on Acrobatics checks involving balance, climbing, or aerial maneuvers.

**Aerial Reflexes.** Reduce falling damage by an amount equal to five times your level. You can jump 10 feet further than normal. You can stand from prone using only 5 feet of movement.

**Natural Showmanship.** Gain proficiency in Persuasion or Deception. You can mimic voices and accents you have heard.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Thornkin
Thornkin are living children of the Verdant Cradle, beings of bark, vine, root, thorn, and sap who walk in shapes that only partly resemble flesh. Their bodies change with season, injury, soil, and light, blooming, hardening, shedding, or sleeping according to rhythms older than stone. Some remain in deep groves and cradle-wilds, while others were taken, displaced, or stranded in the cities of Orimond, where their roots search for life beneath pavement and iron. A Thornkin carries the patience of growing things and the quiet threat of nature denied too long.

#### Origin
___
The Thornkin first emerged in the Verdant Cradle, where life is not merely abundant but sovereign. They grew from ancient root systems, awakened groves, blood-fed gardens, and places where memory passed through soil instead of speech. Some were shaped naturally by the Cradle’s will, while others were cultivated by forgotten rites or called into motion when forests needed hands, eyes, and voices. In later ages, many Thornkin were uprooted by trade, conquest, experimentation, or planar accident, leaving them to survive far from the living networks that once sustained them.

#### Appearance
___
Thornkin appear as humanoid figures grown from bark, vines, roots, foliage, moss, flowers, and thorned growths. Their skin may resemble pale wood, dark bark, green stems, dry bramble, or wet root, often split with seams of sap rather than blood. Leaves, petals, fungi, seedpods, or twisting branches may grow from their shoulders, spine, hairline, or limbs, changing with age and season. Their eyes are often dark, amber, green, or luminous like light through leaves. When wounded, they seep resin or sap, and when still, they can be mistaken for carved wood, overgrowth, or a shrine reclaimed by nature.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Thornkin identity is rooted in cycles: growth, dormancy, flowering, decay, and return. They value patience, mutual dependence, memory of place, and the understanding that survival does not always mean motion. Many think of themselves through groves, seed-lines, seasons, or the land that first called them awake rather than through blood family. Displaced Thornkin often carry a deep ache for soil that knows their name, while urban Thornkin learn to treat cracks in stone, abandoned lots, rooftop gardens, and sewer moss as fragments of sanctuary. To them, nature is not peaceful. It is persistent.

#### Societal Roles
___
Thornkin commonly serve as grove-wardens, herbalists, boundary-keepers, root-speakers, wildland scouts, living shields, seasonal oracles, and caretakers of damaged ecosystems. In cities, they may become gardeners, reclamation workers, healers, smugglers of rare seeds, protectors of forgotten green spaces, or quiet saboteurs against industries that poison land beyond recovery. Their endurance and regenerative nature make them formidable defenders, but many prefer prevention over violence. When they do fight, they rarely do so in haste. A Thornkin’s wrath is slow to rise, but once rooted, it is difficult to remove.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Thornkin names often come from plants, seasons, growth patterns, old groves, or the circumstances of their awakening. Some use soft, natural names such as Briar, Rowan, Alder, Moss, Veyra, Lethwyn, Thistle, or Willowmere, while others bear harsher names tied to thorns, scars, or survival, such as Blackroot, Sapscar, Ironbloom, Winterthorn, Deepbark, or Redvine. Names may change after hibernation, fire, pruning, transplantation, or flowering. A Thornkin living among other peoples may adopt a simple spoken name while keeping a deeper root-name shared only with trusted companions or the land itself.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Thornkin exist uneasily among stone, steel, smoke, and regulated gardens. Some live in green districts, temple groves, rooftop orchards, and reclaimed ruins where roots can still reach water. Others wander the concrete wilderness, drawn to neglected parks, cracked foundations, drainage channels, and abandoned lots where wild growth survives without permission. They are often valued for healing, cultivation, and ecological repair, yet feared when their presence exposes how fragile urban control truly is. A Thornkin in the city is never entirely alone; somewhere beneath the pavement, something is still growing.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Thornkin means leaning into patience, endurance, and the tension between rootedness and displacement. Decide what kind of environment shaped you: an ancient grove, a violent garden, a city crack, a sacred marsh, or a place that no longer exists. Your character may be gentle, alien, protective, stubborn, or quietly furious at what civilization calls progress. In play, Thornkin suit druids, rangers, clerics, wardens, fighters, and any character built around resilience, healing, terrain, and seasonal change. Your presence asks a simple question: what will grow after the walls fall?

#### Thornkin Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Thornkin mature slowly, reaching adulthood around 30 years of age. Most live between 200 and 300 years, though ancient Thornkin rooted in old forests, ruin-groves, or deep Verdant places may endure far longer.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Tyrikai
The Tyrikai are small, sharp-eyed survivors descended from the ancestral stock of the Pykari, shaped by the cruel landscapes of Maligath rather than the open roads of Orimond. Where the Pykari became wanderers of omen, flame, and motion, the Tyrikai remained behind in a hellish realm of ash, hunger, predation, and hostile powers far larger than themselves. They are quick, wiry, pragmatic, and difficult to kill, thriving in the spaces between stronger peoples who mistake dominance for permanence. A Tyrikai does not survive by ruling the wasteland. They survive by understanding when to hide, when to bargain, when to bite, and when to vanish.

#### Origin
___
The Tyrikai descend from the same ancient root as the Pykari, before that lineage split across realms and destinies. When some of their ancestors wandered outward, others remained in Maligath, adapting over generations to its scorched valleys, predatory ruins, bitter wells, and endless conflicts between powers that barely noticed them. Life in Maligath rewarded speed, caution, salvage instinct, and peripheral awareness. Their bodies grew smaller and leaner, their senses widened, and their culture became one of movement, scavenging, negotiation, and refusal to die for someone else’s war.

#### Appearance
___
