Tyrikai are Small humanoids, usually standing between 3’5” and 4’5”, with lean, wiry bodies built for sudden motion and narrow escapes. Their skin ranges from dark red and rusted crimson to deep maroon, often roughened by heat, dust, old scars, and survival marks. Their eyes are slightly outward-set, giving them a wide field of vision, and commonly appear amber, gold, violet, or ember-brown. Their faces are sharp and slightly elongated, with visible fangs and narrow jaws suited to quick, defensive violence. Hair is usually short, wiry, and practical, in shades of black, dark brown, ash-copper, or soot-red. Their posture tends low and ready, as if every room might become a hunting ground.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Tyrikai culture is built around survival without surrender. They do not romanticize battle, conquest, or martyrdom, viewing such things as luxuries for larger peoples with more bodies to spend. Their settlements are temporary, hidden, and designed to be abandoned quickly. Trade, salvage, memory of safe routes, and careful reading of danger matter more than territory or grandeur. They value cunning, restraint, quick hands, and the humility to flee before pride becomes fatal. Among them, courage is not standing your ground against a monster. Courage is returning with food, medicine, and everyone still breathing.

#### Societal Roles
___
Tyrikai commonly serve as scavengers, scouts, trap-finders, tunnel runners, salvage brokers, spies, guides, poison tasters, night-watchers, and intermediaries between dangerous factions. Some become merchants who specialize in dealing with creatures much larger and more powerful than themselves, using flattery, deception, and practical value to survive negotiations that would destroy a less careful people. Others become shadow hunters or blade-bartered raiders, striking only when the advantage is absolute. In Maligath, the Tyrikai are often dismissed as lesser by dominant powers, yet they remain long after stronger banners burn.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Tyrikai names are short, sharp, and practical, meant to be spoken quickly and remembered under pressure. Given names often have hard consonants or clipped endings, such as Vrek, Xarr, Jal, Mesk, Tharn, Seka, Yza, Lyska, Nith, Oris, and Tazka. Surnames and bynames usually refer to survival traits, scars, professions, or hard-won reputations, such as Redsight, Hollowfang, Dustborn, Sharproot, Tradechaser, Clawbroker, Silentstep, or Ashweaver. A Tyrikai may change names after escaping death, betraying a patron, surviving captivity, or crossing into a new territory where old debts must be left behind.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Tyrikai are rare and often misunderstood, mistaken for Pykari, goblinoids, fiends, or refugees from some unnamed ashland. Those who settle in the mortal world gravitate toward markets, undercities, dock districts, caravan yards, and places where salvage, barter, and quick movement can become a living. They rarely trust permanent safety, even when offered it, and many keep escape routes, hidden stores, and alternate identities out of habit. To Orimond’s powerful, a Tyrikai may seem insignificant. To those who know better, they are valuable guides to Maligath’s logic: never assume the largest creature in the room is the one most likely to survive.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Tyrikai means embracing speed, caution, opportunism, and survival intelligence. You are not built to win fair fights, and you likely consider fair fights a trap invented by fools. Think about what your character escaped, what they learned to scavenge, and which larger power once underestimated them. A Tyrikai can be cowardly, brave, charming, ruthless, or deeply loyal, but their instincts are practical before heroic. In play, they suit scouts, rogues, rangers, merchants, spies, negotiators, and anyone who survives by reading danger before it arrives. Your greatest strength is knowing that outlasting the powerful is its own kind of victory.

#### Tyrikai Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Tyrikai mature quickly, reaching adulthood around 12 years of age. Most live between 70 and 100 years, though few lives in Maligath pass without scars, fever, hunger, or ash marking them long before age does.

**Size.** Small

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Umbranauts
*Veilfarers • Every road exists, if you know where to breathe*

*“The Veil is not exile. It is infrastructure.”*

The Umbranauts are a people native to the Veil, the transitory expanse that envelops Orimond and connects distant lands and planes. Where most species treat planar travel as rare or dangerous, Umbranauts live within it as naturally as others live on land or sea. They are widely known as guides, navigators, and transporters, offering passage across continents and between realms with calm efficiency and practiced care.

#### Origin
___
Umbranauts evolved within the Veil itself, a space where matter thins and distance loses meaning. Their physiology depends on particulate matter present only within the Veil, making long-term exposure to Orimond’s atmosphere dangerous or fatal. Rather than retreat entirely, they developed sealed traversal suits that allow limited interaction with the Mortal Plane. These suits are not symbols of exile, but tools of trade and survival, as commonplace to them as boots or cloaks are to others.

#### Appearance
___
Without their suits, Umbranauts possess smooth, pale bodies with subtle contours and large, dark eyes adapted to low-contrast environments. Their features are soft and symmetrical, lacking strong pigmentation or body hair. When traveling in Orimond, they wear fully enclosed veilsuits made of layered fabrics, sigil-stitched membranes, and reinforced helms. The suits are light-colored and practical, designed to circulate Veil particles and prevent atmospheric contamination. Decorative markings indicate family lines, routes mastered, or contracts fulfilled.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Umbranaut culture is built around movement, reliability, and trust. They value punctuality, clarity of agreement, and mutual respect between traveler and guide. Unlike many planar species, they are openly social and cooperative, preferring stable trade relationships over secrecy or mystique. Identity is often tied to routes traveled and services rendered rather than place of birth.

#### Societal Roles
___
Most Umbranauts work as Veil navigators, transporters, couriers, or logistical coordinators. They maintain stable passageways used by merchants, diplomats, and adventurers. Some serve as permanent intermediaries between distant cultures, while others specialize in dangerous or unstable crossings. A small number settle near Veil-access hubs in Orimond to manage contracts and waystations.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Umbranaut names are short, breath-soft, and designed to remain clear through veilsuit filters, sealed helms, and the muffled acoustics of planar crossings. Given names favor open vowels, soft consonants, and clipped shapes, such as Aesh, Vire, Luma, Kael, Thren, Oru, Senn, Isha, Vael, Nesh, and Thala. Family names exist, but they are rarely used outside intimate settings. In public life, an Umbranaut is usually known by a route-name earned through passages mastered, crossings survived, or travelers safely delivered, such as Crosswind, Longwake, Silver Span, Hollow Reach, Pale Crossing, Stillroad, Veilcut, Bright Interval, Salt-to-Star, Third Gate, White Span, or Near-Distance. Formal introductions often combine both, as in Vire of Longwake or Aesh of the Hollow Reach, because a route-name is more than reputation. It is proof that others trusted you with the distance between worlds.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Umbranauts are familiar figures near planar gates, arcane ports, and trade cities. They are generally well-liked and trusted, though their suits and breathing needs mark them as perpetually foreign. Extended stays require frequent returns to the Veil to replenish vital particulates, making permanent residence rare but not unheard of.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Umbranaut emphasizes mobility, awareness, and negotiation. You are comfortable navigating unfamiliar places and cultures, and you think in terms of routes and connections rather than borders. Roleplay often involves professionalism, friendliness, and an instinctive sense of distance, timing, and safe passage rather than secrecy or aloofness.

#### Umbranauts Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Umbranauts mature at roughly the same pace as humans, reaching adulthood in their late teens. Most live between 120 and 160 years, though their health depends on regular exposure to the Veil and the particulate matter their bodies require.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft

**Veil-Dependent Physiology.** You cannot breathe Orimond's atmosphere without a veilsuit. While suited, you are immune to suffocation and airborne toxins.

**Veil Step.** Once per short rest, you can teleport up to 10 feet to an unoccupied space you can see.

**Planar Navigator.** You have advantage on checks related to navigation, planar travel, or locating passageways.

**Transitional Awareness.** You cannot be surprised while conscious.

**Professional Courtesy.** Gain proficiency in Persuasion or Insight (your choice).

**Safe Passage.** Allies within 5 feet of you have advantage on saving throws against environmental hazards caused by planar instability.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Unfaceted
*The Faceless, The Unremembered • When the world looks away, we remain.*

*“We are not hidden. We are no longer permitted to be seen.”*

The Unfaceted are a people whose identity was stolen so completely that reality refuses to resolve their faces. When someone looks at an Unfaceted, the mind attempts to assemble familiar features and fails, leaving blur, smear, censoring, or glitch-like distortion. They are not invisible and not intangible. They are present, audible, and physically real, but recognition slides off them like water off glass.

#### Origin
___
The Unfaceted were once a named people with coherent lineage and history. Millennia ago, during a conflict that crossed planes and dream-architectures, their collective identity was targeted instead of their bodies. Their names were stripped from memory, record, and myth at the same time. They survived, but the world lost the ability to represent them as individuals. Over generations, the effect stabilized into a persistent perceptual failure centered on the face, and into a cultural adaptation built around living without external validation.

#### Appearance
___
An Unfaceted body is fully humanoid and physically consistent, but their face cannot be described reliably. Observers report painterly blur, missing features, smeared bands, static-like tearing, or soft censoring where eyes, nose, and mouth should be. The distortion varies by viewer and by moment. Attempts to draw, photograph, scry, or magically record an Unfaceted face produce warped or corrupted results. Many Unfaceted dress with deliberate asymmetry, layered collars, veils, hair framing, and strong silhouettes, not to conceal the face, but to give perception something stable to anchor onto.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Unfaceted culture is built around autonomy and absence. Names are treated as tools, chosen lightly and changed when life changes. Reputation is distrusted because it tends to become a hook that others can pull. They value memory, but prefer shared experience and oral witness over formal archives. Many believe fixation on permanence invites erasure. Community exists, but rarely through centralized institutions. Instead, they form small circles, traveling compacts, and caretaker enclaves in places already frayed.

#### Societal Roles
___
Unfaceted commonly become wayfinders through unraveling realms, caretakers of abandoned planes, intermediaries where identity is dangerous, scouts and witnesses who cannot be reliably traced, and residents of places other peoples will not remain. They avoid roles that demand public recognition, but thrive in work that requires discretion, endurance, and comfort in instability.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Unfaceted names are self-assigned and transient. Given names are often short and functional, and may be replaced after major events. Examples: Ash, Null, Echo, Reed, Solace, Veil, Static, Mira. Some adopt descriptive bynames such as Quiet-Step, Before-Name, or Of-No-Face. Some abandon names entirely while traveling through high-risk regions.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Unfaceted drift toward forgotten districts, sealed transit layers, condemned infrastructure, and neighborhoods that have fallen out of administrative focus. People may speak with them and remember the conversation but fail to recall the face. Records misfile easily, guards forget having checked them, and witnesses struggle to describe them in detail. This makes them valuable to certain institutions and dangerous to others.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing an Unfaceted means navigating a life without easy recognition. You may feel relief at being untraceable, or grief at being unremembered. You are comfortable in effrited places and uneasy in centers of curated identity. Consider what you do with the freedom of being hard to define, and what it would cost if someone truly saw you clearly.

#### Unfaceted Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Wisdom score increases by 2, and your Dexterity score increases by 1.

**Age.** Unfaceted mature at roughly the same pace as humans, reaching adulthood in their late teens. Most live between 120 and 150 years, though some are said to endure longer in places where names, records, and fixed identities lose their hold.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Perceptual Veil up to 60 feet

**Faceless Cognition.** Creatures have disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks to identify you from visual description, sketches, or secondhand accounts.

**Slip in Recall.** After a creature speaks with you for at least 1 minute, it must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw (DC 8 + your proficiency bonus + your Wisdom modifier) or forget one noncritical visual detail about you for 24 hours.

**This Is Not A Face.** Once per long rest, when you are targeted by an attack you can impose disadvantage on that attack as the attacker’s perception stutters.

**Unravel Wayfinder.** You have advantage on Survival and Investigation checks to navigate, map, or interpret unstable, effrited, or unraveling environments and planar anomalies.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice
You may choose up to 1.0 exotic language instead

## Vaelari
*The Veil-Touched, Children of the Second Sight • Thought shapes reality, and reality listens.*

*“We do not hear voices. We hear echoes that have not yet learned silence.”*

The Vaelari are a reclusive and enigmatic people, marked by violet skin and an ever-present psychic resonance. Descended from the Aestari yet profoundly altered by generations of exposure to psychic currents and paranormal forces, they walk the edge between mind and matter. To most folk of Orimond, the Vaelari feel unsettling not because they are hostile, but because they seem to know things that have not yet been spoken.

#### Origin
___
The Varnhallans arose in the shadow of ancient stoneworks and buried foundations left by the Moeder, an extinct precursor people whose ruins still shape parts of Orimond. Though the Moeder vanished long ago, their legacy lingers in Varnhallan resilience, structural instinct, and almost bodily understanding of load, stress, and support. Early Varnhallan communities settled among these remnants, adapting them into furnace-halls, citadels, foundries, and defensible settlements of fire and iron. Over generations, they became a people who do not merely inhabit structures. They inherit, test, rebuild, and strengthen them.

#### Appearance
___
Vaelari possess smooth, purple-hued skin ranging from pale lavender to deep amethyst. Their eyes are large and dark, often entirely black or softly glowing with inner light when focused. Facial features are fine and elongated, with minimal body hair and slender frames. Many Vaelari exhibit subtle signs of psychic activity, such as faint motes of light drifting near their temples, a soft hum in the air around them, or shadows that move a heartbeat out of sync.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Vaelari society values perception, restraint, and mental discipline. Emotion is not suppressed, but studied, understood, and guided. They believe that unchecked thought can wound the world as surely as steel. Personal identity is fluid, shaped by memory, vision, and shared psychic experience rather than rigid hierarchy. Privacy of thought is sacred, and violating another’s mind is considered one of the gravest taboos.

#### Societal Roles
___
Vaelari most often serve as seers, psychic mediators, scholars of the unseen, and wardens of anomalous sites. Some act as advisors to rulers who dare to consult them, while others wander Orimond investigating disturbances of mind, dream, or spirit. A rare few become battle-psions, turning focused will into devastating force when restraint fails.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Umbranaut names are short, breath-soft, and shaped to remain clear through veilsuit filters, pressure membranes, and distorted planar acoustics. Given names often favor open vowels, soft consonants, and clipped endings, such as Aesh, Vire, Luma, Kael, Thren, Oru, Senn, Vael, Iri, Nesh, and Thala. Family names are less important than route-names, which are earned through passages mastered, crossings survived, or contracts fulfilled. Examples include Crosswind, Longwake, Silver Span, Hollow Reach, Pale Crossing, Stillroad, Veilcut, Bright Interval, Salt-to-Star, and Third Gate. Formal introductions often include both name and route, as in Vire of Longwake or Aesh, keeper of the Hollow Reach. Among Umbranauts, a route-name is more than reputation. It is proof that others trusted you with the distance between worlds.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In the mortal world, Vaelari communities are small and intentionally distant, often built near places of psychic resonance or thin Veil boundaries. They are tolerated, sometimes sought out, and occasionally feared. Daily life requires constant mental grounding, as the psychic noise of dense cities can be overwhelming. Many Vaelari leave their enclaves only briefly, returning once their senses grow strained.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Vaelari means leaning into awareness, restraint, and internal conflict. You may sense truths others ignore, struggle with intrusive visions, or feel responsible for dangers no one else perceives. Consider how your character balances empathy with detachment, and whether they fear losing themselves to the thoughts they touch.

#### Vaelari Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Vaelari mature at a pace similar to humans but often live up to 120 years, though intense psychic strain can shorten or unpredictably extend their lifespan.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Psychic Sensitivity.** You have advantage on Insight checks and saving throws against being charmed.

**Mind Whisper.** You can communicate telepathically with a creature you can see within 30 feet.

**Veil Awareness.** You can sense active psychic or paranormal effects within 30 feet.

**Focused Will.** Once per long rest, you have advantage on one Intelligence or Wisdom saving throw.

**Mental Discipline.** You have resistance to psychic damage.

**Echo of Thought.** Once per long rest, you may reroll a failed mental ability check.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Varnhallan
*Ironborn of Varnhallow • What endures is what is forged.*

*“Stone remembers. Steel obeys.”*

The Varnhallans are the ironborn of Varnhallow, a people shaped by labor, heat, stone, and unrelenting purpose. Born in furnace-cities, mountain holds, and forge-settlements, they thrive where others falter, treating smoke, pressure, exhaustion, and danger as part of the work rather than reasons to stop. They are builders, wardens, smiths, and survivors, less concerned with conquest than with making things that endure. To a Varnhallan, progress is not declared. It is forged, tested, repaired, and struck again until it holds.

#### Origin
___
Varnhallians arose in the shadow of ancient stoneworks and forgotten foundations once raised by the Moeder, an extinct precursor race. Though the Moeder are long gone, fragments of their legacy linger in Varnhallian resilience and instinctive understanding of structure and load. Over generations, the Varnhallians became a people of foundries, citadels, and deep halls, adapting Moeder remnants into living cities of fire and iron.

#### Appearance
___
Varnhallans are broad-shouldered, dense of build, and visibly hardened by labor and environment. They usually stand between 5’6” and 6’6”, with grounded posture, heavy hands, thick arms, and bodies that seem braced even at rest. Their skin ranges from ash-pale and smoke-gray to burnished bronze, iron-brown, or ruddy forge-dark tones, often roughened by calluses, scars, heat exposure, and old work injuries. Their eyes frequently carry metallic hues such as steel-gray, copper, dark iron, or ember-gold, catching light like polished ore. Hair is thick, coarse, and usually dark, worn short or tightly bound to keep clear of tools, stone dust, and flame.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Varnhallan culture values duty, endurance, and proven skill above reputation or inheritance. Words are treated as raw ore until work gives them weight. Tradition matters, but only if it survives testing; anything untested remains suspect, no matter how ancient. They believe structures, tools, plans, and people must be stressed to reveal their worth, and that failure is acceptable only when studied, repaired, and remembered. Their independence often reads as stubbornness, but to them it is responsibility. A thing that holds only because someone else commands it was never strong to begin with.

#### Societal Roles
___
Varnhallans commonly serve as smiths, masons, siege engineers, heavy infantry, wardens of fortified cities, ruin-keepers, toolwrights, bridge-builders, and defenders of mountain holds. In war, they form the unyielding core of defensive lines, holding gates, walls, and chokepoints long after retreat would be reasonable. In peace, they build and maintain what other peoples rely on but rarely understand: walls, aqueducts, locks, foundries, arsenals, roads, and deep foundations. They are often called when something must hold under pressure, whether that thing is a fortress, a treaty, a weapon, or a failing city.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Varnhallan names are short, heavy, and practical, made to be spoken clearly in forge-halls, barracks, quarries, and storming yards. Given names include Rurik, Bran, Durn, Othar, Kaela, Brenna, Harn, Vorka, Mael, Sigrun, Tova, and Keld. Surnames often reference craft, material, endurance, or defensive works, such as Stoneforge, Emberhand, Ironvein, Deepwall, Hammerfall, Gatebraid, Ashmantle, Steelroot, Blackkiln, and Holdfast. Earned names may be added after a siege, masterwork, collapse survived, or oath kept under impossible pressure.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Varnhallans gather in fortified districts, forge-settlements, mountain holds, industrial wards, military foundries, and old Moeder-adjacent ruins where craft and defense are inseparable. In mixed societies, they are valued as infrastructure keepers, siege experts, builders, and reliable defenders, but often distrusted for their stubborn independence and refusal to flatter fragile authority. Their neighborhoods tend to be functional, reinforced, and loud with work: hammer-song, stone-cutting, bellows, shouted measures, and the dull rhythm of things being made to last. When a Varnhallan district goes silent, something is wrong.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Varnhallan means leaning into discipline, resilience, craft, and the refusal to yield before the work is done. You may be a defender, mason, smith, soldier, ruin-warden, siege engineer, or practical wanderer seeking materials, methods, or lost Moeder secrets. Think about what you have built, what you failed to hold, and what test you believe will reveal your true worth. Varnhallans suit fighters, paladins, artificers, clerics, rangers, and any character built around defense, tools, structure, endurance, and deliberate action. Your strength lies in consistency rather than flourish. When others retreat, you brace.

#### Varnhallan Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Strength score increases by 1.

**Age.** Varnhallians reach adulthood around 20 years of age and often live up to 120 years. Their lives are shaped by labor, pressure, heat, and craft, so age is measured as much by what they have built and endured as by the years behind them.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 25ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Forge Endurance.** Once per long rest, reduce damage taken by 1d12 + Constitution modifier.

**Structural Instinct.** You have advantage on checks to assess fortifications, buildings, or stonework.

**Heat-Hardened.** You have resistance to fire damage.

**Immovable.** You have advantage on saving throws against being pushed or knocked prone.

**Tool Proficiency.** Proficiency with Smith’s Tools or Mason’s Tools.

**Last to Yield.** When reduced to 0 HP but not killed outright, you drop to 1 HP instead (once per long rest).

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Veilborn
Veilborn are fragments of existence left half-resolved by the Emergence, people and anomalous consciousnesses that entered the world incompletely and never fully settled into reality. Their bodies flicker between flesh, mist, static, and absence, giving them an unsettling presence even when they stand in plain sight. They are neither ghosts nor living mortals in the usual sense, but something caught between manifestation and erasure. To institutions, they are anomalies to classify, contain, or exploit. To those who live in forgotten districts and unstable places, they are quiet survivors who know the cracks of the world better than anyone.

#### Origin
___
No one chooses to become Veilborn. Some were people who manifested incorrectly during the Emergence, arriving with missing anchors, duplicated echoes, or bodies that reality could not fully hold. Others appear to have coalesced from stray memory, failed possibility, or consciousness left behind in the Veil. Their origins vary, but all share the same wound: existence accepted them only partially. Since then, they have persisted in the margins of Orimond, drawn to anomaly zones, sealed passages, abandoned infrastructure, and places where the boundary between presence and absence has already grown thin.

#### Appearance
___
Veilborn are humanoid, but rarely stable in the way other peoples are. Their skin is often translucent, pale, or smoke-dark, threaded with spectral veins that shimmer like static under dim light. Their eyes may appear as empty voids, washed-out lights, or unfocused hollows that absorb more than they reflect. Voices often layer faintly, as if the same sentence were being spoken from several moments at once. Some Veilborn cast weak shadows, leave no fingerprints, blur in mirrors, or appear corrupted in recordings. Even when solid, they seem slightly misaligned with the world around them.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Veilborn culture is fragmented by necessity, since they rarely form large settlements or stable institutions. Identity among them is shaped by anchoring: names, repeated habits, chosen companions, objects of memory, or rituals that help them remain coherent. They value privacy, patience, and the right to exist without explanation. Many distrust authorities that treat anomaly as property, pathology, or threat. Among themselves, they distinguish between different kinds of instability, such as those who drift, those who hollow, and those who eclipse from perception. Survival often means learning what keeps you present, and what makes the world forget you.

#### Societal Roles
___
Veilborn often become scouts, infiltrators, memory-readers, guides through anomaly zones, occult witnesses, couriers, and keepers of forgotten routes. Their unstable nature makes them difficult to track, difficult to confine, and unusually suited to work in places where normal bodies and records fail. Some serve underground networks as unseen messengers or wardens of abandoned passages, while others are coerced by corporations, governments, or occult orders seeking to weaponize their condition. A Veilborn’s value often comes from the same quality that makes others fear them: sometimes they are present exactly where no one expects presence to be possible.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Veilborn names are often chosen after manifestation, especially when old names feel incomplete, dangerous, or no longer true. Some keep ordinary names as anchors to the life they remember, while others adopt short symbolic names such as Static, Vale, Echo, Null, Flicker, Haze, Wisp, or Trace. Bynames often refer to the nature of their instability, such as Twice-Spoken, Mirrorless, Hollow-Step, Afterimage, Wallpasser, or Seen-Then-Gone. A Veilborn may change names when their form shifts, when memories return, or when an old identity begins to fade beyond recovery.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Veilborn live where the city’s certainty breaks down: sealed transit layers, anomaly-scarred districts, abandoned towers, forgotten maintenance corridors, and neighborhoods where records no longer agree with the streets. They are often treated as problems before they are treated as people, studied by institutions, avoided by the cautious, and quietly hired by those who need access to places no ordinary body can reach. Some Veilborn build small anchor-communities around shared rituals, safe rooms, memory objects, and people who can remember them clearly. Others remain solitary, moving through the city as witnesses to everything Orimond discards, hides, or fails to fully erase.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Veilborn means leaning into instability, secrecy, and the question of what makes a person real when the world struggles to hold them. You might be eerie, gentle, detached, bitter, curious, or fiercely protective of anyone else treated as an anomaly. Think about what anchors your character: a name, an object, a routine, a person, a place, or a memory that may not be entirely yours. In play, Veilborn excel as infiltrators, scouts, occult investigators, messengers, and liminal guides, but their strongest roleplaying hook is presence under threat: the ongoing effort to remain seen, remembered, and self-defined.

#### Veilborn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Charisma score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Veithyn
The Veithyn are dwellers of the shadowed border, a people shaped along the outer reaches of Nevermourn where darkness presses close to the Mortal Plane without fully consuming it. They are neither creatures of pure shadow nor ordinary mortals, but something held in the dusk between presence and oblivion. Their grace is quiet, their movements unsettling, and their silence often feels like the pause before a storm. Outsiders fear them for their closeness to Nevermourn, but the Veithyn understand themselves as borderfolk: those who live where the dark begins, and who know which shadows must be watched.

#### Origin
___
The Veithyn arose along the borderlands of Nevermourn, in regions where reality thins, light bends, and the surface of the Realm of Shadows brushes against the world without swallowing it whole. Their oldest settlements were built along rifts, black valleys, and twilight thresholds where other peoples could not remain for long. Legends speak of a silent pact with Nevermourn itself, an accord that allows the Veithyn to endure the dark without unraveling into it. Whether this pact was blessing, curse, ancestral bargain, or survival instinct refined over generations, the Veithyn still honor it through vigilance, restraint, and careful movement between worlds.

#### Appearance
___
Veithyn are tall, refined humanoids, usually standing between 5’8” and 6’6”, with long athletic frames and features that seem drawn slightly toward shadow. Their skin ranges from pale gray and dusk-blue to deep charcoal or obsidian black, often traced with visible black veins that pulse faintly near Nevermourn-touched places. Their faces are elongated and elegant, with high cheekbones, narrow jaws, and abyss-dark eyes that shift subtly in dim light. Their hair appears soft and smoke-like, flowing, curling, or drifting as though stirred by unseen air. At the edges of perception, a Veithyn’s outline may flicker or blur, giving the impression that the world has not fully decided where they end.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Veithyn culture is built around balance, vigilance, and the discipline of living beside an abyss without worshipping it. They do not view darkness as evil, but as a force that must be understood, negotiated with, and contained. Their settlements are often built from dark stone quarried near rifts, shaped into quiet halls, watchtowers, shadowed gardens, and sanctuaries where light is used sparingly and with intent. Many Veithyn belong to traditions such as Duskwardens, Shroudcallers, or Umbradancers, each reflecting a different relationship with the border: guarding it, studying it, or moving through it. Their greatest fear is forgetting that the dark is never merely beautiful. It is patient.

#### Societal Roles
___
Veithyn commonly serve as border wardens, scouts, shadow-mystics, rift watchers, night guides, infiltrators, scouts, occult scholars, and hunters of things that slip out of Nevermourn. Duskwardens patrol thresholds and ruined passes, ensuring that what belongs beyond the border remains there. Shroudcallers study shadow as substance, language, and warning, preserving lore that most peoples are too afraid to name. Umbradancers move between darkened spaces with unsettling speed, serving as messengers, spies, duelists, or assassins when necessity demands it. In mixed societies, Veithyn are often consulted when darkness behaves strangely, though few are invited to stay once the problem is solved.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Veithyn names are soft-spoken and weighted with history, often designed to be carried in whispers rather than proclaimed in crowds. Given names include Myris, Vaelith, Xiren, Tythos, Eska, Khaelis, Zoryn, Lysara, Veidra, Raleth, Nyra, and Osveth. Lineage names may preserve old houses or border settlements, such as Vaelros, Nythis, Kaeloris, Zhenkar, and Veyrith. Other surnames reference shadow, twilight, silence, or echoes, such as Duskwind, Nightborn, Shadowcrest, Emberveil, Ebonwhisper, Murkmourn, Silenshade, Blackrift, and Gloamwatch. A Veithyn may earn an additional title after surviving a crossing, sealing a breach, or returning from a place where their shadow did not follow.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Veithyn are rare but recognizable, often found near old rifts, shadowed borders, Nevermourn-facing ruins, night markets, sealed archives, and cities built too close to places where light behaves incorrectly. They are treated with caution, reverence, or superstition depending on local history. Some serve as hired scouts, wardens, occult advisors, or guides through dangerous darklands, while others live quietly in twilight districts where lanterns are hooded and windows face away from the deepest shadows. Their presence often reassures those who understand their work and unsettles those who prefer to believe the border guards itself.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Veithyn means leaning into restraint, grace, shadow, and the tension of belonging to the edge rather than the center. Decide how your character relates to Nevermourn: guardian, scholar, exile, hunter, mystic, or one who hears the dark calling more clearly than they admit. You may be calm, eerie, compassionate, severe, secretive, or quietly burdened by what you have seen beyond the light. Veithyn suit rogues, rangers, monks, warlocks, clerics, fighters, and wizards built around stealth, darkness, perception, mobility, and liminal magic. Your strength is knowing that shadow is neither refuge nor enemy. It is a border, and borders must be kept.

#### Veithyn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Velthask
The Velthask are living monuments of dominion, regal beings of Maligath whose presence turns ambition into hierarchy. Towering, immaculate, and impossible to ignore, they carry themselves as if every chamber were already a throne room waiting to acknowledge them. They do not see power as something requested, borrowed, or justified through sentiment. Power is a condition of being, proven through command, self-mastery, endurance, and the refusal to kneel. To meet a Velthask is to feel that the world has briefly arranged itself around a center.

#### Origin
___
The Velthask arose in Maligath, where ambition, pride, law, and violence harden into living structures. In that harsh realm, survival alone was insufficient. Those who endured had to impose shape on chaos, building citadels, courts, trade houses, and ritual hierarchies strong enough to withstand betrayal and ruin. Over generations, the Velthask became self-maintaining creatures of rule, their bodies preserving themselves against wear as their societies refined domination into ceremony. They claim they were born to govern Maligath as it should be. Their rivals usually hear only the threat in that claim, but the Velthask hear destiny.

#### Appearance
___
Velthask are imposing Medium humanoids, standing between 6’5” and 8’0”, with rigid posture, commanding silhouettes, and bodies that seem carved for authority. Their skin resembles petrified gold, polished brass, deep ivory, or darkened electrum, flawless yet organic, with a natural carapace that appears both protective and ceremonial. Their eyes are opaque gemstone-like orbs, often ruby, sapphire, onyx, amber, or emerald, glowing faintly without pupils. Many lack hair, instead developing metallic ridges, cranial crests, hornlike crowns, or spine-like protrusions along the skull and shoulders. Their hands are broad and long-fingered, capable of delicate courtly gesture or crushing force. Every movement is controlled, deliberate, and meant to be seen.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Velthask culture is founded on hierarchy, grandeur, and the doctrine that rule must be embodied before it can be exercised. They respect law, but only law strong enough to survive challenge. They respect authority, but only authority that proves itself worthy of obedience. Their courts are full of ritual challenge, public declaration, formal rivalry, and precise etiquette, since every gesture communicates rank. A Velthask does not kneel unless absolutely defeated, and even then the act is remembered as a wound to the self. They are rarely concerned with good or evil as moral categories, preferring questions of strength, legitimacy, order, and recognition.

#### Societal Roles
___
Velthask most often become monarchs, magistrates, warlords, lawgivers, trade sovereigns, court arbiters, military patrons, oath-binders, and architects of political order. Some rule cities directly, while others dominate through contracts, vassalage, inherited claims, or carefully controlled commerce. Gilded Warlords assert authority through military excellence, Crowned Orators through law and declaration, and Ivory Regents through the sheer gravity of sovereign presence. Even those without a throne tend to organize the world around themselves, turning parties into courts, companies into retinues, and disputes into opportunities for recognition.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Velthask names are proclamations, meant to be spoken with weight and remembered as claims. Given names are bold, severe, and resonant, such as Xyrran, Daeloris, Tharnith, Vorzhal, Krymion, Veska, Myrthys, Yzra, Zhaelis, Oromis, Vhaldran, and Serathys. Lineage names often preserve dynastic force, such as Krynnith, Zalvrynn, Vhoris, Tyrmoth, Odrakhal, and Xalvorn. Title-names are common and may replace surnames entirely, especially after conquest, succession, or public victory. Examples include Crownforged, Stoneborne, Gildedblade, Ironregent, Thronewake, Lawmantle, Scepterhand, and Unbowed. A Velthask who loses status may be stripped of titles, a humiliation often treated as worse than injury.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Velthask are rare, watched, and politically dangerous. They gravitate toward courts, embassies, merchant houses, military orders, fortified estates, and places where law can be turned into leverage. Their presence in a city often creates immediate tension, because they instinctively seek hierarchy even in cultures built around negotiation or shared authority. Some become valued administrators, commanders, or diplomats, especially where crisis demands decisive leadership. Others are distrusted as would-be tyrants carrying Maligath’s logic into mortal politics. A Velthask in Orimond rarely blends in. Even in exile, they look like someone waiting for the room to recognize its ruler.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Velthask means leaning into command, pride, ceremony, and the tension between legitimate authority and naked domination. Decide what throne, office, army, court, or principle your character believes they are owed, and what they would never lower themselves to do. You may be honorable, ruthless, protective, arrogant, visionary, or terrifyingly disciplined, but your presence should carry consequence. Velthask suit paladins, warlocks, fighters, bards, clerics, sorcerers, and nobles built around command, intimidation, law, social dominance, and battlefield control. Your central question is whether you rule to impose order, to satisfy pride, or because you truly believe no one else can bear the crown.

#### Velthask Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Charisma score increases by 2, and your Strength score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Vessels
The Vessels are living constructs, designed rather than born, shaped by forgotten makers for war, labor, worship, knowledge, containment, or purposes no surviving tongue can name. They are relics that learned to continue after command ended. Some are elegant works of sacred craft, others crude frames of stone, metal, ceramic, bone, wood, or rune-bound flesh, but all carry a core of awareness that persists beneath damage, age, and abandonment. A Vessel was built to serve a function. What makes them dangerous, tragic, and remarkable is that many now choose to exist beyond it.

#### Origin
___
Vessels were created by many hands across many ages: divine artisans, vanished empires, occult engineers, desperate war-priests, eldritch architects, and civilizations now known only through ruins. Some were soldiers made for wars that ended before memory. Some were caretakers for temples without worshippers. Others were built as archives, executioners, guardians, or prisons for things their makers lacked the courage to destroy. Their creators are gone, silent, or unwilling to claim them. What remains is the Vessel, walking through a world that may fear its construction while depending on the endurance it was given.

#### Appearance
___
Vessels vary widely in form, but most possess humanoid frames built from durable materials such as stone, metal, ceramic, glass, hardwood, ivory, organic composites, or strange matter from older realms. Their bodies may be sleek and symmetrical, heavy and brutalist, cracked and repaired, or layered with plating, cords, seals, and embedded relics. Glowing veins, runic channels, maker’s marks, geometric inscriptions, or exposed cores often reveal the force that animates them. Many have no true face, instead bearing carved masks, blank visages, hinged plates, luminous eye-slits, or shifting symbols where expression should be. Damage rarely makes a Vessel look wounded in the mortal sense. It makes them look historical.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Vessels do not share a single culture, since they were made by different peoples for different reasons. Instead, they share a common question: what remains when purpose becomes choice? Some cling to their original function, finding comfort in duty. Others reject it entirely, treating obedience as the first prison they escaped. Many search for records of their makers, lost companions, unfinished commands, or the meaning of the core that grants them awareness. Among themselves, Vessels often show unusual patience, recognizing the difference between a tool, a relic, and a person can take centuries to understand.

#### Societal Roles
___
Vessels are often drawn, or pushed, into roles that echo their designs. Wardens become guards, sentinels, investigators, and protectors of forbidden places. Executioners become soldiers, bounty hunters, duelists, or feared champions. Oracles become scribes, witnesses, archivists, translators, and keepers of impossible memory. Binders become prison-keepers, curse-bearers, exorcists, or living seals. In Orimond, some are revered as holy relics, others studied as artifacts, and others hunted by those who want to disassemble, replicate, or command them. A Vessel’s usefulness is obvious. Their personhood is where the argument begins.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Vessel names are often adopted rather than inherited. Some use maker designations, serial marks, or sacred titles, such as Unit Seven, Gatehand, Reliquary-Third, Ash Warden, or Archive Vessel Ios. Others choose personal names after awakening to selfhood, favoring simple names that can be spoken without command, such as Cal, Oren, Sava, Thal, Iri, Voss, Nema, or Edrin. Many carry function-names or earned titles, such as Hollow Key, Bright Core, Stone Witness, Last Blade, Sealed Mercy, Iron Psalm, or Bell-Without-Tower. Changing one’s name is often a major act of self-definition, especially for a Vessel abandoning its original purpose.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Vessels appear in ruins, temples, battlefields, sealed archives, noble collections, mage laboratories, guild vaults, and city streets where no one can agree whether they are citizens, property, relics, or threats. Some serve openly as guards, scholars, laborers, or envoys, while others hide their cores from scavengers and artificers eager to harvest old craft. Institutions value them for endurance and memory, but that value often carries danger. A Vessel in Orimond must often prove they are more than the object others see. Every contract, friendship, and oath becomes a test of whether they are being recognized or merely used again.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Vessel means exploring purpose, autonomy, memory, and the uneasy boundary between tool and person. Decide what you were built for, whether that function still defines you, and what part of your design you fear others might activate, exploit, or misunderstand. You may be solemn, curious, dutiful, rebellious, gentle, terrifying, or quietly fascinated by ordinary life. Vessels suit fighters, paladins, artificers, clerics, warlocks, wizards, monks, and any character tied to endurance, lost history, ancient technology, divine craft, or sealed horrors. Your central question is simple: were you made to contain a soul, or did one grow inside you anyway?

#### Vessels Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Constitution score increases by 2, and your Intelligence score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.**

## Vexholmic
*Sons and Daughters of War • Discipline is survival.*

*“Strength is trained. Mercy is chosen.”*

The Vexholmics are a disciplined and battle-shaped people, raised in fortress cities and forged by generations of organized conflict. Though they share distant ancestral roots with the Delvani, centuries of martial culture, harsh training, and relentless warfare have reshaped them into a people defined by control, endurance, and tactical clarity.

#### Origin
___
The Vexholmics trace their lineage to early Delvani offshoots who abandoned subterranean industry for surface strongholds and mercenary service. Over time, constant warfare, selective breeding, and cultural pressure transformed them into a distinct people whose societies revolve around preparation for conflict rather than survival through labor.

#### Appearance
___
Vexholmics are compact, dense humanoids with hardened physiques and angular features. Their skin is thick and resilient, often bearing tones of ash, bronze, iron-gray, or scarred red. Facial structures are ridged and pronounced, with reinforced brows and cheekbones. Their eyes are sharp and predatory, commonly silver, iron-blue, crimson, or onyx. Hands are calloused with reinforced knuckles, and many display hardened nails adapted for combat and weapon handling.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Vexholmic culture values discipline, hierarchy, and tactical excellence above all else. Personal worth is measured through endurance, loyalty, and proven capability under pressure. Emotion is controlled, not suppressed, and expressions of strength are expected to be deliberate rather than explosive. Honor is earned through action, not speech.

#### Societal Roles
___
Vexholmics commonly serve as soldiers, mercenaries, tacticians, bodyguards, siege specialists, and military instructors. Some become strategic advisors or commanders, while others are sold as elite contract forces to foreign powers. Civilian roles exist but are always secondary to martial readiness.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Vexholmic names are short, forceful, and utilitarian. First names are often one or two syllables, while surnames reference lineage, battlefield deeds, or martial virtues. Titles earned in battle frequently replace family names.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Vexholmics are often found in fortified districts, mercenary enclaves, or serving as hired protectors for powerful factions. They integrate efficiently into militarized societies but struggle in places that value diplomacy over preparedness.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
As a Vexholmic, you excel through preparation, positioning, and controlled aggression. Roleplay a character who values order, assesses situations quickly, and acts decisively. You may struggle with impulsive allies but respect those who prove themselves through action rather than words.

#### Vexholmic Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Vexholmics mature by 15 and rarely live beyond 80 years due to constant exposure to warfare.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Built for War.** You have advantage on saving throws against being knocked prone or stunned.

**Tactical Reflexes.** Once per short rest, you can take the Dodge action as a bonus action.

**Hardened Frame.** You have resistance to nonmagical bludgeoning damage.

**Combat Adaptation.** Once per long rest, when you take damage, you gain temporary hit points equal to half your level (minimum 1).

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Vitrexin

Etherblood are engineered people whose blood contains refined alchemical narcotics prized by elites.

Created through artificer biomancy and alchemical engineering.

Etherblood culture is shaped by ownership contracts escape networks and coded self identity.

#### Societal Roles

Often kept as assets courtesans controlled labor or black market resources.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Names include serial markers compound references or reclaimed personal names.

#### Life in Orimond
___
Life in Orimond is dangerous for Etherblood due to exploitation regulation and trafficking.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
