## Vok
*Furnacekin, Ember-Blooded • “The fire remembers.”*

*“Stone cracks. Steel bends. Fire endures.”*

The Vok are dense, heat-bearing keepers of Cinderhold, a people whose bodies store warmth, steady flame, and release power with deliberate restraint. Though they bear traces of Dren ancestry, the Vok have become something distinct: not ash-walkers or hearth-keepers, but living vessels of furnace-heat, ember-current, and volcanic pressure. They are practical, grounded, and deeply intolerant of waste. Where the Cindralis shape fine works with patient hands, the Vok tend the deep fires and hidden flows that keep Cinderhold alive.

#### Origin
___
The Vok emerged from Dren-descended communities that settled near Cinderhold’s volcanic roots, forge-vaults, lava channels, and deep heat shrines. Generations of life among controlled flame, pressure-stone, conductive ores, and bound elemental currents changed them into natural heat vessels, able to gather, hold, and release thermal force through body and craft. Their ancestors endured fire as a condition of the world. The Vok learned to make fire into duty. Over time, they formed a close alliance with the Cindralis, who refine delicate works above while the Vok maintain the furnaces, vents, bellows, and emberworks below.

#### Appearance
___
Vok are Medium humanoids, usually standing between 5’8” and 7’0”, with dense, stocky builds shaped by heat, pressure, and efficient movement. Their skin ranges from deep bronze and rusted iron to coal-gray, dark umber, and volcanic black, often glowing faintly along seams, vents, or pulse-lines when they carry excess heat. Their eyes shine in molten gold, ember-orange, coal-red, or storm-blue, flickering subtly with exertion or stored power. Hair is often short, bristled, and metallic in texture, resembling scorched wire, cooled filament, or fine strands drawn from ore. Their hands are thick-fingered but precise, with subtle heat vents along the knuckles, palms, or wrists.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Vok culture is built around stability, efficiency, maintenance, and controlled release. Waste is treated as both practical failure and moral failing, whether in flame, metal, labor, speech, anger, or time. They respect systems that hold under pressure and people who improve what they inherit rather than merely complain about its flaws. Their communities are orderly and interdependent, with status earned through reliability, calibration, and calm during crisis. A Vok who keeps a forge-vault from bursting, a lava gate from failing, or a furnace district from freezing is honored more deeply than one who wins glory in a duel.

#### Societal Roles
___
Vok commonly serve as furnace-keepers, emberwrights, forge wardens, vent-stabilizers, lava-channel tenders, pressure-stone masons, elemental binders, smiths, kiln masters, and guardians of deep volcanic works. Pyroconductors specialize in flame handling, heated metals, and forge-side labor. Arcvolt Technicians become storm-channelers, rune-current readers, and handlers of lightning-bound devices. Magma-Bound Sentinels guard crater roads, deep heat wells, and unstable volcanic passages. In Cinderhold, the Vok are the quiet force beneath the city’s craft, keeping bellows breathing, lifts moving, gates sealed, baths warm, kilns steady, and foundries alive.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Vok names are firm, heavy, and structured, often carrying thermal, mineral, or craft associations. Given names include Jorrek, Durnis, Malrik, Vethan, Tormek, Xyra, Othiel, Rhenka, Talyis, Vezna, Korrun, Braska, and Voltan. Surnames and earned names often reference heat, ore, deep craft, or service to the furnaces, such as Heatbinder, Coilbrand, Emberforge, Voltshard, Ironcurrent, Gearstrike, Sparkgrind, Thermoset, Furnacehand, Deepcoil, Current-Keeper, and Ashcircuit. A Vok may gain a new name after calming a runaway forge, surviving an ember surge, repairing a deep vent, or saving a district from fire, smoke, or cold.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Vok are most common in Cinderhold, forge districts, volcanic settlements, mountain foundries, deep halls, and cities that depend on controlled heat for survival. They are respected for competence, though outsiders often mistake their economy of speech and motion for coldness. Vok quarters are warm, reinforced, and practical, built around shared furnaces, stone vents, tool alcoves, heat baths, emergency shutters, and communal workshops. They are often called when a kiln fails, a mine grows too hot, a forge spirit becomes unstable, or a city’s hidden heatworks begin to falter. When the deep fires misbehave, people send for a Vok.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Vok means leaning into discipline, technical insight, controlled force, and the belief that survival depends on systems that hold. Decide what kind of power your character understands best: forge-fire, volcanic pressure, storm-current, rune-craft, or the quiet authority of keeping others warm and safe. You may be pragmatic, stern, protective, dryly funny, proud, or obsessed with eliminating waste wherever you find it. Vok suit artificers, fighters, wizards, clerics, rangers, and any character built around tools, fire, lightning, endurance, craft, or hazardous environments. Your strength is controlled output: knowing when to store heat, when to release it, and when to close the vents before everything burns.

#### Vok Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Vok mature around 25 and can live 200–300 years, though many choose to work until their bodies finally fail.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Fire-Tempered.** Resistance to fire damage.

**Dren Legacy.** Advantage on saving throws against exhaustion and environmental heat.

**Forge Insight.** Proficiency with smith’s tools or mason’s tools.

**Living Furnace.** Ignore penalties from extreme heat environments.

**Enduring Frame.** Once per long rest, reduce incoming damage by an amount equal to proficiency bonus.

**Ember Memory.** Advantage on checks related to ancient structures, forges, or volcanic sites.

**Languages.**

## Vorraki
*Oathbound Enforcers, Architects of Force • They built a world where we take orders.
We built a culture where we take care of our own.*

*“Strength without discipline is noise. Discipline without strength is a lie.”*

The Vorraki are the shackled titans of Orimond, a people of fortified enclaves, disciplined armies, and controlled violence. Their nations are rarely vast, but they are feared far beyond their borders, for a Vorraki host can decide the fate of wars larger realms are too proud to fight honestly. They are soldiers, tacticians, shield-bearers, siege-breakers, and oath-bound contractors whose military strength is bought, leased, negotiated, or pledged under strict terms. They were not made to serve. They built societies where force is organized, priced, restrained, and remembered.

#### Origin
___
The Vorraki arose in harsh borderlands and contested marches where survival required more than strength. It required formations, supply lines, discipline, and the ability to turn limited territory into unbreakable defense. Over generations, Vorraki clans consolidated into small martial nations, fortress-states, and contract-holds whose value lay in trained force rather than fertile land or imperial reach. Their history is full of sieges, defensive pacts, mercenary charters, and wars fought under foreign banners for Vorraki gain. Outsiders often call this selling themselves. Vorraki call it sovereignty by other means.

#### Appearance
___
Vorraki are tall, powerful humanoids, usually standing between 6’0” and 7’2”, with dense musculature and an imposing, tactical presence. Their builds are broad and heavy without being clumsy, shaped for impact, endurance, and controlled violence. Skin tones range from charcoal and iron-brown to deep bronze, ash-gray, basalt-blue, and dark umber, often marked by scars, service tattoos, campaign brands, or battle honors. Their faces are strong and severe, with heavy brows, broad jaws, flattened or boar-like noses, and elongated upper canines that may remain visible even when the mouth is closed. Their eyes are often dark, reflective, or stone-like, giving their stare an unreadable weight.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Vorraki culture is built around martial sovereignty. They value discipline over fury, formation over individual glory, tactics over bravado, and national memory over personal vanity. Their societies are organized through war-councils, fortress houses, officer lineages, shield-companies, and oath-charters that define when, where, and for whom Vorraki force may be used. A contract is not a chain if it is negotiated from strength, and a campaign is not shameful if it feeds the hold, strengthens the people, and preserves independence. Uncontrolled violence is despised. War is a craft, and craft requires restraint.

#### Societal Roles
___
Vorraki commonly serve as professional soldiers, shield-captains, siege engineers, heavy infantry, war advisors, border wardens, military governors, fortress quartermasters, drillmasters, and commanders of leased companies. Their small nations often export military strength through carefully written charters, sending companies to fight in foreign wars while retaining command structures, cultural law, and rights of withdrawal. Some Vorraki become independent mercenary lords or military envoys, while others remain in their homeland training the next generation. In Orimond, to hire Vorraki is expensive. To betray their terms is catastrophic.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Vorraki names are short, hard, and practical, suited to shouted commands, shield-line calls, and campaign records. Given names include Blaze, Kray, Roka, Brunt, Vex, Daro, Strix, Maul, Tasha, Varn, Zera, Nok, Grath, Orra, and Korr. Company names and campaign titles often function as surnames, earned through deeds, defeats, victories, or formations served. Examples include Ironshade, Grudgeborn, Tenback, Deadright, Haulmark, Onechain, Gatehand, Bloodbrace, Stonejaw, Lastwall, Breakline, Red Phalanx, Black Standard, and Third Shield. A Vorraki may change titles after joining a new company, surviving a failed campaign, breaking a siege, or returning home with honor intact.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Vorraki are encountered as embassy guards, chartered companies, military advisors, fortress delegates, leased regiments, and disciplined foreign hosts camped outside city walls under negotiated terms. Their nations may be small, but few powers treat them lightly. Vorraki troops are hired to hold borders, break sieges, protect trade roads, suppress monsters, reinforce failing armies, or tip the balance in conflicts where local soldiers cannot be trusted. Their presence in a city is both reassurance and threat: someone has paid for order, and the terms of that order are written somewhere in Vorraki hands.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Vorraki means leaning into disciplined might, martial professionalism, and the politics of force under contract. Decide what hold, company, campaign, defeat, or charter shaped you, and whether you fight for homeland, coin, oath, honor, leverage, or survival. You may be protective, intimidating, strategic, blunt, honorable, ruthless, patriotic, or deeply suspicious of rulers who spend soldiers like loose copper. Vorraki suit fighters, paladins, barbarians, rangers, clerics, warlords, and any character built around command, protection, intimidation, formation tactics, and controlled violence. Your strength is not merely that you can fight. It is that your people made war into policy and survived by setting the terms.

#### Vorraki Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Vorraki reach maturity at 16 and live up
to 80 years, though many die young in the
brutal world of Concord City.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** You can see in dim light within 60 feet
as if it were bright light, and in
darkness as if it were dim light.

**Relentless Endurance.** When reduced to 0 HP but not killed outright, you drop to 1 HP instead (once per long rest).

**Brute Precision.** When making a Strength (Athletics) check, you may double your proficiency bonus (once per short or long rest).

**Calculated Violence.** Add your Strength modifier to initiative instead of Dexterity.

**Commanding Presence.** Gain proficiency in Intimidation or Persuasion (your choice).

**Tactical Efficiency.** You can use the Help action as a bonus action.

**Commanding Voice.** Gain proficiency in Insight.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Teleryn
The Teleryn are the nomad cousins of the Vorraki, broad-bodied warrior clans who move with herds, wagons, forgebeasts, and contract-banners across Orimond’s harsher roads. Where the Vorraki built small martial nations and leased disciplined armies, the Teleryn kept to clan routes, selling their strength as escorts, sellswords, caravan guards, monster-hunters, and battlefield auxiliaries. They are often mistaken for brutal raiders by those who judge only their tusks, weapons, and size. In truth, most Teleryn are deeply practical and surprisingly peaceful, preferring paid service, negotiated passage, and herd-life over conquest.

#### Origin
___
The Teleryn share ancient kinship with the Vorraki, descending from the same broad martial stock that learned to survive through strength, cohesion, and tactical discipline. Where the Vorraki settled into fortress-states and military charters, the Teleryn followed the open routes, adapting to migration, seasonal hardship, and the care of powerful companion beasts. Their clans grew around motion rather than borders, carrying portable forges, ancestral weapons, herd rites, and contract customs from one region to another. They became warriors for a price because war found the roads anyway, and because a paid blade can choose its terms more freely than a conscripted one.

#### Appearance
___
Teleryn are powerful humanoids with heavy frames, thick limbs, and dense musculature suited to travel, labor, and sudden violence. They are often shorter and more compact than Vorraki, but broader through the chest, neck, and shoulders, with low, grounded stances shaped by long marches and mounted life. Their skin commonly ranges from rust-red, clay-brown, burnt ochre, and dark umber to charcoal-black or weathered bronze, often marked by travel scars, clan tattoos, sun-darkening, and ritual ash. Many have broad noses, heavy brows, large expressive ears, and prominent tusks that curve upward or outward from the jaw. Their hair is usually coarse and dark, worn in braids, knots, shaved patterns, or practical cuts that show clan marks and travel status.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Teleryn culture is built around matriarchal clans, contract law, road survival, and careful stewardship of useful creatures. Their small societies are led by elder women, herd-mothers, forge-matrons, route-keepers, and contract-speakers, whose authority comes from judgment, continuity, and the ability to keep the clan fed, paid, sheltered, and together. Strength is respected, but needless violence is considered wasteful, since every injury weakens the whole camp. Teleryn travel with bonded beasts such as Heart-Fur Yakul, which warm winter camps, and Ember-Crete Forgebeetles, which serve as mobile forges. These creatures are companions, tools, and clan obligations, cared for with the same seriousness as weapons, children, and elders.

#### Societal Roles
___
Teleryn commonly serve as sellswords, caravan guards, beast-handlers, outriders, camp wardens, contract duelists, mobile smiths, monster hunters, road negotiators, and mercenary auxiliaries. In battle, they are valued for discipline, endurance, and the ability to operate far from supply lines by relying on clan logistics and beast-supported camps. Outside war, they escort pilgrims, protect merchant roads, repair tools and armor, broker safe passage, and manage traveling markets. Their best warriors are not reckless berserkers, but professionals who know when violence is worth the price and when a strong campfire, a fed beast, and a signed agreement will solve more.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Teleryn names are bold, practical, and often tied to clan routes, beasts, contracts, or deeds of protection. Given names tend to be short and forceful, such as Brak, Torga, Vesh, Ruun, Ogra, Hettel, Marn, Korga, Daska, Voln, Shura, and Tek. Clan names often reference animals, weather, roads, or camp traditions, such as Heartfur, Redtusk, Yakul-Road, Forgebeetle, Ashhide, Longhorn, Embercart, Stormcamp, Ironmane, or Warmback. Earned names may mark a fulfilled contract, saved herd, winter crossing, or battle survived, such as Keeps-the-Line, Beetlefriend, Snow-Warder, Paid-in-Steel, Hearth-Tusk, or Three Roads Home.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Teleryn clans are most often seen at caravanserais, border markets, winter passes, mercenary yards, pilgrimage roads, and temporary camps outside cities that prefer their protection more than their presence. They arrive with beasts, wagons, portable shrines, hides, tools, and contract poles hung with tokens of completed service. Some cities hire them seasonally to guard routes or reinforce militias, while rural communities value them as traders, smiths, and monster deterrents. Teleryn rarely settle permanently, but their camps can become familiar landmarks, returning year after year with the same songs, beasts, debts, and warnings from the road.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Teleryn means leaning into strength without cruelty, professionalism without servility, and the deep bonds of clan, contract, and companion creatures. Decide what your character travels with, such as a winter beast, forgebeetle, riding animal, hunting bird, pack lizard, or ancestral wagon, and what contract or clan obligation brought them into adventuring life. You may be peaceful until paid to fight, gentle with animals but terrifying with enemies, practical in negotiation, or deeply proud of never breaking terms. Teleryn suit fighters, rangers, barbarians, paladins, druids, beast masters, and any character built around road-life, protection, mercenary ethics, animal handling, and mobile survival. Your strength lies in knowing that a blade is only one tool among many, and usually the loudest one.

#### Teleryn Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Teleryns reach maturity at 16 and live up
to 80 years, though many die young in the
brutal world of Concord City.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** You can see in dim light within 60 feet
as if it were bright light, and in
darkness as if it were dim light.

**Languages.**

## Wesftilestes
*Keepers of the Hidden Tapestry • Knowledge must be guided, or it will unravel the world.*

*“Reality is not broken. It is unfinished.”*

The Weftislestes are the keepers of the hidden tapestry, scholars and arcanists born with an instinctive awareness of the Weft, the underlying lattice through which magic, matter, memory, and possibility are quietly threaded. To most peoples, reality is a surface to be survived. To the Weftislestes, it is a pattern to be read, preserved, and, when necessary, rewritten. Their home city of Erelis is one of Orimond’s great academic citadels, devoted to anomaly study, tesseral magic, and the dangerous art of seeing too much. A Weftislestes does not merely ask what is true. They ask what structure allowed truth to appear.

#### Origin
___
The Weftislestes arose in Erelis, where generations of scholars, mages, archivists, and anomaly-watchers lived under sustained exposure to tesseral forces. Over time, this study changed them. Children were born with eyes that followed invisible correspondences, minds that sorted memory into layered structures, and bodies subtly aligned to arcane geometry. Some claim the first Weftislestes were ordinary mortals who studied the Weft until the Weft began studying them in return. Others believe Erelis was founded where the hidden lattice of existence had already frayed, and the Weftislestes are simply the people who learned to survive in that knowledge.

#### Appearance
___
Weftislestes appear humanoid, but their bodies carry mesmerizing signs of hidden geometry. Their skin shifts subtly under different light, ranging from opalescent ivory and pale lapis to star-flecked gray, nebular blue, or iridescent copper, sometimes patterned with faint tessellations that seem to align with an unseen grid. Their pupils may appear as spirals, fractals, or shifting angular forms, while their irises shimmer as though perceiving several layers of reality at once. Their hair often seems woven with refracted light, fine filaments, or spectral strands, in shades of nebula black, glacial silver, mirror-white, deep indigo, or luminous lavender. Their shadows sometimes ripple a heartbeat out of sync, and strong emotion may leave brief afterimages behind them.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Weftislestes culture is built around intellectual discipline, controlled inquiry, and the careful curation of dangerous knowledge. They believe knowledge must be guided, tested, and contextualized, because an unbound truth can distort the mind as surely as a spell can distort flesh. Their central philosophy, the Tesseral Code, teaches that perception is only the first veil, that the Weft is deeper than appearance, and that anything unraveled may also be rewritten. Erelis prizes discovery, but secrecy is woven into its institutions as tightly as learning. To be Weftislestes is to inherit both wonder and restraint: the hunger to know, and the fear of what knowing can loosen.

#### Societal Roles
___
Weftislestes most often serve as arcanists, anomaly scholars, tesseral architects, archivists, investigators, spell theorists, ritual geometers, memory cataloguers, and advisors on unstable magical phenomena. Echelon Weavers study the Weft as doctrine and structure, preserving established theory. Lattice Shapers apply tesseral principles to wards, architecture, movement, and spatial manipulation. Riftcallers push the boundaries of accepted research, sometimes becoming visionaries, sometimes disasters with tenure. Outside Erelis, Weftislestes are sought for their ability to interpret anomalies, decode impossible ruins, stabilize magical disturbances, and identify patterns that other scholars mistake for chaos.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Weftislestes names are elegant, structured, and often built from repeating or fractal syllables intended to echo scholarly lineage, personal discipline, or arcane specialization. Given names include Serathis, Kaedrin, Tholmir, Xelros, Ormari, Vaelren, Iskalia, Saeryn, Lysithea, Xyrelle, Vesmira, and Thessa. Family names and scholarly names often reference the Weft, academic houses, or theoretical traditions, such as Tesserval, Lyramir, Echoris, Mystran, Orristhar, Codex, Archivis, Threnis, Evenshade, and Thaelrun. Formal introductions may include a field, thesis, or academy affiliation, especially within Erelis, where a name without intellectual context is considered incomplete.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Weftislestes are most visible in Erelis, but their influence reaches far beyond its lecture halls, libraries, observatories, and sealed laboratories. They are called to investigate anomalous landscapes, advise courts on magical disturbances, inspect impossible architecture, and contain phenomena that ordinary mages can only describe as wrong. Their reputation is double-edged. Many admire their insight, precision, and breadth of learning, while others distrust their secrecy and fear that Erelis studies problems it should leave buried. A Weftislestes abroad is often treated as both scholar and warning sign, because their arrival suggests that reality has developed a pattern worth worrying about.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Weftislestes means leaning into intellect, pattern recognition, curiosity, and the ethical tension of knowledge that can reshape the world. Decide what your character studies, what anomaly changed them, and what truth they are tempted to pursue despite warnings. You may be precise, aloof, fascinated, cautious, arrogant, compassionate, or quietly terrified by what you understand. Weftislestes suit wizards, artificers, warlocks, clerics, bards, rogues, and any character built around investigation, arcana, memory, spatial magic, or forbidden research. Your strength lies in seeing the thread before others see the knot, and knowing which one to pull.

#### Wesftilestes Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Wisdom score increases by 1.

**Age.** Weftislestes age slowly, reaching adulthood around 40 years old, with lifespans exceeding 200 years. Their connection to the Weft preserves them, though extended reality manipulations can accelerate or distort aging.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Perception Beyond the Veil.** You can sense nearby magical distortions, invisible creatures, or anomalies within 30 feet, though you do not always understand them. You have advantage on Intelligence (Arcana) and Investigation checks related to Weft anomalies or dimensional fluctuations.

**Weftwoven Memory.** You can recall any event you have personally experienced with perfect clarity, unless your memory has been intentionally altered. You gain proficiency in one Intelligence-based skill of your choice: Arcana, History, or Investigation.

**Tesseral Reflex.** Once per short rest, when a creature makes an attack against you, you can use your reaction to impose disadvantage on that attack as you shift a fraction of a second ahead of impact.

**Fractal Mind.** You have advantage on saving throws against mind-affecting effects, including charm, fear, or confusion.

**Languages.**

## Zakariss
The Zakariss are tyrants of the unstable sky, massive Veil-born conquerors who seek to chain the impossible and make dominion out of drift. Where Umbranauts navigate the Veil and Kerevahn build lighthouses to stabilize its currents, the Zakariss carve territory from living instability, raising war-fortresses, border-fields, and brutal dominions where no fixed land should exist. Their bodies are barely stable, held together by runes, will, and raw Veil pressure. They do not ask the world to make room for them. They force space to obey.

#### Origin
___
The Zakariss emerged within the Veil, in regions where unstable matter, broken distance, and violent possibility condensed into living force. They are not wanderers, guides, or accidental echoes. They are a people born from the refusal to dissolve. Early Zakariss learned to bind their own unraveling bodies with stabilizing sigils, then turned that same craft outward, forcing temporary structures, war roads, and fortress-realms into being. Their long conflict with the Kerevahn is rooted in this difference of purpose: the Kerevahn stabilize passages so others may survive them, while the Zakariss seize Veil cores to anchor conquest.

#### Appearance
___
Zakariss are towering humanoids, often standing between 7’0” and 9’0”, with broad shoulders, heavy limbs, and an unnatural density that makes even their stillness feel violent. Their flesh resembles half-solid war-stone, scarred hide, and Veil matter bound together by pulsing sigils that shift with emotion, strain, and command. Their skin may appear basalt-black, bruised violet, storm-gray, or rune-lit bronze, sometimes cracking with seams of unstable light. Their eyes burn like molten glyphs, and when enraged their jaws may split wider than mortal anatomy should allow, revealing a second row of crystalline Veil-teeth. Their hands are built not merely to crush, but to grip, tear, and shape unstable reality.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Zakariss culture is built around dominion, hierarchy, and the conquest of instability. They reject chaos because chaos wastes power. To them, drift must be seized, weakness must be cut away, and any force that can be shaped has already admitted it can be ruled. Their hierarchy is brutal but direct: those who hold their form, their fortress, and their followers longest command those who falter. Dissolution is not only death, but disgrace. A Zakariss measures identity through territory claimed, enemies broken, sigils earned, and the degree to which reality itself resists their will before yielding.

#### Societal Roles
___
Zakariss most commonly serve as warlords, fortress-builders, Veil conquerors, shock troops, siege-breakers, phase-hunters, spell-renders, and commanders of unstable dominions. Some become core-takers, hunting the resources needed to stabilize their drifting fortresses. Others specialize in breaking teleportation, countering phase-shifts, or anchoring hostile terrain long enough for armies to cross. In mixed realms, they are feared as mercenaries, living weapons, and dangerous specialists against Veil phenomena. They are rarely trusted, but often hired when the problem is too large, too unstable, or too violent for subtler peoples to solve.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Zakariss are not given true names at birth or manifestation. They begin with guttural designations, battle-sounds, or rune-marks such as Zhak, Vross, Khar, Drekh, Uzzor, Thraal, Korrzh, or Mek. A true name is carved through conquest, endurance, and recognition by rivals. Earned names often reference broken horizons, seized cores, shattered gates, or dominions held against dissolution, such as Chainfield, Corebreaker, Rift-Hammer, Fortress-Jaw, Skybinder, Veilcrusher, Black Bastion, Dominion-Fist, or Horizon-Torn. A Zakariss who loses a fortress, dissolves under pressure, or is defeated publicly may have part of their name stripped away.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Zakariss are rare and almost always treated as threats before they are treated as guests. They appear near Veil breaches, unstable battlefields, Kerevahn lighthouse routes, mercenary courts, forbidden military contracts, and places where rulers believe overwhelming force will solve what caution cannot. Their ability to stabilize or shatter Veil effects makes them valuable, but their appetite for control makes every alliance precarious. A Zakariss presence in a city changes the mood of the room: exits are noted, wards are checked, and everyone wonders who was desperate enough to invite one.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Zakariss means leaning into force of will, dominance, unstable embodiment, and the desire to impose order on chaos by strength alone. Decide what your character seeks to claim: a fortress, a name, a lost core, a conquered route, freedom from their hierarchy, or proof that they can exist without ruling. You may be brutal, disciplined, proud, strategic, strangely honorable, or dangerously close to unraveling. Zakariss suit barbarians, fighters, paladins, warlocks, sorcerers, and any character built around resilience, battlefield control, anti-magic pressure, and raw physical presence. Your central tension is whether you master instability, or merely become the loudest expression of it.

#### Zakariss Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Zhimeus
*The Alchemists of Blooming Rot*

The Zhimeus are the alchemists of blooming rot, an ancient people shaped by the toxic abundance of Nhal-Zhym. They are kin to older graceful lineages, but centuries of spore-choked air, fungal medicine, and controlled decay have refined them into something stranger and more resilient. Where others see rot as ruin, the Zhimeus see process: a body becoming material, poison becoming cure, infection becoming knowledge, and death becoming a reagent in the next transformation. They do not fear decomposition. They study it, cultivate it, and make it useful.

#### Origin
___
The Zhimeus arose in Nhal-Zhym, a dangerous land of fungal hollows, toxic wetlands, rot-fields, medicinal molds, and alchemical gardens where survival required more than resistance. It required understanding. Their ancestors adapted slowly to the region’s spores and poisons, learning to filter, ingest, refine, and repurpose what would kill most other peoples. Over generations, this intimacy with decay transformed their bodies, customs, and economy. The Zhimeus became masters of controlled entropy, producing elixirs, antidotes, stimulants, venoms, regenerative salves, and biological wonders from substances no other people could safely touch.

#### Appearance
___
Zhimeus retain a trace of old elegance, but their forms are marked by exposure, refinement, and cultivated decay. They are Medium humanoids, often tall and elongated, with subtly warped proportions, narrow shoulders, and deliberate posture. Their skin commonly appears metallic, fungal, or mineral-stained, ranging from brass, bronze, copper, and oxidized verdigris to pale mushroom-gray or dark tarnished gold. Their faces remain refined, with high cheekbones and long features, though often hollowed, weathered, or softened by spore adaptation. Hair is thin, filament-like, or mycelial, sometimes interwoven with fungal growths, dusted braids, silver webs, or pale tendrils. Their eyes are deep-set and luminous, with bioluminescent flecks suspended like spores in liquid glass.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Zhimeus culture is built around refinement through decay. They believe nothing should be wasted, because all matter is in the process of becoming useful to something else. Corpses, failed crops, spoiled food, infection, venom, and blight are handled with caution, but also with respect as materials in transition. Their society prizes patience, containment, precision, and experimental courage. Sporeweavers study toxins and living chemistry, Rotpriests commune with fungal networks and decomposing matter, while Bonecarvers transform remains into reagents, tools, medicine, or ritual objects. To the Zhimeus, cleanliness means balance and control, not sterility.

#### Societal Roles
___
Zhimeus commonly serve as alchemists, herbalists, poison-handlers, plague wardens, apothecaries, fungal cultivators, rot-chamber keepers, corpse refiners, antidote makers, and makers of rare medicines. Their expertise is indispensable wherever disease, toxin, blight, or contamination threatens ordinary methods. They also supply regulated elixirs, stimulants, anesthetics, biological catalysts, and dangerous reagents to cities, armies, temples, and mage colleges. Outsiders often fear their work, but those same outsiders come begging when a poison has no name, a wound refuses to close, or a field must be saved by understanding the rot within it.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Zhimeus names often reflect ancestry, craft, spore-line, or alchemical discipline. Given names are elegant but slightly sharp in sound, such as Veythis, Xorlan, Thalrin, Jevrak, Mornis, Ithra, Zelis, Xythea, Lirnath, Qemaya, Voriss, and Nhalira. Lineage names may preserve older houses or adapted bloodlines, such as Vhryzhal, Omberis, Kelrith, Nyzareth, Velmyr, and Qorathis. Profession-names and earned titles are common, including Sporeweaver, Rotbinder, Bloomwright, Decayforged, Mold-Sage, Venomglass, Gravebloom, and Verdigris-Hand. A Zhimeus may add a title after developing a cure, surviving a mutation, mastering a rot-field, or refining a substance previously thought unusable.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Zhimeus are most strongly associated with Nhal-Zhym and the trade routes that carry its medicines, toxins, spores, and reagents into the wider world. Their enclaves are carefully regulated, humid, sealed, and thick with the scent of earth, vinegar, medicinal smoke, and living fungus. Outsiders are often quarantined before entering Zhimeus districts, less from hostility than from practical concern. Beyond Nhal-Zhym, Zhimeus are valued as apothecaries, plague consultants, battlefield medics, poison experts, and alchemical specialists, though many communities treat them with suspicion until danger makes their knowledge necessary.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Zhimeus means leaning into precision, patience, controlled danger, and the philosophy that decay is transformation rather than failure. Decide what your character refines: poison, medicine, corpses, memory, fungal life, mutation, or the line between healing and harm. You may be calm, clinical, nurturing, unsettling, curious, devout, or dangerously experimental. Zhimeus suit artificers, druids, wizards, clerics, rogues, rangers, and any character built around alchemy, toxins, medicine, fungi, death rites, or biological transformation. Your strength lies in knowing that what others discard may be the most powerful ingredient in the room.

#### Zhimeus Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** Zhimeus mature at a similar pace to Aestari, reaching adulthood around 80 years of age. Their lifespan is long but unstable, typically 500–700 years, though many succumb earlier due to alchemical exposure, planar degradation, or internal entropy imbalance.

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Withering Adaptation.** You have advantage on saving throws against poison and disease, and you have resistance to necrotic damage.

**Cultivated Decay.** You gain proficiency with Alchemist's Supplies or Herbalism Kit (your choice). You have advantage on Intelligence checks related to alchemy, toxins, fungi, blight, or contaminated environments.

**Alchemical Physiology.** When you spend Hit Dice during a short rest, you may reroll one Hit Die and use the new result.

**Sporesight.** You can sense the presence of disease, poison, rot, or unnatural decay within 30 feet, but not its exact source.

**Echoes of the Aestari.** You have advantage on saving throws against being charmed.

**Refined Entropy.** Once per long rest, you can ignore disadvantage imposed by environmental corruption or blight on one ability check or saving throw you make.

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

## Zyrrkhal
The Zyrrkhal are the still rulers of Maligath, ageless beings of structure, memory, and absolute form. Where the Velthask impose dominion through grandeur and will, the Zyrrkhal embody dominion as permanence: the belief that reality has a correct shape, and that all instability is evidence of lesser understanding. They are not conquerors in the ordinary sense. They do not hunger for novelty, expansion, or applause. They preserve, enforce, and refine what they believe already stands perfected. To a Zyrrkhal, change is rarely progress. More often, it is erosion wearing a flattering mask.

#### Origin
___
The Zyrrkhal arose in Maligath’s oldest fixed places: black citadels, still courts, basalt archives, sealed causeways, and ancient structures that resisted the realm’s violence by refusing to yield. Their earliest histories describe them as guardians of a design they did not create, only inherited and learned to embody. Over generations, or perhaps through rites older than generation itself, their bodies ceased to deteriorate, becoming static vessels of memory and law. Some believe the Zyrrkhal were shaped by Maligath to preserve its first architecture. The Zyrrkhal usually correct this claim. Maligath, they say, was shaped correctly because they remained.

#### Appearance
___
Zyrrkhal are tall Medium humanoids, usually standing between 6’2” and 7’0”, with rigid, sculpted physiques and an unsettling lack of bodily drift. Their skin often resembles polished basalt, pale stone, black marble, cold ivory, dark iron, or ash-gray ceramic, smooth and unblemished in ways that feel deliberate rather than youthful. Their features are symmetrical, severe, and statue-like, with long faces, sharp brows, still mouths, and eyes that appear like fixed glass, obsidian, silver, or dark gemstone. They move with minimal waste, each gesture precise and final. Even their stillness feels architectural, as though the room has adjusted itself around a load-bearing pillar.

#### Culture & Identity
___
Zyrrkhal culture is founded on structure as sacred truth. They believe hierarchy, memory, law, and form are not inventions, but the natural state of existence revealed when chaos is stripped away. Emotion is treated with suspicion, not because it is weak, but because it introduces distortion. Their societies prize endurance, exact record, unbroken offices, and the preservation of patterns across centuries. The Stonelocked guard places and laws through patient immobility. Hollow Scholars interpret the hidden design beneath history and architecture. Black Crowned lineages rule as embodiments of order rather than mere political authorities. A Zyrrkhal does not ask whether a system is kind. They ask whether it holds.

#### Societal Roles
___
Zyrrkhal commonly serve as archivists, magistrates, citadel wardens, pattern-scholars, oath judges, structural advisors, rulers, ceremonial guardians, and keepers of ancient Maligathan law. They are called upon when something must be preserved without compromise: a treaty, a prison, a throne, a lineage, a city plan, a forbidden mechanism, or a truth too dangerous to reinterpret. They rarely hurry and rarely improvise, but their long memory makes them formidable strategists and administrators. Where others see stagnation, they see continuity. Where others see tyranny, they see the cost of preventing collapse.

#### Naming Conventions
___
Zyrrkhal names are formal, heavy, and often unchanged across vast spans of time. Given names tend to sound carved rather than spoken, such as Zyrrath, Kholvren, Azkhyr, Tholm, Veyrkal, Ozhant, Krythis, Malzhor, Iskaryn, and Vhalos. Lineage names often reference stone, crowns, patterns, citadels, or unbroken offices, such as Stonelocked, Black Crown, Hollow Pattern, Basalt Throne, Iron Measure, Stillmantle, Obsidian Law, or Gate-Without-Rust. Titles are frequently more important than personal names, especially among rulers and scholars. A Zyrrkhal may hold the same title for centuries, and losing it is treated less as demotion than as structural failure.

#### Life in Orimond
___
In Orimond, Zyrrkhal are rare, formal, and deeply unsettling to cultures built on negotiation, improvisation, or change. They appear as envoys from Maligath, legal theorists, archive-keepers, oath witnesses, wardens of sealed places, or exiled nobles whose mere presence makes rooms feel more rigid. Courts and institutions value their perfect memory and incorruptible records, but distrust their contempt for compromise. They are most comfortable in fortified embassies, old archives, stone districts, and halls where protocol still carries weight. A Zyrrkhal in Orimond does not adapt quickly, and this is exactly what makes them useful to some and intolerable to others.

#### Playstyle & Roleplaying
___
Playing a Zyrrkhal means leaning into permanence, precision, memory, and the tension between order and life. Decide what structure your character believes must never change: a law, a throne, a city, a vow, a pattern, a prison, or their own self. You may be calm, severe, principled, arrogant, protective, inflexible, or quietly fascinated by mortal unpredictability. Zyrrkhal suit wizards, paladins, clerics, fighters, warlocks, artificers, and any character built around control, memory, investigation, endurance, and resistance to alteration. Your central question is whether you preserve what is necessary, or merely fear becoming something new.

#### Zyrrkhal Traits
___
**Ability Score Increase.** Your Intelligence score increases by 2, and your Constitution score increases by 1.

**Age.** 

**Size.** Medium

**Speed.** Your base walking speed is 30ft

**Vision.** 

**Languages.** You know 2 standard languages of your choice

# Spells

#### Ashen Breath
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You exhale a short-lived plume of gray, acrid smoke that spreads in a 15-foot cone before thinning into nothingness. The vapors sting the throat and seize the breath of those caught within.

Each creature in the area must make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure: The creature chokes on the harsh fumes. Until the start of its next turn, it cannot take reactions.
• Success: The creature resists the irritation and suffers no effect.

The smoke dissipates almost immediately after leaving your lungs, leaving no lingering cloud or obscuration. Creatures that do not need to breathe are unaffected.

#### Blink and You Missed It
*Transmutation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You drift slightly out of step with immediate perception, your presence sliding across awareness without properly settling.

Until the start of your next turn, creatures that visually perceive you struggle to form a stable impression of your presence.

When a creature sees you during this time, it must succeed on an Intelligence check against your spell save DC to consciously register and remember you.

• Failure: The creature notices nothing unusual and does not retain awareness of your presence. It behaves as though you were never observed unless you later interact with it directly.
• Success: The creature perceives you normally and is unaffected by this spell.

The effect immediately ends for a creature if you:

• Attack
• Speak
• Physically interact with it or its environment in an obvious way

This spell has no effect on creatures that rely on non-visual senses to detect you.

#### Cauterize Through Time
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You snap your fingers through tangled chronology, sending a searing ripple into a wound that never had time to close.

Choose one creature within range and make a ranged spell attack. On a hit, the target takes 1d6 fire damage as heat blooms from an impossible instant.

The target must then make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure: The creature has disadvantage on the next Constitution saving throw it makes to maintain concentration before the end of your next turn.
• Success: No additional effect.

The flames manifest as a brief, unnatural cauterization, more like an event imposed upon the flesh than a conventional burn.

#### Ceiling Watcher
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 20.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

A faint, eye-like shape appears upon a ceiling, wall, or corner within range. The illusion is motionless, silent, and incapable of perception. It persists for the duration.

A creature that can see the watcher and is unfamiliar with the spell may use its action to examine the illusion, making a Wisdom (Perception) check against your spell save DC.

• Success: The creature recognizes the watcher as illusory and is unaffected.
• Failure: The creature experiences a subtle but persistent unease while it can see the watcher.

While uneasy, the creature:

• Has disadvantage on its next Stealth check made before the start of its next turn.
• Suffers mild distraction at the DM’s discretion (hesitation, discomfort, brief glances).

This effect ends immediately if the creature interacts with the illusion or no longer sees it.

The watcher produces no light, sound, or other sensory output.

#### Cinder Veil
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 5.0 feet
**Components:** S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

A faint shimmer of drifting embers surrounds you, radiating a fragile warmth that repels the bite of cold.

Until the start of your next turn, the first time you would take cold damage, reduce that damage by 5 (minimum 0).

If you are within an area of magical darkness, the embers glow with a dim, smoldering light. While the veil persists, creatures within 5 feet can clearly perceive your outline.

#### Clockless Chess
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You conjure a small, spectral chessboard in an unoccupied space within range. Translucent pieces manifest upon its surface and begin to move of their own accord, enacting a silent and inscrutable match.

The game progresses without intervention, the pieces shifting with deliberate precision. No matter how long it is observed, the contest invariably concludes in a perfect stalemate.

The board and its pieces are intangible, emit no sound, and provide no strategic insight. Creatures may watch the game, but cannot influence its outcome.

The chessboard vanishes when the spell ends.

#### Conjure Mild Inconvenience
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You summon a trivial but deeply irritating inconvenience to plague a creature or small area within range. No damage is dealt, and no serious harm is inflicted—just mild frustration.

Roll a d10 and consult the Chaos Table below to determine the exact annoyance:
Clarifications:- The inconvenience is purely cosmetic, causing no damage or severe disadvantage.- The DM can creatively adjust minor details based on the narrative scenario.
| d10 | Minor Annoyance (Chaos Table) |
|----- |----------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 1 | A sock disappears from the target’s foot, never to be found again. |
| 2 | A sudden, unbearable itch appears exactly where the target can't reach. |
| 3 | The target’s shoelaces immediately untie themselves repeatedly for 1 minute. |
| 4 | A random book or document the target is holding becomes incorrectly labeled, causing confusion. |
| 5 | The target’s keys or similar small celebrityl item vanish momentarily, reappearing only after thorough searching. |
| 6 | An annoying dripping sound emanates nearby but has no identifiable source. |
| 7 | The target’s clothes become slightly uncomfortable—too itchy, tight, or loose—for exactly one minute. |
| 8 | A persistent and unexplained humming noise surrounds the target, audible only to them. |
| 9 | Every surface the target touches for the next minute feels oddly sticky. |
| 10 | A harmless but persistent fly or insect buzzes around the target’s face, impossible to swat or catch. |

#### Crawling Dread
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You insinuate a faint but maddening illusion into the mind of a creature within range, provoking the persistent sensation of unseen movement across their skin.

The target must make an Intelligence saving throw.

• Failure: Until the start of its next turn, the creature is distracted by the sensation. The next time it takes an action requiring fine motor control or concentration, it must first make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, the action is wasted as the creature reflexively recoils, brushes at phantom irritants, or shifts in discomfort.
• Success: The creature is unaffected.

The effect ends immediately if the creature takes damage.

#### Dead Air
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You impose a fleeting hush of unnatural stillness upon living expression, as though speech itself has momentarily forgotten its vitality.

Until the start of your next turn, creatures within range experience subtle disruption of verbal continuity:

• Spoken phrases may emerge halting, toneless, or faintly delayed, as if briefly drained of animation.
• Creatures have disadvantage on Charisma (Deception and Persuasion) checks that rely on confident or fluid speech.
• Attempts to convey nuanced or emotionally charged meaning may feel curiously flattened or disjointed at the GM’s discretion.

This effect does not silence creatures or prevent communication. It introduces only a transient sense of conversational inertia, where words feel briefly bereft of their usual force.

#### Dice Storm
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You call upon the fractured laws of probability, summoning a swirling rain of polyhedral objects—tiny magical dice—within a 10- foot radius centered on you. The clattering projectiles slam into everything nearby.

Each creature of your choice in the area must make a Dexterity saving throw or take 2d6 bludgeoning damage. On a successful save, they take half damage. The damage is nonlethal unless otherwise specified.

Chaos Surge:

Immediately after casting, roll a d20. On a natural 20, the dice manifest as larger and denser projectiles (e.g., d20s the size of coconuts). Choose one of the following critical effects, or let the DM improvise:- The target is knocked prone.- One object in the area is crushed or broken.- A random magical effect is triggered (see Wild Magic surge table).- The area becomes difficult terrain until the end of your next turn (covered in slippery dice).- You regain 1 hit point (the dice land just right to boost your morale).

#### Directional Sense
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 10 minutess

You briefly attune your awareness to subtle spatial cues, allowing instinct and perception to align.

For the duration, you gain a faint sense of orientation toward a location or direction you specify when casting the spell. This sense does not reveal exact routes or hidden passages, but provides a persistent intuitive impression of general bearing.

While the spell persists:

• You have advantage on Wisdom (Survival) checks made to navigate, track direction, or avoid becoming lost.
• You have advantage on checks made to resist becoming disoriented or confused by natural environmental effects such as twisting corridors, dense terrain, or shifting landmarks.

This spell does not reveal concealed doors, bypass physical barriers, or penetrate magical effects that obscure space or perception. Illusions, magical mazes, and extradimensional distortions function normally.

#### Dirge Pulse
*Necromancy cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You emit a low, mournful resonance that brushes against fading consciousness.

Choose a point within range. Any creature within range that is at 0 hit points and making death saving throws gains a fleeting anchor to life.

• The next time such a creature succeeds on a death saving throw before the start of your next turn, it immediately becomes Stable.

This spell has no effect on creatures that are not making death saving throws.

If an undead creature is within range when the pulse is released, it takes 1 psychic damage.

#### Drifting Echo
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You attune your perception to faint temporal residues, sensing the dying impressions of recent activity.

For the duration, you perceive vague, distorted auditory impressions of events that occurred in the area within the last hour. These echoes are fragmented and imprecise, conveying only general emotional tones, rhythms of movement, or the presence of speech rather than intelligible content.

By using your action to concentrate on a specific location within range, make an Intelligence (Investigation) check. The clarity of the impressions depends on the result:

• Low Result: You discern only indistinct murmurs, tonal shifts, or emotional residue.
• Moderate Result: You perceive recognizable patterns such as the number of speakers, intensity of movement, or general activity.
• High Result: You extract fleeting but useful details, such as isolated words, sudden disturbances, or notable anomalies, at the GM’s discretion.

This spell does not reproduce exact conversations, reveal precise identities, or function in areas where sound was magically suppressed or reality significantly distorted.

#### Dripping Hour
*Transmutation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You induce a fleeting temporal slippage in a Small or smaller object you can see within range. A faint afterimage of the object lingers where it stood a moment before, creating perceptual uncertainty.

Until the start of your next turn, the object’s position appears subtly unstable.

A creature that attempts to directly manipulate or interact with the object must make an Intelligence saving throw.

• Failure: The creature hesitates or misjudges the object’s true position. The interaction fails and produces no effect.
• Success: The creature interacts with the object normally.

This effect does not move the object, alter its properties, or prevent creatures from perceiving it. The afterimage is purely perceptual and occupies no physical space.

#### Dust Veil
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You stir loose particles from the surrounding terrain, momentarily shrouding yourself in a shifting haze.

When a creature you can see makes an attack roll against you, you may use your reaction to impose disadvantage on that roll.

The veil disperses immediately after the attack is resolved.

This spell produces no effect in environments devoid of loose dust, ash, sand, or similar particulate matter, at the GM’s discretion.

#### Echoing Stomp
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self (10.0-foot radius)
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You strike the ground with a forceful stomp, sending a concussive tremor through nearby surfaces.

Each creature within a 10-foot radius of you must make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure: The creature takes 1d6 thunder damage and cannot take reactions until the start of its next turn.
• Success: The creature takes no damage and suffers no additional effect.

This spell produces no effect on surfaces incapable of transmitting vibration, such as deep water, loose sand, or similarly unstable terrain, at the GM’s discretion.

#### Eclipse Touch
*Abjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Touch
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You trace a fleeting sigil upon a creature you can touch, marking it with a dim, transient ward.

Until the start of your next turn, the first time the target would take fire damage, reduce that damage by 1d4 (minimum 0). The sigil then fades.

#### Erased Footsteps
*Transmutation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Touch
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You briefly distort how a surface records the passage of creatures.

Touch a non-magical surface occupying a 5-foot space. For the duration, the affected area cannot retain visible tracks, footprints, or similar traces of movement.

Creatures attempting to track movement through the area must succeed on a Wisdom (Survival) check against your spell save DC. On a failure, the surface provides no usable signs of passage.

This spell does not conceal creatures, alter sound, or mask other forms of evidence such as scent, displaced objects, or magical detection.

#### Expired Authority
*Enchantment cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You fracture a creature’s certainty at the instant it attempts to impose its will.

Choose one creature within range that you can see. If the target attempts, before the start of its next turn, to:

• Issue a command
• Enforce an instruction
• Compel behavior
• Exercise social or hierarchical authority

It must make a Charisma saving throw.

• Failure: The creature hesitates and the attempted action is delayed until the start of its next turn, wasting the original effort.
• Success: The action proceeds normally.

This spell has no effect on purely physical actions or attacks.

#### Fabricated Memory
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 5.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You momentarily disturb a creature’s short-term recall, introducing a harmless inconsistency in its immediate perception of events.

Choose one creature within range that you can see. The target must succeed on an Intelligence saving throw or briefly misremember a purely trivial detail that occurred within the last round.

Examples of trivial details include:

• Where it placed a small object
• Whether it spoke a minor phrase
• The exact position of an item in hand
• A negligible sensory impression

The false memory lasts only until the start of the target’s next turn, at which point the mind corrects itself. The effect cannot alter decisions, beliefs, loyalties, or awareness of danger.

A creature engaged in combat has advantage on the saving throw.

#### Fascination
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 12.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

A subdermal neurological impulse is implanted in the target’s cognitive prioritization center, making them incapable of focusing on anything but the caster.

The target must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save:

- The affected target follows the caster wherever they go, unable to take their eyes off them.
- If attacked, the target enters a berserk fury, attacking anyone who obstructs their pursuit of the caster (+1 to hit,- 1 AC).
- The target may repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success.

#### Flawed Step
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You slip momentarily out of alignment with your immediate position, reappearing a heartbeat away as space misjudges your presence.

You teleport up to 5 feet to an unoccupied space you can see.

This movement:

• Is instantaneous
• Requires no movement
• Does not provoke opportunity attacks

You must be able to stand in the destination space.

#### Flickering Veil
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You briefly destabilize your visual presence, causing your form to waver and shimmer like a heat-haze mirage.

Until the start of your next turn, the first attack roll made against you by a creature that relies on sight is made with disadvantage.

If you move before the spell ends, you leave behind a faint afterimage that lingers until the start of your next turn. The afterimage is purely visual and has no mechanical effect.

#### Ghost Slap
*Necromancy cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You conjure a fleeting spectral impact that strikes a creature with an invisible, percussive force.

Choose one creature within range. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become momentarily disoriented.

• On a failure, the creature has disadvantage on the next attack roll it makes before the end of its next turn.

• A creature affected by this spell is subtly destabilized. The next time it makes a saving throw against a Necromancy spell before the end of your next turn, it rolls the save with disadvantage.

• On a success, the creature resists the effect.

The force leaves no wound, only a sharp, humiliating jolt, like a reprimand delivered by unseen hands.

#### Glassheart
*Abjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 reaction
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

Your form splinters like struck glass at the instant of catastrophic impact.

Reaction, which you take when a creature scores a critical hit against you.

The triggering attack becomes a normal hit instead.

You take 1d4 psychic damage, representing the violent mental strain of sustaining the fracture. This damage cannot be reduced in any way.

Once you use this spell, you cannot do so again until the start of your next turn.

For a brief moment, your body appears threaded with faint, luminous cracks before snapping back into solidity.

#### Grasp of the Unseen
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You manifest a fleeting, invisible spectral hand that interferes with the physical world.

Choose a creature or unattended object within range.

• Creature: The target must succeed on a Strength saving throw or have its speed reduced by 10 feet until the start of its next turn.

• Object: You move the object up to 10 feet in a direction of your choice. The object must weigh no more than what you could lift with one hand.

The hand vanishes immediately after the effect.

#### Grounded Ward
*Abjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You draw your stance into harmony with the world’s unseen foundations, rooting yourself within the Weft of matter and force.

Until the start of your next turn, the first time you would take thunder or force damage, reduce that damage by 1d8.

While the ward holds, your body feels unnaturally steady, as though invisible roots anchor you against the shock of hostile energies.

This spell ends early if you are forcibly moved or lifted from the ground.

#### Gutterwake
*Transmutation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 15.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You stir the idle squalor of your surroundings, coaxing motion from filth, dust, and shallow refuse. Grime ripples, loose debris shifts, and stagnant water shivers in uneasy response.

Creatures in a 15-foot cone originating from you must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or become momentarily unsettled by the sudden movement. Affected creatures have disadvantage on the next opportunity attack they make before the end of their next turn.

This effect represents distraction rather than restraint and does not otherwise hinder movement or actions.

If you cast this spell in an area containing visible debris, dust, liquid, or grime, you may forgo the disorienting effect and instead shape the disturbed material into a fleeting image, symbol, or pattern. The image occupies a space within the cone and remains for 1 minute before collapsing back into disorder.

#### Hesitation Courtesy
*Abjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 reaction
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You lace a creature’s hostile intent with a moment of intrusive doubt, a fleeting disruption of certainty that arrives at the brink of action.

When a creature you can see within range makes an attack roll against you, you may use your reaction to impose hesitation. The creature must make a Wisdom saving throw.

On a failure, the creature subtracts 1d4 from the triggering attack roll.

This spell has no effect on creatures immune to being charmed.

Once a creature has been affected by this spell, it is immune to its effects until the start of your next turn.

#### Hollow Gaze
*Necromancy cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 15.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

Your eyes empty into unsettling stillness, reflecting a depth that living minds instinctively recoil from.

Choose one creature you can see within range. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or be momentarily disturbed by the void-touched gaze.

On a failure:

• The creature has disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks until the start of your next turn
• If the creature is concentrating on a spell, it has disadvantage on the next Constitution saving throw it makes to maintain Concentration before the start of your next turn

A creature that succeeds on the saving throw is unaffected.

Once a creature is affected by this spell, it is immune to its effects until the end of your next turn.

#### Hollow Stare
*Enchantment cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

Your gaze fixes upon a creature with disquieting emptiness, your features seeming subtly wrong, as though perception itself resists holding your image.

Choose one creature you can see within range. The target must make a Charisma saving throw.

On a failure, the creature’s sense of self falters:

• It has disadvantage on Intelligence checks until the end of its next turn
• The first time it speaks before the end of its next turn, its words emerge strained and uncertain

If the creature fails the saving throw by 5 or more, its next spoken sentence is subtly distorted to all listeners except you. The words are audible, but their meaning is misinterpreted or partially lost, as determined by the DM.

A creature immune to being charmed is unaffected.

Once a creature is affected by this spell, it is immune to its effects until the end of your next turn.

#### Impression of Near Portent
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 15.0 feet
**Components:** V
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You briefly attune your senses to the subtle tensions of unfolding possibility, allowing reality to express itself through fleeting symbolic impressions.

For the duration, you receive a momentary sensory omen associated with the next meaningful event that occurs within range. The omen manifests as a minor, intangible sensation chosen by the GM, such as:

• A sudden chill or warmth
• A faint flicker or shimmer
• A fleeting taste or scent
• A sensation of weight or lightness
• A distant or indistinct impression

The omen is symbolic in nature and conveys no explicit information about the event’s form, source, or outcome. Its meaning, if any, is interpretive and may be ambiguous or misleading.

Once the omen manifests, the spell ends.

#### Jagged Step
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 5.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You disturb the ground beneath your feet, wrenching loose a shard of splintered stone or wood that lashes outward in a sudden, violent burst.

Creatures of your choice within 5 feet of you must make a Dexterity saving throw.

On a failure, a creature takes 1d6 slashing damage.

Loose fragments briefly litter the ground in the affected area. Until the start of your next turn, the area is considered hazardous terrain for hostile creatures. The first time a creature willingly moves within the area during that time, it takes 1 slashing damage.

#### Lantern of the Forgotten
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self (30.0-foot radius)
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 10 minutess

You conjure a faint, spectral lantern that hovers near your shoulder for the duration. The lantern sheds dim light in a 30-foot radius, visible only to you and Hollow creatures.

The lantern moves with you and provides no illumination to other creatures.

When a Hollow creature enters the lantern’s light for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there, it must make a Wisdom saving throw.

• Failure: The creature cannot willingly move beyond the lantern’s light radius for 1 minute.
• Success: The creature is unaffected and becomes immune to this effect for 24 hours.

A restrained creature may repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success.

The lantern is intangible and cannot be interacted with or damaged.

#### Listening to the Living Ground
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 60.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 10 minutess

You attune your senses to subtle vibrations carried through the surrounding environment, reading motion through resonance rather than sight.

For the duration, you become aware of the movement of creatures within 30 feet that are in contact with the same surface or structure as you (ground, floor, wall, or similar medium).

While attuned:

• You sense whether creatures are moving or stationary
• You discern their direction of movement and relative speed (slow, normal, rapid)
• You do not learn exact location, identity, or number of creatures

This perception functions through solid materials and does not rely on vision, but it fails if:

• You are not touching a surface capable of transmitting vibration
• The creature is not in contact with a connected medium
• Significant interference (violent tremors, heavy machinery, thunderous effects) obscures the signals

This sense does not reveal creatures that are perfectly motionless.

#### Log
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 50.0 feet
**Components:** V
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You conjure a single, entirely ordinary wooden log in an unoccupied space on the ground within 50 feet. The log is nonmagical, mundane, and appropriately sized to serve as a seat, obstacle, or improvised tool.

The log may be handled or used as a standard object. If wielded as an improvised weapon, it deals 1d4 bludgeoning damage.

Though perfectly normal, the log carries a faint and inexplicable sense of significance. When the log appears, you may roll on the Log Essence Table (if your table uses one) to determine its wood type or subtle character. This has no inherent mechanical effect.

The log persists until destroyed or otherwise removed.
| d8 | Log Essence |
|---- |---------------------------------- |
| 1 | Oak – Solid, dependable, mildly judgmental. |
| 2 | Pine – Smells great but sheds needles constantly. |
| 3 | Birch – Pale, elegant, oddly smooth to the touch. |
| 4 | Mahogany – Impossibly classy. You feel underdressed. |
| 5 | Driftwood – Damp, salty, and whispers ancient secrets. |
| 6 | Petrified – Heavy, stone- like, cold and eternal. |
| 7 | Hollow – Echoes slightly when tapped. Creepy. |
| 8 | Fierywood – Warm to the touch. Never burns. |

#### Lurking Gloom
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You stir a brief knot of light-swallowing gloom that clings to a creature’s senses.

Choose one creature you can see within range. The target must make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure:
A numbing pall dulls the creature’s awareness. Until the end of its next turn, the creature suffers a –5 penalty to Wisdom (Perception) checks and to its passive Perception.

• Success:
The creature resists the effect with no penalty.

If the target is already standing in dim light or darkness, it makes the saving throw with disadvantage.

#### Mage Sand
*Conjuration cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V
**Duration:** Permanent

A small heap of fine, golden sand appears in your open hand. The sand is mundane, nonmagical, and behaves as ordinary sand in all respects, save for one peculiarity: it is perpetually damp.

The sand cannot be dried by mundane means, though this property has no inherent mechanical effect. Once conjured, the sand persists until it is scattered, discarded, or otherwise separated from your hand, at which point it becomes indistinguishable from normal wet sand.

Despite centuries of speculation, the sand appears to serve no practical or mystical purpose.

#### Mindsling
*Evocation cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 60.0 feet
**Components:** V
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You form a sharpened shard of mental force—an arrow of intent, a spike of memory, or a piercing thought—and hurl it toward a creature within range.

Make a ranged spell attack against the target. On a hit, the target takes 1d8 psychic damage.

The shard is invisible to those without psychic sensitivity, leaving no physical trace. To mundane observers, the effect may resemble the target momentarily flinching or losing focus.

Thematic Delivery

You choose the form your psyslings take. Examples include:
- A crystalline memory dart
- A shimmering synaptic spike
- A phrase spoken backward that drills through thought
- A fractal glyph burned across the air

The number of shards you manifest increases as you gain levels.
Each shard can target the same or different creatures. You make a separate attack roll for each.
### Psysling Cantrip Progression

| Character Level | Damage | Number of Shards |
|----------------- |-------- |------------------ |
| 1st | 1d8 | 1 |
| 5th | 1d8 | 2 |
| 11th | 1d8 | 3 |
| 17th | 1d8 | 4 |

#### Missing Ledger
*Divination cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You subtly displace an object’s presence in the perceptions of others, as though its existence had been poorly recorded.

Choose one unattended, nonmagical object within range no larger than a book. For the duration, the object is visually and cognitively deemphasized.

Creatures other than you who perceive the object must succeed on an Intelligence (Investigation) check against your spell save DC to consciously notice it. On a failure, the creature treats the object as overlooked, misplaced, or irrelevant to its attention, though the object remains physically present.

The effect ends immediately if the object is handled, moved, or directly interacted with, or if a creature is explicitly directed to examine the object.

This spell does not render the object invisible, suppress sound, or prevent accidental contact. It merely encourages the mind to disregard what is plainly there.

#### Misthreaded Record
*Illusion cantrip*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 rounds

You induce a momentary flaw in the Erelian Erudits’ registries, causing a document, card, or written record within range to appear subtly misaligned with its proper place in the Loom. Labels blur, markings seem inconsistent, and the record feels faintly out of order.

Any creature attempting to reference or rely upon the affected record must succeed on an Intelligence (Investigation) check against your spell save DC to notice the inconsistency. The disturbance is fragile. Once examined closely or deliberately scrutinized, the misthread resolves and the record settles back into its proper form.

You slam your foot down onto the ground, sending a controlled shockwave rippling through the asphalt, knocking foes back and disrupting their balance.- Saving Throw: Each creature within 5 feet of you must make a Strength saving throw.- On a failed save, the creature is pushed 5 feet away from you.- On a successful save, the creature remains unaffected by the shockwave.- Additionally, any creature that fails the saving throw takes 1d6 sound damage as the shockwave disturbs their equilibrium.
