*8th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 hours
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 24 hourss

You invite a spirit back into the world of the living, but only for a limited time.
 
- The summoned spirit returns in physical form for 24 hours.
- They remember everything from their death and are aware that this is temporary.
- At the end of the spell’s duration, the spirit knows who summoned them—and may not be happy about it.

#### Touch of the Nereid
*8th-level Transmutation*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Touch
**Components:** S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You touch the target's flesh, feeling their breath flutter like candlelight in the abyss.
 
- The target must make a Constitution saving throw (- 2 penalty). On a failure, they drown instantly, as if submerged in unseen waters.
- Those who survive describe a vision of something immense, watching from beneath the surface.
- Those who fail leave behind no corpse, only a damp outline where they once stood.

 Some whisper that victims of this spell are not truly dead, but merely waiting… elsewhere.

#### Abhaaldrac’s Unmaking Descent
*9th-level Evocation*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self (300.0-foot radius)
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 24 hourss

You call upon Abhaaldrac, the World Destroyer who drifts beyond the Far Cosmos, and invite a fragment of its attention to fall upon the world. The moment its presence presses against reality, the Loom begins to tear.

Across the affected region, existence destabilizes violently. Gravity bends toward impossible vectors, structures shear and realign, and the Veil fractures as alien geometries intrude. The land does not merely break, it is rewritten according to principles that do not belong to this world.

Anomalous entities and cosmic hazards manifest spontaneously, acting without pattern, allegiance, or mercy. Spellcraft within the area becomes dangerously unstable as Abhaaldrac’s influence distorts intent and outcome, causing magic to misfire, mutate, or recoil upon its caster.

At its highest invocation, Abhaaldrac does not withdraw. The descent completes, and the region becomes a permanent scar upon reality, a place where the Far Cosmos presses close and the world forever remembers that it was once seen by something vast enough to end it.
Point of origin and size: Choose a point you can see within 300 feet. The effect fills a 1-mile-radius region centered on that point. This is a regional phenomenon, not a combat template.
Duration: The region persists for 24 hours. If cast at 10th level, the region becomes permanent and functions as a quarantined anomaly site (DM discretion on containment and escalation).
Region traits: The region is considered planar-thin and geomagnetically unstable. The following effects apply throughout the region unless a specific hazard result says otherwise.
Spatial shear: Straight-line movement remains possible, but structures, corridors, and sightlines may no longer align. Doors can open into non-adjacent rooms. Climbing routes can lead somewhere else than expected.
Gravity lurches: At intermittent moments, gravity “pulls” toward a temporary vector. Creatures can be knocked prone, lifted, or slammed into nearby surfaces depending on the hazard roll.
Veil fractures: The region intermittently produces anomalous entities and hazards. They are not summoned allies. They act according to their own instincts or the hazard entry.
Hazard cadence: At the start of each hour, and whenever the DM wants to emphasize escalation (entering a landmark, casting a spell, loud battle, opening a sealed door), roll once on the Abhaaldrac Hazard Table. The result affects a sub-area chosen by the DM, typically a 300 to 1,000 foot zone, or follows the party if you want it to feel predatory.
Unstable spellcraft: Whenever a creature casts a spell of 1st level or higher inside the region, they must make a spellcasting ability check against DC 15 + the spell’s level.
- Success: The spell functions normally.
- Failure: Roll once on the Spellcraft Misfire Table. The spell slot is still expended.
- Rituals: A ritual cast within the region automatically triggers a misfire roll at completion unless the caster succeeds on the above check.
- Counterspell and Dispel Magic: These also require the check. On a failure, they misfire instead of resolving normally.
Safe pockets: The DM may place rare “still points” where hazard cadence is reduced (for example, hazard rolls only every 6 hours). These are valuable objectives and should feel earned.
Abhaaldrac Hazard Table (d12)
	1.	Gravity Lurch. Each creature in the affected sub-area makes a Strength saving throw (DC 18) or is knocked prone and slides 30 feet toward the current vector.
	2.	Structural Shear. The ground and walls “realign.” Difficult terrain for 10 minutes. Doors, corridors, and stairways in the sub-area no longer connect as mapped.
	3.	Vector Inversion. Ranged weapon attacks and spell attacks in the sub-area have disadvantage until the next hazard roll as trajectories bend unpredictably.
	4.	Veil Splinters. 1d4 anomalous entities manifest in the sub-area. Use any appropriate stat blocks, but they are hostile or indifferent, never friendly by default.
	5.	Chromatic Pressure. Creatures must make a Constitution save (DC 18) or take 4d8 psychic damage and have disadvantage on Wisdom checks for 1 hour.
	6.	Null Draft. Magical light is suppressed in the sub-area for 1 hour. Nonmagical flames sputter and dim.
	7.	Echo Weather. A localized storm of particulate debris, ash, or metallic dust. Heavily obscured beyond 30 feet for 10 minutes.
	8.	Inertial Snap. Each creature makes a Dexterity save (DC 18) or takes 6d6 bludgeoning damage as the environment “catches up” with their motion.
	9.	Bleached Silence. Sound is muffled. Creatures have disadvantage on Perception checks that rely on hearing for 1 hour.
	10.	Horizon Fold. The sub-area becomes subtly larger inside than outside. Travel time doubles for 1 hour.
	11.	Predatory Geometry. The sub-area produces a moving hazard that pursues the nearest creature for 10 minutes (treat as a hazard that forces Dex saves each round or each minute outside combat).
	12.	The Loom Tears. The next spell cast in the region automatically triggers a misfire roll, even if the check succeeds.

Spellcraft Misfire Table (d12)
	1.	Recoil. The caster takes 3d6 force damage per spell level.
	2.	Inversion. The spell’s damage type becomes psychic, or if it was psychic, it becomes force.
	3.	Offset Targeting. The spell originates from a point 30 feet in a random direction from the intended point.
	4.	Overreach. The spell affects one additional random valid target in range.
	5.	Underreach. The spell’s range is halved. If already touch, it fails harmlessly but still expends the slot.
	6.	Backwash. The caster is affected as if they were also a target, if the spell can legally target them.
	7.	Mutation. The spell gains a cosmetic anomaly, and a minor mechanical twist chosen by the DM (for example, difficult terrain, a loud shriek, or a lingering stench).
	8.	Dead Channel. The spell fizzles. No effect. Slot expended.
	9.	Double Cast. The spell resolves normally, then immediately repeats against the same targets with half effect.
	10.	Wild Exchange. Swap a key parameter, chosen by the DM: line becomes cone, sphere becomes cube, or range becomes self with area centered on caster if applicable.
	11.	Arcane Fracture. The caster cannot cast spells of that level or higher for 1 minute.
	12.	Call Attention. Roll immediately on the Hazard Table, then apply the hazard at the spell’s point of origin.

#### Cataclysm of Tainted Radiance
*9th-level Evocation*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 120.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You tear open a forbidden wellspring of corruptive radiance, flooding the area with searing, unnatural light that clings to flesh and stone alike. Each creature in the affected area must make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure: The creature takes 8d10 radiant damage and becomes Tainted for 1 minute.
• Success: The creature takes half damage and is not Tainted.

While Tainted, a creature is visibly marked by unstable radiance:

• The creature sheds dim light in a 10-foot radius.
• The creature cannot benefit from being Invisible.
• The creature has disadvantage on Stealth checks.
• At the end of each of its turns, the creature emits a surge of corruptive light. Any creature within 10 feet takes 1d4 radiant damage. This damage occurs once per turn per Tainted creature.

When a creature first becomes Tainted, roll d100. On a result of 01–10, the creature manifests a unique anomaly or corruption determined by the GM. This roll is made once per creature per casting.

The radiance produced by this spell is considered unnatural and persists only for the duration of the Tainted condition.

#### Create Spell
*9th-level Transmutation*
**Casting Time:** 1 minutes
**Range:** Self
**Components:** None
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You attempt the most perilous act of arcane mastery: the forging of a previously unknown spellform. Through intense concentration and esoteric procedure, you impose a new magical working upon the fabric of the world.

When you cast this spell, you design a new spell effect. The nature, magnitude, and limits of the created spell are determined by the GM, who is the final arbiter of its viability, scope, and consequences.

As guidance for adjudication:

• Cantrip / 1st–3rd Level Effects: Minor, narrow, or situational workings.
• 4th–6th Level Effects: Significant combat or utility magic, typically with constraints or risks.
• 7th–8th Level Effects: Exceptional workings involving control, transformation, or life-altering influence, always accompanied by serious drawbacks or instability.
• 9th-Level Effects: World-shaping magic comparable only to the most extreme known spells.

The created spell becomes part of your personal magical repertoire if deemed stable. Only one created spell may remain stable in this manner at any time.

Attempts to maintain multiple created spells may result in failure, collapse, or unforeseen magical consequences at the GM’s discretion.

⸻

Risks & Consequences

The act of forging a spell is inherently dangerous. The GM may impose consequences appropriate to the magnitude of the effect, including but not limited to:

• Exhaustion or physical debilitation
• Psychic or force backlash
• Memory erosion or cognitive distortion
• Permanent scars of magical strain
• Unintended side effects or flaws

Failure may produce partial, distorted, or hazardous outcomes.

#### Crown Decree of Stillness
*9th-level Abjuration*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 hours

You proclaim a sweeping decree that asserts royal authority over an entire district. All creatures within range must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failure, they are compelled to remain in place, believing compliance to be their lawful duty. Affected creatures cannot initiate hostilities unless attacked and automatically suppress panic and fear responses in favor of obedience.

Throughout the area, structures of order fall silent as conduits of control shut down or enter enforced dormancy, responding only to authority recognized by the Crown. When invoked at its greatest height, the decree persists until undone by equally potent magic, binding all who failed their save to the stillness of sanctioned order.

#### Exiled from the Self
*9th-level Divination*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 60.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Permanent

You pronounce a sentence of absolute dissociation, severing a creature from the continuity of its own existence.

Choose one creature within range. The target must make a Charisma saving throw.

• Failure: The creature’s personal identity collapses.

The creature loses all autobiographical memory, including its name, history, allegiances, beliefs, and sense of self. It retains languages, proficiencies, and functional knowledge, but experiences them as dislocated capabilities devoid of personal meaning.

The creature:

• Does not recognize allies, enemies, or prior relationships.
• Possesses no emotional or psychological attachment to its past.
• Treats its own abilities, possessions, and skills as unfamiliar phenomena.
• Cannot voluntarily act in accordance with prior loyalties or motivations.

This effect is permanent.

The identity may be restored only by:

• A Wish spell
• Direct reconstruction of the creature’s self through extensive external records, memories, or artifacts, at the GM’s discretion
• Effects capable of rewriting reality or the Loom itself

• Success: The creature is unaffected.

#### Great Severance of the Lattice
*9th-level Evocation*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Self
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 hours

You impose a vast field of severance that disrupts the sustaining frameworks of magical continuity.

Choose a point you can see within range. A sphere with a radius of up to 1 mile becomes subject to the severance for the duration.

Within the area:

• All magical light is extinguished, and nonmagical light sources produce only dim light

• Spells and magical effects that require ongoing concentration are suppressed

• Magical effects that create persistent emanations, auras, or sustained constructs are suppressed

• Teleportation and planar travel into or out of the area fail

Suppressed effects resume when the spell ends, provided their durations have not expired.

Artifacts and deific effects are unaffected at the GM’s discretion.

#### Heartbreaker
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Permanent

You utter a phrase meant for only one soul, a truth too immense or cruel for mortal cognition. The chosen creature within range hears the words perfectly, though no other being can perceive them.

The target must make a Constitution saving throw.

Failure:
The creature’s vital rhythms collapse under the unbearable revelation. It dies instantly as its heart violently seizes. This death cannot be reversed by any means short of Wish or similarly supreme magic.

Success:
The creature survives, but its body rebels against the psychic trauma. It becomes Paralyzed for the duration. While paralyzed in this way, the creature remains conscious, aware, and capable of perception but cannot move, take actions, or speak.

Duration (on a success): 1d6 + 6 weeks.

Regardless of the outcome, the strain leaves a permanent mark upon the creature’s physical form. Its Strength and Constitution scores are each reduced by 1. This reduction cannot be removed except by Wish or comparable magic.

The spoken phrase is not remembered, yet its emotional weight lingers like a wound without shape.

#### Judgment of the Loom
*9th-level Divination*
**Casting Time:** 1 minutes
**Range:** 60.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Permanent

You invoke a sovereign correction upon the tapestry of existence, demanding that the Loom reassess a creature’s legitimacy.

Choose one creature you can see within range. The target must make a Charisma saving throw.

Failure:
The creature’s thread is excised from causal continuity. The creature vanishes, and all non-magical memories, records, and mundane evidence of its existence are erased.

Reality does not rewind. Physical consequences, altered states, and completed events caused by the creature remain intact, though their origins become rationalized, obscured, or rendered uncertain at the DM’s discretion.

This erasure cannot be reversed except by Wish or comparably supreme magic.

Success:
The creature resists the judgment. Its thread holds, but the strain of the attempted excision leaves a visible metaphysical scar. The creature is Stunned until the end of its next turn.

⸻

The act of rendering judgment destabilizes the caster’s own thread. Upon casting this spell, you become Unstable for 7 days:

• You have disadvantage on saving throws against enchantment and divination spells
• Divination magic can more easily perceive you (attackers have advantage on checks made to locate or scry you)

⸻

Such violations of continuity rarely pass unnoticed. The casting of this spell may attract the attention of vast regulating intelligences, custodial forces, or Loom-bound arbiters, whose responses are determined by the DM.

#### Lamentbound Dram
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 90.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** 1 minutes

You flood a creature’s body with lament-saturated vitality, destabilizing the agreements that sustain its physical form.

Choose one creature you can see within range. The target must make a Constitution saving throw.

• Failure: The creature takes 8d10 poison damage and becomes Mutated for the duration.
• Success: The creature takes half damage and suffers no mutation.

While Mutated, the creature’s physiology warps unpredictably:

• The creature has disadvantage on Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution ability checks.
• At the start of each of its turns, the creature takes 1d10 poison damage as its body strains against itself.
• The creature’s speed is reduced by half.
• Visible distortions mark the creature’s form.

At the end of each of its turns, the creature may repeat the Constitution saving throw, ending the mutation on a success.

If a Mutated creature is reduced to 0 hit points, its body collapses into a corrupted husk. The corpse becomes a hazardous zone in a 10-foot radius for 1 minute. Creatures entering or starting their turn in the area take 2d6 poison damage.
While Mutated:
- At the start of each of the target’s turns, roll 1d6 to determine a mutation:
 | d6 | Mutation Effect |
 |---- |------------------ |
 | 1 | Their limbs distend uncontrollably. They have disadvantage on melee attacks. |
 | 2 | Eyeless growths bloom across their face. They are blinded until the start of their next turn. |
 | 3 | Tumorous bone spines burst outward. The creature takes 2d6 piercing damage. |
 | 4 | Their flesh becomes translucent and jelly- like. They gain vulnerability to bludgeoning damage. |
 | 5 | Parasitic nerves wriggle under their skin. They cannot take reactions. |
 | 6 | Their lungs restructure into gills. They begin suffocating unless submerged in liquid. |

#### Mirabel's Final Verse
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Touch
**Components:** S
**Duration:** Permanent

You seal a creature beneath a catastrophic affliction that denies the mercy of death itself.

You must touch one creature. The target must make a Charisma saving throw.

• Failure:
A permanent curse takes hold.

– The creature contracts a supernatural disease or madness chosen at casting.
– The creature cannot die while the curse persists. Damage, aging, suffocation, starvation, and similar effects cannot kill it.
– When reduced to 0 hit points, the creature becomes Paralyzed but remains conscious and aware.
– While at 0 hit points, the creature is stable, cannot act, and continues to perceive its surroundings.
– The creature does not regain hit points naturally. Only magical healing can restore it above 0 hit points.
– If healed, the creature immediately resumes normal function, though the curse remains.

• Success:
The spell has no effect.

⸻

The curse is extraordinarily difficult to remove.

It may be ended only by magic capable of undoing the most powerful afflictions, such as Wish, True Resurrection, or Greater Restoration cast using a spell slot of 9th level. The GM may permit other suitably exceptional narrative interventions.

#### Obliteration Memorandum
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 60.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You issue a sanctioned directive that targets the body itself—its fluids, its functions, its very architecture. The spell sends a binding sigil through the bloodstream of one creature within range, turning their own vital systems against them.

The target must make a Constitution saving throw.

- On a failure, their blood ignites with administrative intent, warping to fulfill the directive. They take 10d10 poison damage, and for the duration, they are affected by Internal Rebellion (see below).
- On a success, the target takes half damage and is not otherwise affected.

Internal Rebellion: 
For the duration of the spell, the creature suffers the following effects:
- Hemorrhagic Pulses: At the start of each of their turns, roll 1d6. On a 1–3, they take 3d6 poison damage as their blood attempts to exit through eyes, ears, and pores. 
- Command Override: The caster may use a bonus action on their turn to force the target to use half their movement in a direction of the caster’s choosing, as their own muscle tissue spasms against them. 
- Hostile System Rejection: If the target attempts to cast a spell or take a reaction, they must first succeed on a Constitution saving throw or the action fails and they take 2d6 psychic damage.

If this spell reduces a creature to 0 hit points, their body implodes into mist and splinters of bone, leaving behind no remains.

#### Recall from Morena's Grasp
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 10.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You invoke a sanctioned accord that authorizes a soul’s return from Morena’s domain. Choose one creature. If a binding covenant or recognized claim exists permitting the creature’s return, its thread is retrieved and rewoven, restoring it to life regardless of how long it has been dead.

If no such accord exists, the Loom refuses the request and the spell fails without effect. The magic does not bargain or plead. It simply checks whether return has been permitted, and acts accordingly.

#### Scouring of the Loom
*9th-level Evocation*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 120.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You unleash a catastrophic unraveling that tears through a creature’s thread in the Loom, stripping away memory, discipline, and learned form in a single annihilating surge. The target must make an Intelligence saving throw. On a failure, it takes 15d10 psychic damage as its mind is emptied, and it forgets all spells and abilities for 1 minute. On a success, it takes half damage and resists the deeper unraveling.

If a creature is reduced to 0 hit points by this spell, its thread is torn free entirely. Memories of its existence vanish from minds, archives, and Erudit registries alike. Only magic of the highest order or direct divine intervention can reweave what has been utterly scoured from the Loom.

#### Strike from the Loom
*9th-level Abjuration*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** 30.0 feet
**Components:** V, S
**Duration:** Instantaneous

You invoke an absolute decree of the Imperatum, striking directly at a creature’s place within existence. The target must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failure, it suffers 20d12 bludgeoning damage as the Loom recoils against its presence, and its name, likeness, and identity are erased from all records and memories of those who fail to recognize the severance.

On a successful save, the creature takes half damage and remains anchored within the Loom. The strike does not merely harm the body. It attempts to deny that the creature was ever meant to persist.

#### Vow of Erasure
*9th-level Necromancy*
**Casting Time:** 1 action
**Range:** Touch
**Components:** S
**Duration:** Permanent

You press your lips to the target’s skin—cheek, brow, hand, or lips. They do not cry out. They do not resist. There is no flash of light, no scream, no struggle.

There is only absence.- A creature with 150 hit points or fewer instantly dies.- After 1d10 rounds, their body crumbles into dust, leaving no corpse, no remains, and no residue.- They cannot be resurrected by any means—not by Wish, True Resurrection, or divine intervention. Their soul is simply gone, erased from all known realms.- Creatures immune to necrotic damage or undeath are not immune to this spell. It bypasses resistance and death saves.

# Diseases

#### Aetherbind Myelitis
Progressive numbness in extremities as aether channels stiffen and calcify
-2 Dexterity and disadvantage on Dexterity-based checks; somatic spellcasting requires DC 13 Constitution save
Philter of Aether Unbinding or Greater Restoration
Full paralysis in 3d6 days if untreated

#### Hideglass Blight
Translucent hardened skin plaques with intense itching and cracking
-1 Dexterity; disadvantage on Stealth and Deception involving touch; fire damage +1 per die
Unguent of Living Bark and druidic rite
Chronic condition with possible permanent mutation

#### Relict Bloom
Bioluminescent fungal nodules along spine accompanied by invasive dreams
Disadvantage on Wisdom saves; DM may impose disadvantage on one Intelligence check per long rest
Consecrated sunlight or Mycocidal Draught
Fungal takeover of crown-mind in 10 days

#### Grave-Eater Fever
High fever and necrotic lesions as body feeds on death energy
Gain 1 exhaustion daily; melee attacks deal +1 necrotic damage; healing halved
Blood-binding ritual or divine sacrifice
Fatal in 2d4 days if untreated

#### Bloodveil Sightrot
Ruptured ocular vessels causing redness blurred vision and afterimages
Disadvantage on ranged attacks and sight-based Perception; scroll use DC 12 Arcana
Oculary Balm of Still Waters ritualized
Blindness after 7 days

#### Ashlung Blight
Chronic cough expelling grey ash residue
Disadvantage on Constitution saves; sprinting causes 1d4 necrotic damage
Breath of Verdant Renewal potion
Lung calcification and death

#### Silverwake Tremor
Uncontrollable muscle shaking triggered by magic exposure
Disadvantage on attack rolls while concentrating; concentration saves at disadvantage
Arcane grounding ritual
Permanent tremors

#### Dreamleech Malaise
Recurring exhaustion-inducing nightmares
Long rests restore only half hit dice; disadvantage on Wisdom saves
Sanctified sleep charm
Madness onset

#### Gilded Blood Syndrome
Veins glow faintly gold and pulse painfully
Healing spells restore half value; advantage on saves vs charm
Alchemical blood distillation ritual
Organ failure

#### Blackroot Consumption
Dark veins spread from feet upward
Movement speed reduced by 10 feet; vulnerability to radiant damage
Root-purge decoction
Necrotic takeover

#### Echo Fever
Hearing whispers and delayed auditory perception
Disadvantage on Perception and Insight; initiative -2
Silence consecration rite
Permanent hallucinations

#### Frostmarrow Decay
Bone pain and cold radiating from joints
Strength -2; vulnerability to cold damage
Marrowfire elixir
Bone collapse

#### Sunscar Affliction
Blistering burns from sunlight exposure
Disadvantage on saves vs fire and radiant; sunlight causes 1d6 damage daily
Shadebinding salve
Photosensitivity for life

#### Verdigris Lung
Greenish breath and metallic cough
Disadvantage on Athletics and Constitution checks
Alchemical lung cleanse
Respiratory failure

#### Mindglass Fracture
Memory fragmentation and delayed responses
Disadvantage on Intelligence checks; spells require DC 10 concentration check
Mindbinding crystal ritual
Personality collapse

#### Carrion Bloom
Rash emitting necrotic spores
Nearby creatures make DC 11 Con save or poisoned
Sporefire fumigation
Contagion spread

#### Voidflux Sickness
Gravity distortion around body
Movement becomes difficult terrain; disadvantage on Dex saves
Planar anchoring sigil
Planar collapse

#### Bleakbone Rot
Bones become brittle and blackened
Critical hits against target occur on 19-20
Stonebone infusion ritual
Skeletal disintegration

#### Spellscar Degeneration
Old spell wounds reopen
Whenever casting a spell take 1d4 force damage
Spellseal grafting ritual
Loss of spellcasting

#### Gravechill
Body temperature drops unnaturally
Speed reduced by 5 feet; disadvantage on death saves
Life-heat infusion
Cardiac stasis

#### Crimson Lung Rot
Blood coughed violently
Constitution checks at disadvantage; dash causes exhaustion
Bloodletting rite
Hemorrhagic death

#### Phantom Limb Sorrow
Limbs feel detached and unresponsive
Disadvantage on Strength checks; initiative -1
Nerve-binding enchantment
Chronic dysfunction

#### Ossuary Fever
Hallucinations of bones and skeletons
Disadvantage on Wisdom saves; frightened condition near undead
Boneward blessing
Psychosis

#### Starfall Sickness
Skin glows faintly and flakes light
Disadvantage on Stealth; radiant damage taken +2
Star-salt immersion
Arcane burnout

#### Inkveil Corruption
Black veins spread from eyes
Disadvantage on Charisma checks; advantage on Intimidation
Void-cleansing ritual
Sensory loss

#### Thornblood Plague
Veins feel sharp and painful
Take 1 piercing damage per movement round
Blood-thinning draught
Cardiac rupture

#### Sable Rot
Shadow clings unnaturally
Disadvantage on saving throws in bright light
Shadow severance rite
Shadow assimilation

#### Candlewaste Disease
Wax-like residue on skin
Fire damage immunity but vulnerability to cold
Wax purge ceremony
Systemic collapse

#### Aetherflux Burn
Internal arcane scorching
Spellcasting causes 1d6 damage
Aether stabilization field
Spell organ failure

#### Chalklung
Skin dries and cracks white
Disadvantage on Constitution saves; vulnerability to thunder
Rehydration alchemy
Organ desiccation

#### Whispering Fever
Auditory hallucinations intensify under stress
Disadvantage on concentration saves
Consecrated silence ritual
Delirium

#### Bloodglass Syndrome
Crystallized blood under skin
Slashing damage resistance; piercing vulnerability
Blood-melting tonic

#### Planar Rash

Random minor wild magic surge daily

Spirit counseling rite

Strength -1; vulnerability to lightning damage

Dreamward sigil

Disadvantage on Constitution checks; fire resistance
Cinder extraction ritual

Salt-purge infusion

Poisoned condition when exerting

Ears bleed and hearing fades
Disadvantage on Perception relying on hearing
Soundward enchantment

Magic dampens around body
Magic resistance but spells cast at disadvantage

Bone marrow stiffens
Cannot regain hit dice on long rest
Marrow-release potion

#### Shattervein Disorder
Painful vascular spasms
Speed reduced by 10 feet; Dex saves disadvantage
Vascular rune therapy
Stroke

#### Crownrot Delirium
Persistent headaches and delusions
Disadvantage on Intelligence and Wisdom checks
Crown-cleansing rite
Loss of autonomy

#### Aegis Decay
Progressive pallor weakness and loss of heat tolerance as innate radiation resistance collapses
While in a radiated realm such as Dreadmere, the Ashenfold or the Realm of Torment, the creature loses 1 point of maximum HP per long rest. This loss cannot be healed or restored while exposure continues
Irreversible condition eventual death if prolonged exposure to radiated realms continues
